Swearing in Cases of Contradictory Acknowledgment: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on swearing in contradictory iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on administering oaths in cases of contradictory iqrar, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Contradictory statements in acknowledgment: Abu Hanifa bars oaths, Abu Yusuf allows them – fatwa follows Abu Yusuf with judicial discretion.

When a person makes contradictory statements in acknowledgment (iqrar) – first affirming, then denying – should the opposing party be required to take an oath? Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf held different views on this question, rooted in the reliability of the contradictory statements versus customary practice. The Hanafi school generally adopted Abu Yusuf's view, but also recognized the judge's discretion in light of the specific circumstances. This lesson unpacks the ikhtilaf and the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The disagreement is whether a person who has made contradictory statements in iqrar (e.g., first acknowledging then denying) should have his opponent sworn. Abu Hanifa says no; Abu Yusuf says yes.
The contradiction makes the acknowledger's statements unreliable, but custom supports administering an oath.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the opponent should not be sworn because the contradiction renders the acknowledger's statements unreliable. He analogizes to the case where someone says 'I have nothing from you' then claims property – such a person is not sworn.
The proof is based on the principle that contradictory statements cancel each other, leaving no basis for an oath.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf holds that the opponent should be sworn due to custom (al-ʿādah). Custom supports using oaths to resolve disputes when evidence is contradictory.
Custom is a recognized source of law in Hanafi fiqh, especially in muʿamalat.
4
Analyze the tarjih and its exceptions
The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's opinion, as chosen by the imams of Khwarazm. However, when the claimant is the heir of the acknowledger, there is a difference of opinion and no preference is given. Additionally, al-Sadr al-Shahid states that the decision to swear is ultimately up to the judge's discretion based on his assessment of the parties.
This shows that even within the preferred view, there is room for judicial ijtihad.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical effect is that under Abu Hanifa's view, the contradictory party avoids an oath, potentially leaving the dispute unresolved. Under Abu Yusuf's view, an oath is administered, which may lead to a resolution if the opponent swears or refuses.
The judge's discretion can also affect the outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيد برد المقر له لأن المقر لو رد إقرار نفسه كان أقر بقبض المبيع أو الثمن ثم قال لم أقبض وأراد تحليف الآخر أنه أقبضه أو قال هذا لفلان ثم قال هو لي وأراد تحليف فلان أو أقر بدين ثم قال كنت كاذباً لا يحلف المقر له في المسائل كلها عند أبي حنيفة لأنه متناقض كقوله ليس لي على فلان شيء ثم ادعى عليه مالاً وأراد تحليفه لم يحلف وعند أبي يوسف يحلف للعادة وسيأتي في مسائل شتى آخر الكتاب أن الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف اختاره أئمة خوارزم، لكن اختلفوا فيما إذا ادعاه وارث المقر على قولين، ولم يرجح في البزازية منهما شيئاً. ولا وقال الصدر الشهيد الرأي في التحليف إلى القاضي وفسره في فتح القدير بأنه يجتهد بخصوص الوقائع فإن غلب على ظنه أنه لم يقبض حين أقر يحلف له الخصم، ومن لم يغلب على ظنه فيه ذلك لا يحلفه، وهذا إنما هو في المتفرس في الأخصام ا هـ .
And it is conditioned by the rejection of the acknowledged because the acknowledger, if he rejects his own acknowledgment, he is like one who acknowledged receipt of the sold item or price, then said 'I did not receive' and wanted to have the other sworn that he delivered it; or said 'this belongs to so-and-so' then said 'it is mine' and wanted to have so-and-so sworn; or acknowledged a debt then said 'I was lying' – the acknowledged is not sworn in all these cases according to Abu Hanifa, because he is contradictory, just as if he says 'I have nothing from so-and-so' then claims wealth from him and wants him sworn, he is not sworn. According to Abu Yusuf, he is sworn due to custom. And it will come in various issues at the end of the book that the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's opinion, chosen by the imams of Khwarazm, but they differed when the heir of the acknowledger claims, with two opinions, and neither was preferred in al-Bazzaziyya. And al-Sadr al-Shahid said: The opinion in swearing is up to the judge, and he explained in Fath al-Qadir that the judge should exert effort based on the specifics of the cases: if he has a strong conviction that the acknowledger did not receive when he acknowledged, he swears the opponent; otherwise he does not swear him. And this is only for one who is discerning about opponents. End quote.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of contradictory statements in acknowledgment (iqrar). It presents the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf. According to Abu Hanifa, if a person makes contradictory statements (e.g., first acknowledging receipt, then denying it), the opposing party cannot be required to take an oath because the contradiction renders the statements unreliable – akin to someone who first says 'I have nothing from you' and then claims property. Abu Yusuf, however, allows swearing based on customary practice (al- adah). The passage notes that the fatwa is generally on Abu Yusuf's view, as chosen by the scholars of Khwarazm, except when the heir of the acknowledger is the claimant, where there is a difference and no preference is given. Additionally, al-Sadr al-Shahid provides a nuanced position: the decision to administer an oath is left to the judge's discretion based on the specific circumstances and his assessment of the parties' credibility. This exemplifies the Hanafi method of balancing textual rules with practical custom and judicial discretion.

Key Terms
التناقض (al-tanaquḍ): Contradiction in statements; here, the acknowledger's inconsistent claims (e.g., first affirming then denying).
التحليف (al-taḥlif): Administering an oath to a party in a dispute.
العادة (al-ʿādah): Custom; in this context, the common practice that supports the administration of an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon opinion (fatwa) on swearing in cases of contradictory acknowledgment?
A) Abu Hanifa's view that no oath is taken.
B) Abu Yusuf's view that an oath is taken due to custom.
C) The judge decides based on the specifics of the case.
D) The heir's claim is always preferred.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, contradictory statements in iqrar do not automatically bar oaths; the mufta bihi allows oaths based on custom, with judicial discretion.

Acceptance of News from a Sinner in Judicial Matters
Dispute over accepting testimony or news from a fasiq person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on accepting news from a fasiq and evaluate the opposing argument using the messenger analogy and witness strength comparison.

Core Idea
The Prophet sent messengers without requiring 'adala; the informant is like a messenger.

This passage presents a significant debate within Hanafi fiqh about the admissibility of news from a sinner (fasiq) in establishing legal rulings. While some later scholars rejected it, the main Hanafi position, championed by Imam Muhammad and al-Sarakhsi, upholds its acceptance based on the practice of the Prophet (SAW) and the practical strength of two fasiq witnesses over one 'adil. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyse how Hanafi usul principles interact with real-world evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: news from a fasiq is accepted and rulings become binding upon the recipient.
This is the mufta bihi position preferred by al-Sarakhsi.
2
Identify the opposing view
Find the opposing argument: scholars in Fath al-Qadir and al-Tahrir reject acceptance, requiring 'adala.
They argue that the non-requirement of 'adala only applies to specific messengers.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Examine the Hanafi dalil: the Prophet (SAW) sent messengers without stipulating 'adala, so a fasiq's news can be accepted analogously. Also, two fasiq witnesses have stronger effect than one 'adil in court.
The analogy with messengers is key.
4
Analyse the opposing proof
Understand the opponent's rebuttal: they restrict the rule to specific messengers, otherwise it would nullify the requirement of 'adala in hadith narration.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: if a fasiq reports a ruling, it is binding in Hanafi practice; if rejected, it is not binding.
This difference affects actual case outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد جعل المصنف من هذه المسائل المسلم الذي لم يهاجر وهو نص محمد في النوادر واختار السرخسي قبول خبر الفاسق تجب عليه الأحكام بخبره لأن المخبر له رسول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والعدالة لا تشترط في الرسول كما قدمناه ، وصححه الشارح ورده في فتح القدير والتحرير بأن عدم اشتراط العدالة إنما هو في الرسول الخاص بالإرسال وإلا فيلزم على قوله أن لا تشترط العدالة في رواية الحديث. وظاهر قوله أو مستورين أنه لا يقبل خبر الفاسقين وهو ضعيف والصحيح قبوله وثبوت هذه الأحكام لأن تأثير خبر الفاسقين أقوى من تأثير خبر العدل بدليل أنه لو قضى بشهادة واحد عدل لم ينفذ وبشهادة فاسقين ينفذ، وقوله إلا بعدل» أي بخبر عدل ولا يشترط فيه لفظ الشهادة؛ كذا في فتح القدير
And the author made among these issues the Muslim who did not migrate, and it is the text of Muhammad in al-Nawadir, and al-Sarakhsi chose accepting the news of the sinner, the rulings are obligatory upon his news because the informant is a messenger of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and uprightness is not stipulated in the messenger as we have presented, and the commentator corrected it and rejected it in Fath al-Qadir and al-Tahrir by saying that the non-stipulation of uprightness is only for the specific messenger, otherwise it would necessitate that uprightness is not required in hadith narration. And the apparent meaning of his saying 'or hidden ones' is that he does not accept the news of sinners, and it is weak, and the correct is its acceptance and the establishment of these rulings because the effect of the news of sinners is stronger than the effect of the news of the upright, evidenced by the fact that if he judges by the testimony of one upright person it is not executed, but by the testimony of two sinners it is executed. And his saying 'except with a just person' means by the news of a just person, and the wording of testimony is not required; as in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage addresses an inter-madhhab dispute about the acceptance of news (khabar) from a fasiq (sinner) for establishing judicial rulings. The Hanafi position, supported by Imam Muhammad in al-Nawadir and preferred by al-Sarakhsi, is that news from a fasiq can be accepted, making obligations binding based on it. The proof is that the Prophet (SAW) sent messengers without requiring them to be 'adl, as the recipient is acting as a messenger of the Prophet. The opposing view, held by some commentators in Fath al-Qadir and al-Tahrir, argues that the lack of requirement of uprightness applies only to specific messengers (rasul khas), not to general news reporting, otherwise it would nullify the need for uprightness in hadith narration. The Hanafi response rebuts by noting that even if the outward meaning of the text ('or hidden ones') seems to reject fasiq news, this reading is weak. The correct position is acceptance because the effect of two fasiq witnesses is stronger than one 'adil witness—a judge can execute a judgment based on two fasiq witnesses but not on one upright witness. Thus, the analogy (qiyas) supports acceptance. The phrase 'except with a just person' is interpreted as requiring a just person for testimony, but the exact wording of testimony is not required. This dispute shows the Hanafi preference for practical effectiveness over a strict requirement of 'adala in certain contexts.

Key Terms
خبر الفاسق (khabar al-fasiq): The report or testimony of a person who commits major sins (fasiq), used in establishing legal rulings.
عدالة (ʿadāla): The quality of being upright, just, and trustworthy; a condition for witnesses in many schools.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which evidence is used to support accepting news from a fasiq?
A) The practice of the Prophet sending messengers without requiring 'adala
B) The consensus of the sahaba
C) The principle that two fasiq witnesses outweigh one 'adil
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts news from a fasiq because the Prophet did not require uprightness in messengers, and two fasiq witnesses have stronger effect than one 'adil witness.

Required Wording for Testimony: 'Ashhadu'
Explaining the required wording for testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required wording for testimony in Hanafi fiqh and explain the linguistic and scriptural basis for using 'Ashhadu' over other words.

Core Idea
Testimony must be given with 'Ashhadu' because it indicates present observation, not past report.

The Hanafi school strictly requires the witness to use the present-tense verb 'Ashhadu' (I testify) when giving testimony. This lesson explores the linguistic reasoning, Quranic evidence, and the consensus (ijma') that underpin this ruling, distinguishing it from alternative wordings like 'Shahidtu' (I testified) or 'A'lamu' (I know).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on wording
Find the explicit statement that the word 'Ashhadu' is the required wording for testimony, and that 'Shahidtu' is not acceptable.
Look for the phrase 'ولا يجوز شهدت'
2
Examine linguistic reasoning
Understand why the present tense ('Ashhadu') is used for current testimony, while the past tense ('Shahidtu') refers to a past event and is therefore invalid for an in-court statement.
The passage compares 'qumtu' (I stood up) as past vs 'aqumu' (I stand) as present.
3
Analyze Quranic evidence
Study the two Quranic verses cited: 12:81 (past tense) and 63:1 (present tense) to see how the Quran distinguishes between past and present testimony.
Verse 12:81: 'وما شهدنا إلا بما علمنا'; Verse 63:1: 'قالوا نشهد إنك لرسول الله'
4
Note the consensus (ijma')
Recognize that the passage claims the ummah, from early generations onward, has consistently used 'Ashhadu' in testimony, treating it as a form of consensus.
The phrase 'جرى على ألسنة الأمة' indicates continuous practice.
5
Appreciate the devotional aspect
Understand that the exclusive use of 'Ashhadu' is not merely conventional but has a devotional (ta'abbudi) element, as no other wording is transmitted from the Prophet or companions.
The passage says 'لا يخلو عن معنى التعبد'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات

هي إخبار عن مشاهدة وعيان لا عن تخمين وحسبان وتلزم بطلب المدعي

كتاب الشهادات
أخرها عن القضاء لأنها كالوسيلة له وهو المقصود وهي سببه . الكلام فيها في مواضع : الأول في معناها لغة وشريعة واصطلاحاً فالأول كما في الصحاح خبر قاطع تقول منه شهد الرجل على كذا وربما قالوا شهد الرجل بسكون الهاء للتخفيف، وقولهم أشهد بكذا أي أحلف والمشاهدة المعاينة وشهده شهوداً أي حضره فهو شاهد وقوم شهود أي حضور وهو في الأصل مصدر وشهد أيضاً مثل راكع وركع ، وشهد له بكذا شهادة أي أدى ما عنده فهو شاهد والجمع شهد كصاحب وصحب وسافر وسفر، وبعضهم ينكره، وجمع الشهد شهود وأشهاد والشهيد الشاهد والجمع الشهداء ا هـ . وفي المصباح فائدة جرى على ألسنة الأمة سلفها وخلفها في أداء الشهادة أشهد مقتصرين عليه دون غيره من الألفاظ الدالة على تحقيق الشيء نحو أعلم وأتيقن وهو موافق لألفاظ الكتاب والسنة أيضاً فكان كالإجماع على تعيين هذه اللفظة دون غيرها، ولا يخلو عن معنى التعبد إذ لم ينقل غيره ولعل السر فيه أن الشهادة المشاهدة وهي الاطلاع على الشيء عياناً فاشترط في الأداء ما ينبئ عن واختصت بشيء يدل على ذلك وهو ما اشتق من اللفظ وهو أشهد بلفظ المضارع ولا يجوز شهدت لأن الماضي موضوع للإخبار عما وقع نحو قمت أي فيما مضى من الزمان، فلو قال شهدت احتمل الإخبار عن الماضي فيكون غير مخبر به في الحال وعليه قوله تعالى حكاية عن أولاد يعقوب عليهم الصلاة والسلام وما شهدنا إلا بما علمنا [يوسف: ٨١] لأنهم شهدوا عند أبيهم أولاً بسرقته حين قالوا إن ابنك سرق فلما اتهمهم اعتذروا عن أنفسهم بأنهم لا صنع لهم في ذلك فقالوا وما شهدنا عندك سابقاً بقولنا إن ابنك سرق إلا بما عايناه

اسم من
المشاهدة

كتاب الشهادات
آنفاً . قوله: (فما يرجع إلى الشاهد البلوغ والحرية الخ ترك السمع وقد ذكره فيما مر الشروح و به تصير ثمانية عشر .

أفاده
هو
من إخراج الصواع من رحله والمضارع موضوع للإخبار في الحال فإذا قال أشهد فقد أخبر في الحال وعليه قوله تعالى قالوا نشهد إنك لرسول الله ﴾ [المنافقون: ١] أي نحن الآن شاهدون بذلك. وأيضاً فقد استعمل أشهد في القسم نحو أشهد بالله لقد كان كذا» أي أقسم فتضمن لفظ أشهد معنى المشاهدة والقسم والإخبار في الحال فكأن الشاهد قال أقسم بالله لقد اطلعت على ذلك وأنا الآن أخبر به وهذه المعاني مفقودة في غيره من الألفاظ فلذا اقتصر احتياطاً واتباعاً للمأثور. وقولهم أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله تعدى بنفسه لأنه بمعنى أعلم وأما الثاني فما ذكره المؤلف بقوله . قوله : (هي إخبار عن مشاهدة وعيان لا عن تخمين وحسبان) أي الشهادة. وصرح الشارح بأن هذا معناها اللغوي وهو خلاف الظاهر وإنما هو معناها الشرعي أيضاً كما في إيضاح الإصلاح والمشاهدة المعاينة كما قدمناه والعيان بالكسر المعاينة كما في ضياء الحلوم فهو تأكيد والتخمين الحدس والحسبان بالكسر الظن. وأورد على هذا التعريف الشهادة بالتسامع فإنها لم تكن عن مشاهدة، وأجاب في الإيضاح بأن جوازها إنما للاستحسان والتعريفات الشرعية إنما تكون على وفق القياس ولكونها إخباراً عن معاينة قال في الخانية : إذا قرئ عليه صك ولم يفهم ما فيه لا يجوز له أن يشهد بما فيه؛ كذا في الحظر والإباحة. وفي الملتقط : إذا سمع صوت المرأة ولم ير شخصها فشهد اثنان عنده أنها فلانة لا يحل له أن يشهد عليها وإن رأى شخصها وأقرت عنده فشهد اثنان أنها فلانة حل له أن يشهد عليها ا هـ . وتمام مسألة الشهادة بما في الصك في شهادات البزازية. وأما معناها في الاصطلاح فقال في العناية : إخبار صادق في مجلس الحكم بلفظ الشهادة. فالإخبار كالجنس، وقوله «صادق» يخرج الأخبار الكاذبة وما بعده يخرج الأخبار الصادقة غير الشهادات اهـ. ويرد عليه قول القائل في مجلس القاضي أشهد برؤية كذا لبعض العرفيات فالأولى أن يزاد لإثبات حق كما في فتح القدير. ولم يقولوا بعد دعوى لتخلفها عنها في نحو عتق الأمة وطلاق الزوجة فلم تكن الدعوى شرطاً لصحتها مطلقاً، وقول بعضهم إنها إخبار بحق للغير على الغير بخلاف الإقرار فإنه إخبار بحق على نفسه للغير والدعوى فإنها إخبار بحق لنفسه على الغير غير صحيح لعدم شموله لما إذا أخبر بما يوجب الفرقة من قبلها قبل الدخول فإنه شهادة ولم يوجد فيها ذلك المعنى كما أشار إليه في إيضاح الإصلاح، وكأنه لاحظ أنه لم يخبر بحق للغير لأن ذلك موجب لسقوط المهر. وجوابه أن سقوطه عن الزوج عائد إلى أنه له فهو كالشهادة بالإبراء عن الدين فإنه إخبار بحق للمديون وهو السقوط عنه وكذا هنا وجعل الإخبار أربعة والرابع الإنكار وعزاه إلى شرح الطحاوي. وأما الثاني فركنها لفظ أشهد بمعنى الخبر دون القسم؛ كذا في الشرح ما لم يأت في آخرها بما يوجب الشك، فلو قال أشهد بكذا فيما أعلم لا تقبل كما لو قال
Book of Testimonies: It is an inform of observation and sight, not of estimation and assumption, and it becomes binding upon the request of the plaintiff. Book of Testimonies: He delayed it after judiciary because it is like a means to it, and the judiciary is the objective and it is its cause. The discussion about it is in topics: the first is its meaning linguistically, legally, and terminologically. As for the first, as in al-Sihah: a decisive statement, from which one says 'the man testified about such-and-such'; sometimes they say 'the man testified' with sukun on the ha for lightening. And their saying 'I testify by such' means 'I swear'. And 'observation' is 'seeing'. And 'he witnessed it' 'witnessing' meaning 'he attended it', so he is a witness, and a group are witnesses meaning attendees, and it is originally a verbal noun; and 'witnessed' also like 'kneeling' and 'he knelt'. And 'he testified for him' 'testimony' meaning 'he gave what he had', so he is a witness, and the plural is 'shuhud' like 'sahib' and 'suhb', 'safir' and 'safar'; some reject it; and the plural of 'shahid' is 'shuhud' and 'ashhad' and 'shahid' is the witness, and the plural is 'shuhada'. End quote. And in al-Misbah: a benefit: it has been upon the tongues of the ummah, its predecessors and successors, in performing testimony: 'Ashhadu', limiting themselves to it without other words indicating verification like 'I know' and 'I am certain'; and it is also in agreement with the words of the Book and Sunnah, so it was like consensus on specifying this word to the exclusion of others. And it is not free from the meaning of devotion since nothing else has been transmitted. Perhaps the secret is that testimony is observation, which is seeing something with one's own eyes, so it is required in performance what indicates that, and it is distinguished by something that indicates that, which is derived from the word, i.e. 'Ashhadu' in the present tense; and it is not permissible to say 'Shahidtu' because the past tense is placed for informing about what occurred, like 'I stood up' meaning in the past time. So if he said 'Shahidtu', it carries the possibility of informing about the past, so he would not be informing about it in the present. And upon that is His statement, the Exalted, narrating from the sons of Ya'qub, peace be upon them: 'And we testified not except according to what we knew' [Yusuf: 81] because they testified before their father initially about his theft when they said 'Your son stole'. When he accused them, they excused themselves saying they had no hand in that, so they said: 'And we did not testify before you previously by our saying that your son stole except by what we saw'... the present tense is placed for informing about the present moment, so when he says 'Ashhadu', he has informed at the present moment. And upon that is His statement, the Exalted: 'They said: We testify that you are indeed the Messenger of Allah' [al-Munafiqun: 1] meaning we are now witnessing that. Also, 'Ashhadu' has been used in oath, like 'I swear by Allah that such and such happened', meaning 'I swear', so the word 'Ashhadu' contains the meanings of observation, oath, and informing at the moment, as if the witness says: 'I swear by Allah that I have seen that and I am now informing of it.' These meanings are absent in other words, so it was limited to it out of caution and following what is transmitted. And their saying 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah' is transitive by itself because it is in the meaning of 'I know'. As for the second, it is what the author mentioned by his saying: 'It is an inform of observation and sight, not of estimation and assumption' i.e. testimony. And the commentator stated that this is its linguistic meaning, which is contrary to the apparent, rather it is its legal meaning also, as in Idah al-Islah. And 'observation' is 'seeing' as we have presented, and 'sight' (al-'iyan) with kasr means 'seeing' as in Diya' al-Hulum, so it is an emphasis. And 'estimation' is conjecture, and 'assumption' (al-husban) with kasr is 'opinion'. An objection was raised against this definition: testimony by hearsay, for it is not from observation. And he answered in al-Idah: its permissibility is only for istihsan, and legal definitions are only according to analogy. And because it is notification from seeing, it is stated in al-Khaniyya: If a document is read to him and he does not understand what is in it, it is not permissible for him to testify about its contents; likewise in al-Hazr wa al-Ibaha. And in al-Multaqat: If he hears a woman's voice and does not see her person, and two witnesses testify before him that she is so-and-so, it is not permissible for him to testify against her; but if he sees her person and she acknowledges in his presence, and two witnesses testify that she is so-and-so, it is permissible for him to testify against her. End. The complete issue of testifying to the contents of a document is in Shahadat al-Bazzaziyya. As for its technical meaning, it is stated in al-Inaya: a truthful inform in the court of judgment with the wording of testimony. 'Inform' is the genus; his saying 'truthful' excludes false informs; what comes after excludes truthful informs that are not testimonies. End. It is objected by someone saying in the court: 'I testify to seeing such-and-such' for some customary matters; so it is better to add 'for establishing a right' as in Fath al-Qadir. And they did not say 'after a claim' because it is absent in cases like manumission of a slave-woman and divorce of a wife; thus the claim is not a condition for its validity absolutely. And some say: it is an inform of a right for another against another, unlike confession which is an inform of a right against oneself for another, and the claim is an inform of a right for oneself against another. This is incorrect because it does not include when he informs of what necessitates separation from her before consummation, for that is testimony and that meaning is not found in it, as indicated in Idah al-Islah. It is as if he noted that he did not inform of a right for another because that necessitates the fall of the dower. The answer is that its fall from the husband returns as a right for him, so it is like testimony of discharge of debt, for it is an inform of a right for the debtor which is the discharge; and similarly here. And he made informs four, the fourth being denial, and he attributed it to Sharh al-Tahawi. As for the second, its pillar is the word 'Ashhadu' in the sense of inform, not oath; thus in the sharh, unless it comes at the end with what necessitates doubt. So if he says 'I testify to such as far as I know', it is not accepted, just as if he said...
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a definition and discussion of testimony (shahada) from the Hanafi perspective. The author opens the Book of Testimonies by stating that testimony is an announcement based on direct observation and sight, not on estimation or assumption. It becomes binding when requested by the plaintiff. The discussion is structured: first, the meaning linguistically, legally, and terminologically. Linguistically, testimony is a decisive statement; the verb 'shahida' is used, and the noun 'shahid' means witness. The plural forms are discussed. A key point is that the ummah, early and later, has consistently used the word 'Ashhadu' (I testify) when giving testimony, not words like 'A'lamu' (I know) or 'Ataqainu' (I am certain). This is considered a form of consensus (ijma') and has a devotional element. The reason is that testimony implies observation, so the wording should indicate present knowledge. 'Ashhadu' is the present tense, indicating current testimony, whereas 'Shahidtu' (I testified) would imply a past event and is therefore not acceptable. The author supports this with Quranic verses: the sons of Ya'qub used 'Shahidna' when referring to past testimony, but when stating present belief, the Quran uses 'Nashhadu' (we testify now). Also, 'Ashhadu' carries meanings of observation, oath, and present informing, which are absent in other words. The definition of testimony as 'inform from observation and sight' is both linguistic and legal, as per the sharh. Objections are raised: testimony by hearsay is not from direct observation. The answer is that such testimony is allowed by istihsan, not by qiyas; legal definitions are based on analogy. Therefore, if someone hears a woman's voice but does not see her, he cannot testify that she is so-and-so; but if he sees her and she acknowledges in his presence, he may testify. Similarly, if a document is read to him and he does not understand, he cannot testify about its contents. The technical definition in al-Inaya is: 'a truthful inform in the court of judgment with the wording of testimony.' This excludes false statements and truthful statements that are not testimonies. An objection that 'Ashhadu bi-ru'yati kadha' (I testify to seeing such) for customary matters is not about a right; thus a better definition adds 'for establishing a right' (li-ithbati haqq). The definition does not require a prior claim because testimony can occur in cases like manumission or divorce where no claim exists. Some defined testimony as an inform of a right for another against another, but this fails to include cases where the testimony causes separation (e.g., a wife testifying about a defect leading to divorce), which does not involve a right for another. The correct view is that testimony is a type of inform, and its pillar is the word 'Ashhadu' used as an inform, not as an oath. If the witness adds 'as far as I know' or expresses doubt, the testimony is not accepted.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahadah): An inform of observation and sight, not of estimation and assumption; legally, a truthful inform in court with the wording 'Ashhadu' to establish a right.
أشهد (ashhadu): The specific wording used for testimony in Hanafi fiqh; a present-tense verb indicating current knowledge and observation, also carrying an oath-like connotation.
مشاهدة (mushahadah): Direct observation or seeing with one's own eyes; the basis for valid testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is 'Shahidtu' not acceptable for testimony?
A) Because it is not an Arabic word.
B) Because it implies a past testimony, not a present one.
C) Because it is used only for oaths, not testimony.
D) Because it indicates uncertainty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the word 'Ashhadu' (I testify) is the only acceptable wording for testimony because it conveys present observation and is supported by Quranic usage and the continuous practice of the ummah.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Legal Definition of Shahada and the Exception of Hearsay
Defining shahada legally and addressing hearsay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal definition of shahada according to Hanafi scholars and explain the exception for hearsay testimony based on istihsan.

Core Idea
Shahada is a truthful inform in court with 'Ashhadu' to establish a right, but hearsay is allowed by istihsan despite lacking direct observation.

This lesson delves into the precise legal definition of testimony (shahada) as given by Hanafi jurists, addressing the requirement of direct observation. It also tackles a key objection: how can hearsay testimony (shahada bil-tasammu') be valid when it is not based on observation? The answer lies in istihsan (juristic preference), which permits hearsay in specific contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Find the technical definition from al-Inaya: 'truthful inform in the court of judgment with the wording of testimony' and note the refinements by other scholars (adding 'for establishing a right').
The definition excludes false statements and non-testimonial informs.
2
Understand the condition of observation
Recognize that the linguistic definition includes 'mushahadah' (observation) and that legal definitions are based on analogy (qiyas).
The passage states that definitions are 'على وفق القياس'.
3
Address the hearsay objection
Read the objection that testimony by hearsay (tasammu') is not based on observation, and the answer that its permissibility comes from istihsan, not qiyas.
The passage says 'جوازها إنما للاستحسان'.
4
Apply the ruling to examples
Examine the practical examples: testifying based on a document without understanding, or based on hearing a voice without seeing the person.
These illustrate when testimony is or is not valid.
5
Recognize the requirement of certainty in wording
Note that the testimony must be given without doubt; adding 'as far as I know' invalidates it.
The passage ends with the example of 'فيما أعلم'.

كتاب الشهادات

هي إخبار عن مشاهدة وعيان لا عن تخمين وحسبان وتلزم بطلب المدعي

كتاب الشهادات
أخرها عن القضاء لأنها كالوسيلة له وهو المقصود وهي سببه . الكلام فيها في مواضع : الأول في معناها لغة وشريعة واصطلاحاً فالأول كما في الصحاح خبر قاطع تقول منه شهد الرجل على كذا وربما قالوا شهد الرجل بسكون الهاء للتخفيف، وقولهم أشهد بكذا أي أحلف والمشاهدة المعاينة وشهده شهوداً أي حضره فهو شاهد وقوم شهود أي حضور وهو في الأصل مصدر وشهد أيضاً مثل راكع وركع ، وشهد له بكذا شهادة أي أدى ما عنده فهو شاهد والجمع شهد كصاحب وصحب وسافر وسفر، وبعضهم ينكره، وجمع الشهد شهود وأشهاد والشهيد الشاهد والجمع الشهداء ا هـ . وفي المصباح فائدة جرى على ألسنة الأمة سلفها وخلفها في أداء الشهادة أشهد مقتصرين عليه دون غيره من الألفاظ الدالة على تحقيق الشيء نحو أعلم وأتيقن وهو موافق لألفاظ الكتاب والسنة أيضاً فكان كالإجماع على تعيين هذه اللفظة دون غيرها، ولا يخلو عن معنى التعبد إذ لم ينقل غيره ولعل السر فيه أن الشهادة المشاهدة وهي الاطلاع على الشيء عياناً فاشترط في الأداء ما ينبئ عن واختصت بشيء يدل على ذلك وهو ما اشتق من اللفظ وهو أشهد بلفظ المضارع ولا يجوز شهدت لأن الماضي موضوع للإخبار عما وقع نحو قمت أي فيما مضى من الزمان، فلو قال شهدت احتمل الإخبار عن الماضي فيكون غير مخبر به في الحال وعليه قوله تعالى حكاية عن أولاد يعقوب عليهم الصلاة والسلام وما شهدنا إلا بما علمنا [يوسف: ٨١] لأنهم شهدوا عند أبيهم أولاً بسرقته حين قالوا إن ابنك سرق فلما اتهمهم اعتذروا عن أنفسهم بأنهم لا صنع لهم في ذلك فقالوا وما شهدنا عندك سابقاً بقولنا إن ابنك سرق إلا بما عايناه

Book of Testimonies: It is an inform of observation and sight, not of estimation and assumption, and it becomes binding upon the request of the plaintiff. Book of Testimonies: He delayed it after judiciary because it is like a means to it, and the judiciary is the objective and it is its cause. The discussion about it is in topics: the first is its meaning linguistically, legally, and terminologically. As for the first, as in al-Sihah: a decisive statement, from which one says 'the man testified about such-and-such'; sometimes they say 'the man testified' with sukun on the ha for lightening. And their saying 'I testify by such' means 'I swear'. And 'observation' is 'seeing'. And 'he witnessed it' 'witnessing' meaning 'he attended it', so he is a witness, and a group are witnesses meaning attendees, and it is originally a verbal noun; and 'witnessed' also like 'kneeling' and 'he knelt'. And 'he testified for him' 'testimony' meaning 'he gave what he had', so he is a witness, and the plural is 'shuhud' like 'sahib' and 'suhb', 'safir' and 'safar'; some reject it; and the plural of 'shahid' is 'shuhud' and 'ashhad' and 'shahid' is the witness, and the plural is 'shuhada'. End quote. And in al-Misbah: a benefit: it has been upon the tongues of the ummah, its predecessors and successors, in performing testimony: 'Ashhadu', limiting themselves to it without other words indicating verification like 'I know' and 'I am certain'; and it is also in agreement with the words of the Book and Sunnah, so it was like consensus on specifying this word to the exclusion of others. And it is not free from the meaning of devotion since nothing else has been transmitted. Perhaps the secret is that testimony is observation, which is seeing something with one's own eyes, so it is required in performance what indicates that, and it is distinguished by something that indicates that, which is derived from the word, i.e. 'Ashhadu' in the present tense; and it is not permissible to say 'Shahidtu' because the past tense is placed for informing about what occurred, like 'I stood up' meaning in the past time. So if he said 'Shahidtu', it carries the possibility of informing about the past, so he would not be informing about it in the present. Commentary
This passage is a definition and discussion of testimony (shahada) from the Hanafi perspective. The author opens the Book of Testimonies by stating that testimony is an announcement based on direct observation and sight, not on estimation or assumption. It becomes binding when requested by the plaintiff. The discussion is structured: first, the meaning linguistically, legally, and terminologically. Linguistically, testimony is a decisive statement; the verb 'shahida' is used, and the noun 'shahid' means witness. The plural forms are discussed. A key point is that the ummah, early and later, has consistently used the word 'Ashhadu' (I testify) when giving testimony, not words like 'A'lamu' (I know) or 'Ataqainu' (I am certain). This is considered a form of consensus (ijma') and has a devotional element. The reason is that testimony implies observation, so the wording should indicate present knowledge. 'Ashhadu' is the present tense, indicating current testimony, whereas 'Shahidtu' (I testified) would imply a past event and is therefore not acceptable. The author supports this with Quranic verses: the sons of Ya'qub used 'Shahidna' when referring to past testimony, but when stating present belief, the Quran uses 'Nashhadu' (we testify now). Also, 'Ashhadu' carries meanings of observation, oath, and present informing, which are absent in other words. The definition of testimony as 'inform from observation and sight' is both linguistic and legal, as per the sharh. Objections are raised: testimony by hearsay is not from direct observation. The answer is that such testimony is allowed by istihsan, not by qiyas; legal definitions are based on analogy. Therefore, if someone hears a woman's voice but does not see her, he cannot testify that she is so-and-so; but if he sees her and she acknowledges in his presence, he may testify. Similarly, if a document is read to him and he does not understand, he cannot testify about its contents. The technical definition in al-Inaya is: 'a truthful inform in the court of judgment with the wording of testimony.' This excludes false statements and truthful statements that are not testimonies. An objection that 'Ashhadu bi-ru'yati kadha' (I testify to seeing such) for customary matters is not about a right; thus a better definition adds 'for establishing a right' (li-ithbati haqq). The definition does not require a prior claim because testimony can occur in cases like manumission or divorce where no claim exists. Some defined testimony as an inform of a right for another against another, but this fails to include cases where the testimony causes separation (e.g., a wife testifying about a defect leading to divorce), which does not involve a right for another. The correct view is that testimony is a type of inform, and its pillar is the word 'Ashhadu' used as an inform, not as an oath. If the witness adds 'as far as I know' or expresses doubt, the testimony is not accepted.

Key Terms
شهادة بالتسامع (shahadah bi al-tasammu'): Testimony based on hearsay, i.e., information received from others rather than direct observation.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a ruling that is more appropriate or easier to apply, often based on custom, necessity, or implied consensus.
إثبات حق (ithbat haqq): Establishment of a legal right; the purpose of testimony in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is hearsay testimony allowed in certain cases according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the definition of testimony does not require observation.
B) Because it is permitted by istihsan despite the general requirement of observation.
C) Because hearsay is considered stronger than direct observation.
D) Because the Quran explicitly permits hearsay.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi legal definition of shahada requires direct observation, but hearsay is exceptionally allowed by istihsan in matters like lineage, marriage, and death.

Shahadat — Testimony

Definition and Linguistic Meaning of Shahada in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining shahada and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of shahada and identify its linguistic and technical elements, including the required wording and conditions.

Core Idea
Testimony requires direct observation and the word 'ashhadu'—hearsay is only accepted by istihsan.

Testimony (shahada) is a cornerstone of Islamic court procedure. This lesson unpacks its precise definition as formulated by Hanafi jurists, starting from the linguistic meaning of 'ashhadu' and building to the technical conditions for validity. You will see how the school navigates between strict requirement (direct observation) and practical necessity (hearsay exceptions via istihsan).

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning of 'ashhadu'
The passage shows that 'ashhadu' means 'I report' in the present tense, indicating immediate news. It is supported by Quran 63:1, where the hypocrites say 'nashhadu' (we witness) meaning 'we now testify'.
The present tense form is key: it conveys instantaneous testimony, not a past event or oath.
2
Extract the matn's definition of shahada
The author defines shahada as 'a report based on direct observation and sight, not on conjecture or assumption'. This is both linguistic and technical.
Note the pairing 'mushahada wa 'iyan' (direct observation and sight) for emphasis.
3
Analyse the objection regarding hearsay
An objection is raised: testimony by hearsay (al-tasammu') is accepted in some cases, yet it lacks direct observation. The Hanafi response is that such acceptance is by istihsan (juristic preference), not analogy, and definitions are based on general rules (qiyas), not exceptions.
This shows how Hanafi usul distinguishes between the general principle and the exceptional ruling.
4
Determine the technical definition from al-Inayah and its refinement
Al-Inayah defines shahada as 'a truthful report in the court of law with the word shahada'. Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir adds 'for establishing a right' to exclude matters of customary observation (e.g., 'I saw the moon').
This refinement ensures the definition covers only legally relevant testimony.
5
Recognize the rukn and invalidating phrases
The pillar (rukn) is the word 'ashhadu' used as a report, not an oath. Phrases like 'fima a'lam' (as far as I know) introduce doubt and invalidate the testimony, as they indicate uncertainty.
The passage gives multiple examples: testimony with 'fima a'lam' is rejected, while 'qad 'alimtu' (I have known) is accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات اه. أفاده هو من إخراج الصواع من رحله والمضارع موضوع للإخبار في الحال فإذا قال أشهد فقد أخبر في الحال وعليه قوله تعالى قالوا نشهد إنك لرسول الله ﴾ [المنافقون: ١] أي نحن الآن شاهدون بذلك. وأيضاً فقد استعمل أشهد في القسم نحو أشهد بالله لقد كان كذا» أي أقسم فتضمن لفظ أشهد معنى المشاهدة والقسم والإخبار في الحال فكأن الشاهد قال أقسم بالله لقد اطلعت على ذلك وأنا الآن أخبر به وهذه المعاني مفقودة في غيره من الألفاظ فلذا اقتصر احتياطاً واتباعاً للمأثور. وقولهم أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله تعدى بنفسه لأنه بمعنى أعلم وأما الثاني فما ذكره المؤلف بقوله . قوله : (هي إخبار عن مشاهدة وعيان لا عن تخمين وحسبان) أي الشهادة. وصرح الشارح بأن هذا معناها اللغوي وهو خلاف الظاهر وإنما هو معناها الشرعي أيضاً كما في إيضاح الإصلاح والمشاهدة المعاينة كما قدمناه والعيان بالكسر المعاينة كما في ضياء الحلوم فهو تأكيد والتخمين الحدس والحسبان بالكسر الظن. وأورد على هذا التعريف الشهادة بالتسامع فإنها لم تكن عن مشاهدة، وأجاب في الإيضاح بأن جوازها إنما للاستحسان والتعريفات الشرعية إنما تكون على وفق القياس ولكونها إخباراً عن معاينة قال في الخانية : إذا قرئ عليه صك ولم يفهم ما فيه لا يجوز له أن يشهد بما فيه؛ كذا في الحظر والإباحة. وفي الملتقط : إذا سمع صوت المرأة ولم ير شخصها فشهد اثنان عنده أنها فلانة لا يحل له أن يشهد عليها وإن رأى شخصها وأقرت عنده فشهد اثنان أنها فلانة حل له أن يشهد عليها ا هـ . وتمام مسألة الشهادة بما في الصك في شهادات البزازية. وأما معناها في الاصطلاح فقال في العناية : إخبار صادق في مجلس الحكم بلفظ الشهادة. فالإخبار كالجنس، وقوله «صادق» يخرج الأخبار الكاذبة وما بعده يخرج الأخبار الصادقة غير الشهادات اهـ. ويرد عليه قول القائل في مجلس القاضي أشهد برؤية كذا لبعض العرفيات فالأولى أن يزاد لإثبات حق كما في فتح القدير. ولم يقولوا بعد دعوى لتخلفها عنها في نحو عتق الأمة وطلاق الزوجة فلم تكن الدعوى شرطاً لصحتها مطلقاً، وقول بعضهم إنها إخبار بحق للغير على الغير بخلاف الإقرار فإنه إخبار بحق على نفسه للغير والدعوى فإنها إخبار بحق لنفسه على الغير غير صحيح لعدم شموله لما إذا أخبر بما يوجب الفرقة من قبلها قبل الدخول فإنه شهادة ولم يوجد فيها ذلك المعنى كما أشار إليه في إيضاح الإصلاح، وكأنه لاحظ أنه لم يخبر بحق للغير لأن ذلك موجب لسقوط المهر. وجوابه أن سقوطه عن الزوج عائد إلى أنه له فهو كالشهادة بالإبراء عن الدين فإنه إخبار بحق للمديون وهو السقوط عنه وكذا هنا وجعل الإخبار أربعة والرابع الإنكار وعزاه إلى شرح الطحاوي. وأما الثاني فركنها لفظ أشهد بمعنى الخبر دون القسم؛ كذا في الشرح ما لم يأت في آخرها بما يوجب الشك، فلو قال أشهد بكذا فيما أعلم لا تقبل كما لو قال [؟] درهم يصح في ظني بخلاف ما لو قال أشهد بكذا قد علمت، ولو قال لا حق لي قبل فلان فيما أعلم يصح الإبراء، ولو قال لفلان علي ألف فيما أعلم لا الإقرار كما ذكره الإمام الحصيري، ولو قال المعدل هو عدل فيما أعلم لا يكون تعديلاً؛ ذكره في باب أدب القضاء للخصاف . والحاصل أن قوله فيما أعلم بعد الإخبار موجب للشك فيه عرفاً فيبطل.
The book of testimonies... He said: it is a report of direct observation and sight, not of conjecture and assumption. And the commentator stated that this is its linguistic meaning, contrary to the apparent, and it is also its legal meaning. Objection is raised regarding testimony by hearsay, as it is not based on observation. The answer: its permissibility is by istihsan, and legal definitions are based on analogy. And its technical meaning in al-Inayah: a truthful report in the court of law with the word shahada. Then they discussed additions and pillars. The pillar is the word ashhadu meaning report, not oath. If he says 'ashhadu bi kadha fima a'lam', it is not accepted. The conclusion: saying 'fima a'lam' after testimony introduces doubt in custom, thus invalidates.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the definition of shahada (testimony) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins with the linguistic meaning of 'ashhadu', showing it indicates immediate present news, supported by Quran 63:1. The commentator presents the definition from the matn: 'a report based on direct observation and sight, not on conjecture or assumption.' He clarifies that this is both linguistic and legal. An objection is raised concerning testimony by hearsay (al-tasammu'), which is permitted by istihsan despite lacking direct observation. The technical definition from al-Inayah is then discussed: 'a truthful report in the court of law using the word shahada.' Critics note this includes even customary matters not involving rights, so the addition 'for establishing a right' from Fath al-Qadir is preferred. The pillar (rukn) of testimony is the word 'ashhadu' used as a report, not an oath. The passage then examines qualifying phrases like 'fima a'lam' (as far as I know), which introduce doubt and invalidate testimony, illustrated with examples from legal practice.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): A truthful report of direct observation in court using the word ashhadu.
أشهد (ashhadu): The verbal form used for testimony, meaning 'I witness' in the present tense.
مشاهدة (mushahada): Direct visual observation of the event.
عيان (iyan): Sight, direct observation; synonym of mushahada.
تخمين (takhmin): Conjecture, guesswork.
حسبان (husban): Assumption, opinion.
تسامع (tasammu'): Hearsay; testimony based on what one has heard from others.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of shahada requires direct observation and the word 'ashhadu', with hearsay accepted only by istihsan for specific cases.

Conditions of Bearing vs Performance of Testimony in Hanafi Fiqh
Detailing conditions for bearing and performing testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditions of bearing (tahammul) and conditions of performance (ada') of testimony, and apply the Hanafi rules regarding each.

Core Idea
Testimony has two stages—bearing and performing—each with its own conditions; what suffices for bearing may not suffice for giving testimony in court.

The Hanafi school meticulously separates the act of witnessing an event (tahammul) from the act of delivering the testimony in court (ada'). This lesson will guide you through the distinct conditions set by Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions, highlighting a key intra-madhhab disagreement on reliance on writing. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly evaluating a witness's capacity to testify.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of conditions
The text divides conditions of testimony into those for bearing (tahammul) and those for performance (ada'). This is the foundational analytical move.
The best classification is from al-Bada'i', as noted in the commentary.
2
Extract the three conditions of bearing
From the passage: sanity at the time of hearing, not being blind, and direct observation of the subject matter (except for specific hearsay cases).
These conditions ensure the witness actually perceived the event.
3
Note what is NOT required for bearing
Puberty, freedom, Islam, and uprightness are explicitly stated as not conditions for bearing. They are required for performance.
This is a key Hanafi principle that other schools may differ on.
4
Analyze the conditions of performance relating to the witness
Conditions include: puberty, freedom, sight, speech, uprightness (as condition for judge's acceptance, not validity), not being a relative/spouse, not being an opponent, and memory at the time of performance.
Adala is 'shart wujub al-qabul' not 'shart jawaz'.
5
Understand the intra-Hanafi disagreement on reliance on writing
Abu Hanifa requires memory at performance even if writing exists; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow reliance on writing if forgotten. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's stricter view.
This shows the school's internal ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثالث فشرطها العقل الكامل والضبط والولاية والقدرة على التمييز بين المدعي والمدعى عليه، وذلك بالسمع والبصر؛ هكذا في الشرح وفتح القدير والعناية ولكن زاد فيها الإسلام إن كان المدعى عليه مسلماً وفي كلامهم، قصور، لأن من الشرائط أن لا يكون بينه وبين المشهود له قرابة الولاد ولا زوجية وأن لا يدفع عن نفسه، مغرماً، وأن لا يجلب لنفسه مغنماً، وأن لا يكون بينه وبين المشهود عليه عداوة دنيوية كما سيأتي مفصلاً والظاهر أنهم إنما تركوا هذه لأن مرادهم بيان شرائط الشهادة في الجملة لا بالنظر إلى المشهود له والمشهود عليه ولذا ترى بعضهم ترك قيد الإسلام لجواز شهادة الكافر على مثله، والأحسن ما في البدائع من شرائطها نوعان: ما هو شرط تحملها وما هو شرط أدائها. فالأول ثلاثة: العقل وقت التحمل، وأن لا يكون أعمى، وأن يكون التحمل بمعاينة المشهود به بنفسه لا بغيره إلا في أشياء مخصوصة يصح التحمل فيها بالتسامع، ولا يشترط للتحمل البلوغ والحرية والإسلام والعدالة حتى لو كان وقت التحمل صبياً عاقلاً أو عبداً أو كافراً أو فاسقاً ثم بلغ الصبي وعتق العبد وأسلم الكافر وتاب الفاسق فشهدوا عند القاضي تقبل. وأما شرائط أدائها فأربعة أنواع: منها ما يرجع إلى الشاهد، ومنها ما يرجع إلى نفس الشهادة، ومنها ما يرجع إلى مكانها ومنها ما يرجع إلى المشهود به. فما يرجع إلى الشاهد البلوغ والحرية والبصر والنطق والعدالة لكن هي شرط وجوب القبول على القاضي لا جوازه، وأن لا يكون محدوداً في قذف، وأن لا يجر الشاهد إلى نفسه مغنماً ولا يدفع عن نفسه مغرماً، فلا تقبل شهادة الفرع لأصله، والأصل لفرعه وأحد الزوجين للآخر، وأن لا يكون خصماً فلا تقبل شهادة الوصي لليتيم والوكيل لموكله، وأن يكون عالماً بالمشهود به وقت الأداء ذاكراً له فلا يجوز اعتماده على خطه من غير تذكر عنده خلافاً لهما. وأما ما يخص بعضها فالإسلام إن كان المشهود عليه مسلماً، والذكورة في الشهادة بالحد والقصاص، وتقدم الدعوى فيما إذا كان من حقوق العباد وموافقتها للدعوى فيما يشترط فيها، فإن خالفتها لم تقبل إلا إذا وافق المدعي عند إمكانه وقيام الرائحة في الشهادة على شرب الخمر ولم يكن سكراناً لا لبعد مسافة والأصالة في الشهادة بالحدود والقصاص، وتعذر حضور الأصل في الشهادة على الشهادة وما يرجع إلى الشهادة لفظ الشهادة والعدد في الشهادة بما يطلع عليه الرجال واتفاق الشاهدين وما يرجع إلى مكانها واحد وهو مجلس القضاء وما يرجع
As for the third, its conditions are complete intellect, precision, legal capacity, and ability to distinguish between plaintiff and defendant, that by hearing and sight... The best is what is in al-Bada'i': its conditions are two types: what is a condition of bearing and what is a condition of performance. The first are three: intellect at the time of bearing, not being blind, and bearing by direct observation of the subject matter not by others except in specific matters where bearing by hearsay is valid. Puberty, freedom, Islam, and uprightness are not conditions for bearing... As for conditions of performance, they are four types...
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the conditions (shurut) of testimony according to the Hanafi school. It first mentions general conditions for performance: complete intellect, precision, legal capacity, and the ability to distinguish between plaintiff and defendant, which requires hearing and sight. Some authors add Islam if the defendant is Muslim, but the commentator notes this is not universal. The best classification is from al-Bada'i', dividing conditions into those of bearing (tahammul) and performance (ada'). Conditions of bearing are three: sanity at the time of hearing (even if later insane or blind), not being blind (so that one can see the subject), and direct observation of the subject matter, except in specific cases where hearsay is accepted (e.g., lineage, death). Notably, puberty, freedom, Islam, and uprightness are not required for bearing; they are required for performance. Conditions of performance are of four types: relating to the witness (puberty, freedom, sight, speech, uprightness as a condition for the judge's acceptance, not for validity; not being la'een in qadhf; not deriving benefit or repelling harm; not being a descendant or ascendant; not being a spouse; not being an opponent like a guardian for an orphan; being knowledgeable and remembering at the time of performance, so relying on one's writing without memory is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the Sahibayn). Specific conditions include Islam if the defendant is Muslim, masculinity for testimony on hadd and qisas, prior claim in civil rights, and the testimony must match the claim. The place is the court, and the number and wording of testimony are also specified.

Key Terms
تحمل الشهادة (tahammul al-shahada): The act of witnessing or receiving the testimony event; bearing the testimony.
أداء الشهادة (ada' al-shahada): The act of delivering testimony in court.
العدالة (al-adala): Uprightness; being free from major sins and not persisting in minor sins.
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision; the ability to accurately recall and report the testimony.
الولاية (al-wilaya): Legal capacity; the ability to act legally, such as being of sound mind and age.
الخصم (al-khasm): An opponent; a person who is party to the case, such as a guardian or attorney.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for bearing testimony (tahammul)?
A) Sanity at the time of hearing.
B) Direct observation of the subject matter (except in specific cases).
C) Puberty and freedom.
D) Not being blind.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school separates conditions of bearing from conditions of performance, allowing witnesses who were immature or non-Muslim at the time of the event to testify later, provided they meet performance conditions at the time of giving testimony.

The Ten Aspects of Testimony (Shahada) in Hanafi Law
Introductory enumeration of key aspects of shahada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the ten key aspects of testimony and state the total conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Hanafi law counts 24 conditions for testimony across bearing, performance, content, and place, but initially states 21.

This lesson introduces the structure of the Book of Testimony from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author lists ten fundamental aspects that frame the entire chapter, from conditions and obligation to proofs and virtues. Mastering this overview prepares you for the detailed rules that follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of conditions
The text states there are 21 conditions total: three for bearing (tahammul), seventeen for performance (ada') — divided into ten general and seven specific — three for the testimony itself, and one for the place. Note that the sub-totals actually sum to 24, which later correction resolves.
The discrepancy is a known textual issue; scholars maintain 24 conditions.
2
Distinguish bearing and performance
Bearing (tahammul) is witnessing an event to later testify. Performance (ada') is delivering testimony in court. Both have separate conditions.
3
Understand the cause of obligation and ruling
Testimony becomes wajib (obligatory) when the right-holder requests it or when the witness fears the right will be lost. The judge must then judge based on that testimony.
4
Grasp the justification for accepting testimony
Analogy would reject testimony due to the possibility of lying, but the stipulation of justice (adalat) and explicit texts (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma) override this, making testimony acceptable and obligatory.
This principle is a key usul point.
5
Recognize the proofs and virtues
The proofs are the Quran (e.g., 4:135), Sunnah, and Ijma. Virtue includes obeying Allah's command to be witnesses for justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات إلى المشهود به قد علم من الشرائط الخاصة. فالحاصل أن شرائطها أحد وعشرون : شرائط التحمل ثلاثة وشرائط الأداء سبعة عشر منها عشر شرائط عامة ومنها سبعة شرائط خاصة، وشرائط نفس الشهادة ثلاثة وشرط مكانها .واحد وسيأتي صفة الشاهد الذي ينصبه القاضي شاهداً للناس والرابع سبب وجوبها طلب ذي الحق أو خوف فوت حقه فإن من عنده شهادة لا يعلم بها صاحب الحق وخاف فوت الحق يجب عليه أن يشهد بلا طلب . الخامس حكمها وجوب الحكم على القاضي السادس في صفتها تحملاً وأداء وسيأتي. السابع في بيان أن القياس عدم قبولها لاحتمال الكذب لكن لما شرطت العدالة ترجح جانب الصدق ووردت النصوص بالاستشهاد جعلت موجبة . الثامن محاسنها كثيرة منها امتثال الأمر في قوله تعالى كونوا قوامين الله شهداء بالقسط ﴾ [النساء : ١٣٥] وهو حسن . التاسع في دليلها وهو الكتاب والسنة والإجماع العاشر في أهلها وقد علم من الشرائط .
Book of Testimonies. Up to what is testified to, it is known from the specific conditions. The summary is that its conditions are twenty-one: conditions of bearing testimony are three, and conditions of performance are seventeen, among them ten general conditions and seven specific conditions, and conditions of the testimony itself are three, and the condition of its place is one. And the description of the witness whom the judge appoints as a witness for people will come. Fourth: the cause of its obligation is the request of the right-holder or fear of losing his right, for whoever has a testimony that the right-holder does not know about and fears that the right will be lost, he must testify without request. Fifth: its ruling is the obligation of judgment upon the judge. Sixth: concerning its description as bearing and performance, and it will come. Seventh: concerning the explanation that analogy would reject it due to the possibility of lying, but when justice is stipulated, the side of truthfulness prevails, and the texts came with the command to take witnesses, so it was made obligatory. Eighth: its virtues are many, such as fulfilling the command in His statement: 'Be upholders of justice, witnesses for Allah' (al-Nisa 4:135), and that is good. Ninth: concerning its proof, which is the Book, Sunnah, and consensus. Tenth: concerning its people, which has been known from the conditions.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Shahadat with an overview of ten key aspects of testimony (shahada). The author first notes that the conditions of testimony total twenty-one: three for bearing (tahammul), seventeen for performance (ada') with ten general and seven specific, three for the testimony itself, and one for the place. Then he lists aspects four through ten: the cause of obligation (request or fear of loss), the ruling (judge must judge), description (to come), the principle that analogy would reject testimony but textual obligation overrides, virtues (citing Quran 4:135), proofs (Quran, Sunnah, ijma'), and the qualified people. This is a memorization anchor for the book's structure.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony; informing about a right in court.
تحمل (taḥammul): Bearing testimony; witnessing an event to later testify.
أداء (adā'): Performing testimony; delivering it in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the cause that makes testimony wajib even without a request?
A) The witness is a relative of the right-holder
B) The witness fears the right will be lost
C) The witness is appointed by the judge
D) The testimony concerns a small amount

Key Takeaway
Testimony in Hanafi law is governed by 24 conditions (initially enumerated as 21) and is wajib when a right may be lost, based on Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma.

Corrected Conditions for Testimony: 24 Not 21
Correction of earlier summary to 24 conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the corrected total number of conditions for testimony in the Hanafi school and break them down into their categories (bearing, performance, witness, statement, place).

Core Idea
Testimony has 24 conditions: 3 for bearing, 21 for performance—17 on the witness, 3 on the statement, 1 on the place.

In the Hanafi school, the conditions for valid testimony are numerous and carefully classified. The matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq summarized them as 21, but the commentator Ibn Nujaym corrects this to 24 for consistency with earlier expositions. This lesson unpacks that correction, clarifying the categories and highlighting an additional nuance about the witness's duty to inform the plaintiff.

Guided Path
1
Identify the error in the matn
Read the commentator's statement: 'This summary is not consistent with what has passed.' Recognize that the matn claimed 21 conditions, but the earlier detailed discussion in the text actually supports 24.
The commentator is correcting a numerical inconsistency, not introducing new law.
2
State the corrected total and its subdivisions
Memorize the four-part breakdown: conditions of bearing testimony (3), conditions of performance (21) which include conditions of the witness (17: 10 general, 7 specific), conditions of the testimony itself (3), and the condition of its place (1).
Total = 3 + 21 = 24. The 21 are further split into 17 + 3 + 1 = 21.
3
Understand the relevance of the plaintiff's knowledge
The commentator adds that a witness must inform the plaintiff of his testimony only if the plaintiff is unaware. If the plaintiff already knows or does not request it, the obligation to testify does not arise immediately.
This nuance affects when testimony becomes obligatory (fard kifaya vs. fard 'ayn).
4
Connect to practice
Apply this classification to a real case: a potential witness must satisfy all 24 conditions. Failure in any one (e.g., a missing general condition like 'adalah) invalidates the testimony.
The qadi must check each category in order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فالحاصل أن شرائطها أحد وعشرون الخ) هذا الحاصل غير موافق لما مر بل الموافق له أن يقال : فالحاصل أن شرائطها أربعة وعشرون : شرائط التحمل ثلاثة، وشرائط الأداء أحد وعشرون، منها شرائط الشاهد سبعة عشر عشرة عامة وسبعة خاصة، ومنها شرائط نفس الشهادة ثلاثة، وشرط مكانها واحد قوله : (وإنما قلنا أو حكماً ليدخل الخ) قال بعض الفضلاء: ونظر فيه المقدسي بأن الواجب في هذا إعلام المدعي بما يشهد فإن طلب وجب عليه أن يشهد وإلا لا إذ يحتمل أنه ترك حقه .
His statement: 'So the summary is that its conditions are twenty-one, etc.' This summary is not consistent with what has passed, but rather what is consistent with it is to say: So the summary is that its conditions are twenty-four: conditions of bearing testimony are three, and conditions of performance are twenty-one; among them conditions of the witness are seventeen: ten general and seven specific; and among them conditions of the testimony itself are three, and the condition of its place is one. His statement: 'And we only said 'or by way of judgment' to include, etc.' Some virtuous persons said: al-Maqdisi examined it, saying that what is obligatory here is to inform the plaintiff of what he witnesses; if he requests, it becomes obligatory to testify, otherwise no, because he might have waived his right.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement where the commentator (Ibn Nujaym) corrects the earlier matn's summary. The matn stated the conditions are 21, but the commentator says this is inconsistent with what was previously mentioned. The correct total is 24: 3 for bearing, 21 for performance (including 17 for the witness, 3 for the testimony itself, and 1 for the place). Then he addresses a point about 'or by way of judgment' and quotes al-Maqdisi's view that if the plaintiff is unaware, the witness must inform him; only then does obligation arise.

Key Terms
شرائط (sharā'iṭ): Conditions; prerequisites for validity of testimony.
تحمل (taḥammul): Bearing testimony; the act of witnessing an event and committing it to memory.
أداء (adā'): Performance of testimony; the act of delivering testimony in court.

Key Takeaway
Testimony in Hanafi law requires 24 conditions: 3 for bearing, 21 for performance—17 on the witness, 3 on the statement, and 1 on the place.
