Obligation to Testify: Proof and Conditions
Ruling on when testimony becomes obligatory and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which testimony becomes obligatory in Hanafi fiqh and apply them to concrete scenarios.

Core Idea
Testimony is a communal duty that becomes personally binding only when specific conditions are met.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains when a witness is obligated to testify and the severe prohibition of concealment. It begins with the Quranic proof (2:283) and clarifies the nature of the duty — fard kifayah that can become fard 'ayn. The author then lays down four conditions that trigger the obligation, with nuanced cases illustrating each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
Find the central ruling: testimony becomes obligatory upon the plaintiff's request, and concealment is forbidden. Note the proof from Quran 2:283 and how the prohibition implies a command to disclose.
The verse 'la taktumu al-shahada' is interpreted as a prohibition of concealment.
2
Distinguish fard kifayah from fard 'ayn
Understand that testimony is generally fard kifayah (communal duty) but becomes fard 'ayn (individual duty) when there are only two witnesses or upon specific request.
This distinction is critical for determining when a witness is sinful for staying silent.
3
List the four conditions for obligation
Extract the four conditions: 1) plaintiff's request (including constructive request), 2) knowledge that the judge will accept the testimony, 3) specificity (ta'ayyun) — no other qualified witness has fulfilled the duty, and 4) absence of two just witnesses informing that the testified matter is invalid.
Each condition has exceptions and details given in the text.
4
Apply the conditions to given cases
Work through the examples: delay without excuse, testifying after six months, death of party, etc. Determine whether the testimony is accepted and whether the witness is sinful.
Focus on how the conditions are met or violated.
5
Note the ikhtilaf on the verse's interpretation
Some exegetes (e.g., al-Qadi) hold that the verse addresses debtors, not witnesses. The author prefers the view that it addresses witnesses, relying on consensus for the obligation.
This shows the importance of multiple proofs and the role of ijma'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتلزم بطلب المدعي أي ويلزم أداؤها الشاهد إذا طلبه المدعي فيحرم كتمانها لقوله تعالى ولا تكتموا الشهادة ومن يكتمها فإنه آثم قلبه ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٨٣] فهو نهي عن الكتمان فيكون أمراً بضده حيث كان له ضد واحد وهو أكد من الأمر بأدائها ولذا أسند الإثم إلى رأس الأعضاء وهو الآلة التي وقع بها أداؤها لما عرف أن إسناد الفعل إلى محله أقوى من الإسناد إلى كله فقوله أبصرته بعيني آكد من قوله أبصرته وفسر الإمام الرازي في أحكام القرآن الكتمان بعقد القلب على ترك الأداء باللسان، وفسر البغوي آثم بفاجر وإن الله يمسخ قلبه بالكتمان وفيه أنه ليس في القرآن وعيد أشد منه . واستدل في الهداية بهذه الآية على فرضيتها مع احتمال أن إيراد نهي المدينين عن كتمانها كما احتمل أن يراد نهي الشهود. قال القاضي : ولا تكتموا الشهادة أيها الشهود أو المدينون والشهادة شهادتهم على أنفسهم ا هـ . فعلى الثاني المراد النهي عن كتمان الإقرار بالدين فالأولى الاستدلال على فرضيتها بالإجماع. واحتمل أن الضمير في قول المؤلف تلزم عائد إلى الشهادة بمعنى تحملها لا بمعنى أدائها فإن تحملها عند الطلب والتعيين فرض كما سيأتي . وعلى هذا فما في فتح القدير من أنه إن أريد بها تحملها فالنهي لكراهة التنزيه التي مرجعها خلاف الأولى مشكل. وذكر الإمام الرازي في أحكام القرآن أن قوله تعالى ولا يأب الشهداء إذا ما دعوا [البقرة: ٢٨٢] عام في التحمل والأداء لكن في التحمل على المتعاقدين الحضور إليهما للإشهاد ولا يلزم الشاهدين الحضور إليهما، وفي الأداء يلزمهما الحضور إلى القاضي لا أن القاضي يأتي إليهما ليؤديا ثم قال : إن الشهادة فرض كفاية إذا قام بها البعض سقط عن الباقين، وتتعين إذا لم يكن إلا شاهدان سواء كانت للتحمل أو الأداء ا هـ. فعلى هذا يقال إنها تلزم أي تفترض كفاية. ثم صرح بأن عليهما الكتابة إذا لم يوجد غيرهما إذا كان الحق مؤجلاً وإلا فلا. ثم إنما يلزم أداؤها بشروط : الأوّل طلب المدعي فيما كان من حقوق العباد حقيقة أو حكماً، وإنما قلنا أو حكماً ليدخل من عنده شهادة لا يعلم بها صاحب الحق وخاف فوت الحق فإنه يجب عليه أن يشهد بلا طلب كما في فتح القدير لكونه طالباً لأدائه حكماً. وإنما قيدنا بحقوق العباد لما في القنية أجاب المشايخ في شهود شهدوا بالحرمة المغلظة بعد ما أخروا شهادتهم خمسة أيام من غير عذر أنها لا تقبل إن كانوا عالمين بأنهما يعيشان عيش الأزواج. ثم نقل عن العلاء الحمامي والخطيب الأنماطي وكمال الأئمة البياعي شهدوا بعد ستة أشهر بإقرار الزوج بالطلقات الثلاث لا تقبل إذا كانوا عالمين بعيشم عيش الأزواج، وكثير من المشايخ أجابوا كذلك في جنس هذا وإن كان تأخيرهم بعذر تقبل. مات عن امرأة وورثة فشهد الشهود أنه كان أقر بحرمتها حال صحته ولم يشهدوا بذلك حال حياته لا تقبل إذا كانت هذه المرأة مع هذا الرجل وسكتوا لأنهم فسقوا إلى آخر ما فيها. الثاني أن يعلم أن القاضي يقبل شهادته فإن علم أنه لا يقبلها لا يلزمه الثالث أن يتعين عليه الأداء فإن لم يتعين بأن كانوا جماعة فأدى غيره ممن تقبل شهادته فقبلت لم يأثم بخلاف ما إذا أدى غيره ولم تقبل فإن من لم يؤد ممن يقبل يأثم بامتناعه وهذا إذا لم تكن شهادته أسرع قبولاً من غيره، فإن كانت أسرع وجب الأداء وإن كان هناك من تقبل شهادته كما في فتح القدير. الرابع أن لا يخبر عدلان ببطلان المشهود به فلو شهد عند الشاهد عدلان أن المدعي قبض دينه أو أن الزوج طلقها ثلاثاً أو أن المشتري أعتق العبد أو أن الولي عفا عن القاتل أن يشهد بالدين والنكاح والبيع والقتل كما في الخلاصة، وإن لم يكن المخبر عدولاً فالخيار للشهود إن شاؤوا شهدوا بالدين وأخبروا القاضي بخبر القضاء وإن شاؤوا امتنعوا عن الشهادة؛ كذا في البزازية. وإن كان المخبر واحداً عدلاً لا يسعه ترك الشهادة به وكذا لو قالا عاينا إرضاعهما من امرأة واحدة وكذا لو عاينا واحداً يتصرف في شيء تصرف الملاك وشهد عدلان عنده أن هذا الشيء لفلان آخر لا يشهدان أنه للمتصرف بخلاف إخبار لا يسعه قوله: (فإن كانت أسرع وجب الأداء الخ) فيه تأمل مقدسي. وكأنه لعدم ظهور وجه لوجوب حيث كان هناك من يقوم به الحق؛ حموي كذا نقله بعض الفضلاء ولكنه بحثه في مقابلة .
His statement: 'And it becomes obligatory upon the request of the plaintiff' i.e., its performance becomes obligatory upon the witness if the plaintiff requests it, so concealing it is forbidden, due to His statement: 'And do not conceal the testimony, and whoever conceals it, his heart is sinful' (al-Baqarah 2:283). So it is a prohibition of concealment, thus a command for its opposite since it has only one opposite, and it is stronger than the command to perform it. Therefore, sin is attributed to the head of the limbs, which is the instrument by which its performance occurs, because it is known that attributing the action to its place is stronger than attributing it to the whole. So his saying 'I saw him with my eye' is stronger than his saying 'I saw him.' Imam al-Razi in Ahkam al-Quran interpreted concealment (kutman) as the heart's resolve to leave performance by the tongue. Al-Baghawi interpreted 'sinful' as 'immoral' and that Allah will transform his heart due to concealment, and there is no threat in the Quran stronger than this. In al-Hidayah, it is used as proof for its obligatory nature, although it is possible that the prohibition is directed to debtors about concealing it, as it is possible that it is intended for witnesses. Al-Qadi said: 'Do not conceal the testimony, O witnesses or debtors, and the testimony is their testimony against themselves.' So on the second interpretation, what is meant is the prohibition of concealing the acknowledgment of debt, so it is better to rely on consensus for its obligatory nature. It is possible that the pronoun in the author's statement 'talzamu' refers to testimony in the sense of bearing (tahammul) not performance (ada'), for bearing upon request and designation is a duty as will come. On this, what is in Fath al-Qadir that if by it (talzamu) bearing is intended, then the prohibition is for dislikedness (karaha tanzih) which is contrary to the first, is problematic. Imam al-Razi mentioned in Ahkam al-Quran that His statement: 'And let not the witnesses refuse when they are called' (al-Baqarah 2:282) is general for bearing and performance, but in bearing it means for the contracting parties to come to them for witnessing, and it does not obligate the witnesses to go to them; in performance it obligates them to go to the judge, not that the judge comes to them to perform. Then he said: Testimony is a communal duty (fard kifaya); if some perform it, it is lifted from the rest, and it becomes specific (ta'ayyun) if there are only two witnesses, whether for bearing or performance. So according to this, it is said that it becomes obligatory, i.e., as a communal duty. Then he stated that writing is incumbent upon them if no one else exists, if the right is deferred, otherwise not. Then its performance is only obligatory under conditions: First: request of the plaintiff in what pertains to the rights of people, actually or by way of judgment. We only said 'or by way of judgment' to include the one who has a testimony unknown to the right-holder and fears loss of the right, for he must testify without request, as in Fath al-Qadir, because he is considered a requester for its performance by way of judgment. We only restricted it to the rights of people because in al-Qunyah, the mashayikh answered concerning witnesses who testified to severe prohibition (hurma mughallaza) after delaying their testimony for five days without excuse that it is not accepted if they knew that both were living as spouses. Then he narrated from al-‘Ala’ al-Hammami, al-Khatib al-Anmati, and Kamal al-A’imma al-Bayya‘i that they testified after six months to the husband’s acknowledgment of triple divorce; it is not accepted if they knew that they were living as spouses. Many mashayikh answered similarly in such cases, but if their delay was due to an excuse, it is accepted. A man died leaving a wife and heirs, and witnesses testified that he had acknowledged her prohibition during his health but did not testify during his life; it is not accepted if this woman was with this man and they remained silent, because they became sinners (fasiqun) etc. Second: that he knows that the judge will accept his testimony; if he knows that he will not accept it, it is not obligatory. Third: that the performance is specific to him; if it is not specific, e.g., they are a group and someone else whose testimony is accepted performed it and was accepted, he is not sinful, unlike if someone else performed and it was not accepted, then the one who did not perform from those whose testimony is accepted is sinful for refusing—this is if his testimony is not quicker to be accepted; if it is quicker, performance becomes obligatory even if there is someone else whose testimony is accepted, as in Fath al-Qadir. Fourth: that two just witnesses do not inform him that the testified matter is invalid. For if two just witnesses testify before a witness that the plaintiff has received his debt, or that the husband divorced her three times, or that the buyer emancipated the slave, or that the guardian pardoned the killer, then he should not testify concerning the debt, marriage, sale, or killing, as in al-Khulasa. If the informants are not just, the witnesses have a choice: if they wish, they may testify concerning the debt and inform the judge of the news of the judgment, and if they wish, they may refrain from testifying—as in al-Bazzaziyyah. If the informant is one just person, he cannot avoid testifying accordingly. Similarly, if two say 'we witnessed his breastfeeding from one woman,' and similarly if they saw one person disposing of something as owners do, and two just witnesses inform him that this thing belongs to someone else, he should not testify that it belongs to the disposer—unlike the informing of one who cannot. His statement: 'If it is quicker, performance becomes obligatory, etc.' al-Maqdisi reflects on this. It seems because the ground for obligation is unclear when there is someone who can fulfill the right; al-Hamawi—as some virtuous persons quoted—but he discussed it in opposition.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about when testimony becomes obligatory. The author begins by explaining that testimony is binding upon the plaintiff's request, and concealment is forbidden based on Quran 2:283 ('wa la taktumu al-shahada'). The prohibition of concealment is a command for its opposite (disclosure), and it is stronger than a direct command to perform because sin is attributed to the heart, the seat of intention. The author cites Imam al-Razi and al-Baghawi on the severity. He notes that al-Hidayah used this verse as proof for obligatory nature, but there is an alternative interpretation that it addresses debtors. So consensus (ijma') is better proof. Then he considers a possible ambiguity: the pronoun in 'talzamu' might refer to bearing (tahammul) rather than performance, but this is problematic as per Fath al-Qadir. Imam al-Razi distinguishes between bearing and performance using verse 2:282. Testimony is a fard kifaya (communal duty) but becomes fard 'ayn if there are only two witnesses. The conditions for obligation are four: 1) plaintiff's request in claims of people (including constructive request when the right-holder is unaware and the witness fears loss), 2) knowledge that the judge will accept, 3) ta'ayyun (specific duty) — if another qualified witness testifies and is accepted, the others are not sinful unless their testimony would be quicker, and 4) no two just witnesses inform that the matter is invalid. Various cases illustrate: delay without excuse, testifying after six months, etc. The passage ends with al-Maqdisi's reflection on the quicker testimony condition.

Key Terms
كتمان (kutmān): Concealment of testimony; the resolve not to perform it.
فرض كفاية (farḍ kifāyah): Communal duty; if some perform, obligation falls from others.
تعين (ta'ayyun): Specific duty; when only two witnesses exist, it becomes fard 'ayn on them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The witness must be a male

Key Takeaway
Testimony is a communal duty that becomes individually obligatory only under specific conditions, with prohibition of concealment based on Quran 2:283.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
6 min
The Communal Obligation of Bearing Witness and Its Individualization
States the ruling on shahada as fard kifayah and when it becomes 'ayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bearing witness as fard kifayah, identify when it becomes 'ayn (individual obligation), and distinguish the duties in tahammul vs. ada.

Core Idea
Witnessing is a communal duty, but becomes individually binding when only two are available.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the obligation of bearing witness. The author uses the Quranic verse (2:282) to establish that shahada is generally a communal obligation (fard kifayah), but it becomes a personal obligation (fard 'ayn) if there are only two witnesses available. The text also distinguishes between two stages: tahammul (undertaking to witness) and ada (performing testimony in court), each with its own procedural requirements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its base ruling
Pinpoint the act being ruled upon: bearing witness (shahada). The base ruling is fard kifayah—a communal obligation that falls from all if some perform it.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence: the Quranic verse 2:282. Note that it is general (amm) and covers both tahammul and ada. The imperative 'let them not refuse' indicates obligation.
The dalil is Quran, with qati al-thubut but zanni al-dalala as per Hanafi usul.
3
Distinguish tahammul and ada
Observe the difference: for tahammul (undertaking), the contracting parties must come to the witnesses. For ada (performance), the witnesses must go to the judge. This affects how the obligation is fulfilled.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh and shapes practical procedure.
4
Apply the condition for ta'ayyun
Understand when the communal obligation becomes individual: when there are exactly two witnesses. This applies equally to tahammul and ada.
The condition is numerical; no other factors are mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في أحكام القرآن أن قوله تعالى ولا يأب الشهداء إذا ما دعوا [البقرة: ٢٨٢] عام في التحمل والأداء لكن في التحمل على المتعاقدين الحضور إليهما للإشهاد ولا يلزم الشاهدين الحضور إليهما، وفي الأداء يلزمهما الحضور إلى القاضي لا أن القاضي يأتي إليهما ليؤديا ثم قال : إن الشهادة فرض كفاية إذا قام بها البعض سقط عن الباقين، وتتعين إذا لم يكن إلا شاهدان سواء كانت للتحمل أو الأداء ا هـ. فعلى هذا يقال إنها تلزم أي تفترض كفاية. ثم صرح بأن عليهما الكتابة إذا لم يوجد غيرهما إذا كان الحق مؤجلاً وإلا فلا.
In Ahkam al-Quran: His statement, the Exalted, 'And let not the witnesses refuse when they are called' [2:282] is general for undertaking and performance. But for undertaking, the contracting parties must come to them for witnessing, and the witnesses are not required to go to them. For performance, the witnesses must go to the judge, not that the judge comes to them to perform it. Then he said: Indeed, bearing witness is a communal obligation; if some perform it, it falls from the rest, and it becomes determined if there are only two witnesses, whether for undertaking or performance. So on this basis, it is said that it is binding, i.e., it is a communal obligation. Then he explicitly stated that they must write if there is no one else, if the right is deferred; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author, commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explains the obligation of bearing witness by quoting the Quranic verse (2:282) which commands witnesses not to refuse when called. The verse is general, covering both tahammul (the initial undertaking to be a witness, i.e., hearing or seeing the event) and ada (the later performance of testimony in court). However, the obligation differs: for tahammul, the contracting parties must come to the witnesses; for ada, the witnesses must go to the judge. The author then states the ruling: shahada is fard kifayah (communal obligation) – if some fulfill it, the obligation is discharged for all; but it becomes 'ayn (individual obligation) if there are only two witnesses, regardless of whether it is for tahammul or ada. Additionally, if the right is deferred (like a debt with a term), the witnesses must write it down if no one else is present; otherwise, writing is not required.

Key Terms
التحمل (al-tahammul): The act of undertaking to bear witness, i.e., being present and witnessing the event or transaction.
الأداء (al-ada): The act of performing testimony in court, i.e., stating what one witnessed.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation: if some members of the community perform it, the obligation is lifted from the rest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when does bearing witness become an individual obligation (ta'ayyun)?
A) When the witness is called by the judge
B) When there are only two witnesses for the case
C) When the right is deferred
D) When the witness fears the loss of the right

Key Takeaway
Bearing witness is generally a communal obligation (fard kifayah), but becomes individually binding (fard 'ayn) when exactly two witnesses exist.

Rulings on Hearsay Testimony and Testifying Before a Just Judge
Rulings on hearsay testimony and the requirement that the judge be just.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a witness may testify based on hearsay and explain when a witness may refrain from testifying before an unjust judge.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is restricted when contradicted by just witnesses; a witness may withhold testimony from an unjust judge.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two important points for witnesses. First, it addresses the delicate situation when two just witnesses testify contrary to what you personally believe—can you still testify? Second, it discusses the character of the judge before whom you are called to testify, and whether an unjust judge obligates you to testify. These rulings safeguard the integrity of testimony and protect the witness from being part of an unjust proceeding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main issues
The passage covers hearsay testimony (shahada bi al-tasamu') and the condition that the judge must be just (adl) for the witness to be obliged to perform. Note the two separate rulings.
2
Analyze the hearsay scenarios
Distinguish between the case of two just witnesses and one just witness. When two just witnesses testify contrary to your prior hearsay knowledge, you may not testify unless you know they are liars. When it's a single just witness, you may testify based on your hearsay unless you believe the single witness.
The exception applies to every testimony.
3
Determine the judge's justice
The fifth condition: the judge must be just. If the judge is unjust, the witness may refrain from testifying. However, if the witness strongly believes the unjust judge will accept his testimony (due to fame, etc.), then testifying becomes obligatory.
Also, a modifier is not obliged to modify a witness if informed he is unjust.
4
Note the authorities cited
The rulings are based on sources like al-Bazzaziyyah, al-Sirajiyyah, and Adab al-Qada' al-Khassaf, indicating the strength of the transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الواحد العدل. ولو أخبره عدلان أنه باعه من ذي اليد له أن يشهد بما علم ولا يلتفت إلى قولهما؛ كذا في البزازية أيضاً. هـ. حتى يشهد فعلى هذا عن وفيها في الشهادة بالتسامع : إذا شهد عندك عدلان بخلاف ما سمعته ممن وقع في قلبك صدقه لم يسع لك الشهادة إلا إذا علمت يقيناً أنهما كاذبان وإن شهد عندك عدل بخلاف ما وقع في قلبك من سماع الخبر لك أن تشهد بالأول إلا أن يقع في قلبك صدق الواحد في الأمر الثاني ا هـ . وينبغي أن يكون الاستثناآن في كل شهادة كما لا يخفى . الخامس أن يكون القاضي الذي طلب الشاهد للأداء عنده عدلاً لما في البزازية : وأجاب خلف بن أيوب فيمن له شهادة فرفعت إلى قاض غير عدل له أن الأداء يمتنع عن عند قاض عدل ا هـ. وجزم به في السراجية معللاً بأنه ربما لا يقبل ويجرح ا لو غلب على ظنه أنه يقبله لشهرته مثلاً ينبغي أن يتعين عليه الأداء، وكذا المعدل لو سأل الشاهد فأخبر بأنه غير عدل لا يجب عليه أن يعدله عنده وهي في أدب القضاء للخصاف.
The single just [witness]. And if two just men inform him that he sold it to the possessor, he may testify based on what he knows and does not pay attention to their statement; likewise in al-Bazzaziyyah. And in it regarding testimony by hearsay: If two just men testify before you contrary to what you heard from someone your heart believes is truthful, it is not permissible for you to testify unless you know with certainty that they are liars. And if a single just man testifies before you contrary to what your heart believes from hearing the news, you may testify based on the first unless your heart believes the truthfulness of the single [witness] in the second matter. And it is fitting that the two exceptions apply to every testimony as is not hidden. Fifth: The judge who requested the witness for performance must be just. For in al-Bazzaziyyah: Khalaf ibn Ayyub answered regarding one who has a testimony and it is raised to an unjust judge: He may refrain from performing before a just judge. And he affirmed it in al-Sirajiyyah, reasoning that perhaps it will not be accepted and a flaw will be found. But if he strongly believes that he will accept it due to his fame, for example, then he must perform. Likewise, the modifier, if he asked the witness and he informed him that he is not just, he is not obliged to modify him before him. And this is in Adab al-Qada' al-Khassaf.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two distinct issues. First, the ruling on hearsay testimony (shahada bi al-tasamu'): if two just witnesses testify before you contrary to what you personally heard from someone you believe is truthful, you may not testify based on your prior knowledge unless you are certain the two witnesses are lying. However, if the witness is a single just man, you may testify based on what you heard first unless your heart settles on the truthfulness of the single witness in the second matter. The commentator notes that these exceptions apply in every testimony. Second, the condition that the judge before whom the witness is to testify must be just (condition number 5). Citing Khalaf ibn Ayyub, if the judge is unjust, the witness may refrain from testifying. But if he has strong reason to believe the unjust judge will accept his testimony (e.g., due to the judge's fame for accepting testimonies), then testifying becomes obligatory. Additionally, if a witness informs a modifier (mu'addil) that a person is unjust, the modifier is not obligated to modify him in court. All rulings are based on Hanafi sources such as al-Bazzaziyyah, al-Sirajiyyah, and Adab al-Qada' al-Khassaf.

Key Terms
الشهادة بالتسامع (al-shahadah bi al-tasamu'): Testimony based on what one has heard from others, not direct sensory experience.
عدل (adl): A just person whose testimony is acceptable; one who avoids major sins and does not persist in minor sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a witness do if two just men testify contrary to what he heard from a truthful person?
A) He must accept their testimony and reject his own knowledge.
B) He may not testify unless he knows with certainty that the two are liars.
C) He must always testify based on his own knowledge.
D) He may choose whichever testimony he prefers.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a witness's duty to testify depends on the reliability of his own knowledge and the justice of the judge.

Conditions for Testimony: Fear of Duress and Excessive Distance
Rulings on witness fearing harm, distance to court, and accepting food or transport.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions (fear and distance) that excuse a witness from testifying, and apply the Hanafi ruling regarding transport for an elderly witness.

Core Idea
A witness is excused if testifying would cause harm, whether from fear or excessive travel.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two more conditions that affect the obligation to testify. The sixth condition concerns the witness's knowledge of the confessor's fear; the seventh deals with distance and the provision of transport. These rulings are anchored in the Quranic prohibition against harming witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the passage to find the sixth and seventh conditions. The sixth is that the witness must not know the confessor confessed out of fear. The seventh is that the witness's location must be close enough to return home the same day.
2
Trace the dalil from the Quran
The Quranic verse 2:282 is cited to prohibit harming witnesses. The phrase 'lā yuḍārra' indicates that imposing hardship like excessive travel is not allowed.
The dalil is qat'i in thubut and dalala.
3
Distinguish the elderly witness ruling
If the witness is elderly and cannot walk, the plaintiff may provide a ride without invalidating testimony. If the witness is able to walk, providing a ride invalidates the testimony.
The rationale is honoring witnesses (ikram al-shuhud), not bribery.
4
Apply to a new scenario
Consider a witness who lives 40 km from court with no public transport, taking a full day round trip. He is not sinful if he does not testify because of hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس أن لا يقف الشاهد على أن المقر أقر خوفاً فإن علم بذلك لا يشهد، فإن قال المقر أقررت خوفاً وكان المقر له سلطاناً، فإن كان في يد عون من أعوان السلطان ولم يعلم الشاهد بخوفه شهد عند القاضي وأخبره أنه كان في يد عون من أعوان السلطان كما في البزازية . السابع أن يكون موضع الشاهد قريباً من موضع القاضي، فإن كان بعيداً بحيث لا يمكنه أن يغدو إلى القاضي لأداء الشهادة ويرجع إلى أهله في يومه ذلك قالوا لا يأثم لأنه يلحقه الضرر بذلك، وقال تعالى ولا يضار كاتب ولا شهيد [البقرة : ۲۸۲] ثم إن كان الشاهد شيخاً كبيراً لا يقدر على المشي إلى مجلس الحاكم وليس له شيء للركوب فأركبه المدعي من . قالوا لا بأس به وتقبل به شهادته لأنه من باب الإكرام للشهود، وفي الحديث «أكرموا الشهود» وإن كان يقدر وأركبه المدعي من عنده قالوا لا تقبل ؛ كذا ذكره الشارح. وفي القنية : الشهود في الرستاق واحتيج إلى أداء شهادتهم هل يلزمهم كراء الدابة؟ قال : لا رواية فيه ولكني سمعت من المشايخ أنه يلزمهم ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير : ولو وضع للشهود طعاماً فأكلوا إن كان مهيئاً من قبل ذلك تقبل، وإن صنعه لأجلهم لا تقبل، وعن محمد لا تقبل فيهما، وعن أبي يوسف تقبل فيهما للعادة الجارية بإطعام من حل محل الإنسان ممن يعز عليه شاهداً أو لا ويؤنسه ما تقدم من أن الإهداء إذا كان بلا شرط ليقضي حاجته عند الأمير تجوز؛ كذا قيل وفيه نظر فإن الأداء فرض بخلاف الذهاب إلى الأمير ا هـ . الملتقط وجزم في
Sixth: That the witness does not know that the confessor confessed out of fear; if he knows that, he should not testify. If the confessor says 'I confessed out of fear' and the beneficiary is a ruler, and if [the confessor] was in the hand of an aide of the ruler and the witness does not know of his fear, he may testify before the judge and inform him that he was in the hand of an aide of the ruler, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. Seventh: That the place of the witness is close to the place of the judge; if it is far such that he cannot go to the judge to perform testimony and return to his family in that same day, they said he does not sin because harm would befall him, and Allah said: 'And do not harm the scribe or the witness' [2:282]. Then if the witness is an elderly man unable to walk to the court and has no means of riding, and the plaintiff provides him a ride, they said there is no harm and his testimony is accepted because it is from the category of honoring witnesses, and in the hadith: 'Honor the witnesses'. But if he is able [to walk] and the plaintiff provides him a ride, they said it is not accepted. This is what the commentator mentioned. In al-Qunyah: Witnesses in the countryside and need for their testimony: Is hiring a mount obligatory upon them? He said: There is no narration about it, but I heard from the shaykhs that it is obligatory. In Fath al-Qadir: If food is placed for witnesses and they eat: if it was prepared previously, it is accepted; if prepared for them, it is not accepted. According to Muhammad, it is not accepted in both cases. According to Abu Yusuf, it is accepted in both cases due to the prevalent custom of feeding those who visit, whether witness or not, and the previous point that gifting without condition to fulfill a need before an authority is permissible. This is said but there is consideration, for performing testimony is an obligation unlike going to the ruler. Al-Multaqat and decided in ...
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage presents three more conditions (6th, 7th) regarding the obligation to testify, along with related rulings. Condition six: the witness must not be aware that the person making a confession did so out of fear. If he knows, he cannot testify on that confession. However, if he is unaware of the fear and the confessor was under a ruler's aide's authority, he may testify and inform the judge of the circumstances. Condition seven: the witness's location should be near the court. If it is so far that he cannot travel there and back in one day, he is not sinful for refusing to testify, based on the Quranic verse forbidding harm to scribes or witnesses. For an elderly witness who cannot walk and has no transport, it is permissible for the plaintiff to provide a ride and the testimony is accepted, as honoring witnesses is recommended (the hadith 'Akrimum al-shuhud'). But if the witness is capable, providing a ride makes the testimony unacceptable. The text then discusses hiring mounts for distant witnesses (opinion it is obligatory) and the issue of witnesses eating food provided by the plaintiff: if prepared before their arrival, testimony is accepted; if prepared specifically for them, it is not according to one view. There is ikhtilaf between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf: Muhammad rejects acceptance in both cases, Abu Yusuf accepts in both due to custom. The author notes a problem: testimony is obligatory, unlike gifts to rulers.

Key Terms
المقر (al-muqqir): The person who makes a confession (iqrar) that may involve another's right.
الرستاق (al-rustaq): The countryside or rural area, as opposed to the city (misr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on testimony if an elderly witness cannot walk and the plaintiff provides a ride?
A) The testimony is not accepted because the ride is a bribe.
B) The testimony is accepted because it is honoring the witness.
C) The testimony is accepted only if the witness pays for the ride.
D) The testimony is not accepted unless the witness is forced to ride.

Key Takeaway
A witness is exempt from testifying if it would cause him harm, whether from fear or excessive distance.

Accepting Food as a Witness: The Ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Rulings on witness fearing harm, distance to court, and accepting food or transport.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute regarding witnesses eating food provided by the litigant, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The acceptance of testimony when witnesses eat food depends on custom and intention, not merely the act of eating.

This passage extends the discussion on witness conditions to the delicate issue of accepting hospitality. While some scholars reject testimony if food was prepared specifically for the witnesses, the Hanafi school follows Abu Yusuf's view that customary hospitality does not disqualify testimony. Understanding this ikhtilaf highlights the Hanafi reliance on 'urf (custom).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios for food
Find the three cases: (1) food prepared beforehand, (2) food prepared for the occasion, and (3) the two opinions of Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.
2
Analyze Muhammad's view
Muhammad says testimony is not accepted in either case, considering any food from the litigant as potential bribery.
This is a strict view.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf says testimony is accepted in both cases due to prevalent custom of feeding visitors, and because the intention is not necessarily corrupt.
This view relies on 'urf.
4
Understand the author's critique
The author notes that testimony is a religious obligation (fard), unlike a gift to a ruler to fulfill a need, so the analogy is imperfect.
This does not overturn the fatwa; it's a note of caution.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage indicates that the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view, as it is the relied-upon position due to custom.
This is the operative ruling for practical fatwa.

Food and Transport for Witnesses – The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on acceptance of testimony when witnesses eat food or ride mounts provided by litigant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the acceptance of testimony when witnesses eat food or ride mounts provided by the litigant, and explain the tarjih (preferred view) and its basis.

Core Idea
Custom permits incidental hospitality but not preparation for testimony.

In the previous lesson, we saw the general discussion in al-Hidayah. Here, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq brings a quote from Sharh Manzumah Ibn Wahban that elaborates on the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Both imams agree that deliberate bribery invalidates testimony, but they differ when the litigant provides food or transport without explicit condition. Understanding this dispute teaches us how Hanafi jurists balance the need to prevent corruption with the reality of customary hospitality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
The passage describes two main scenarios: (1) witnesses taken to a farm and given mounts to ride, and (2) witnesses fed food by the litigant. In each, the ruling depends on the witnesses' ability and the litigant's intent.
Note the distinction between inability (no strength to walk, no ability to hire) and ability.
2
Distinguish preparation from hospitality
Abu al-Layth distinguishes: if the litigant had food and offered it without prior preparation, testimony is accepted; if he prepared food specifically for them, testimony is rejected. This applies when the purpose is testimony.
The key is whether the provision was specially arranged for the witnesses' role.
3
Compare Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
When the litigant gathers people for testimony and provides food/transport as part of that gathering, Abu Yusuf accepts testimony in both cases (food and mounts), while Muhammad rejects in both. This is the core intra-Hanafi dispute.
Their disagreement stems from different weight given to custom ('ādah) vs. the danger of influence.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The tarjih (preferred view) is that of Abu Yusuf, as stated in Sharh Manzumah Ibn Wahban. Custom is given precedence, unless there is clear evidence of bribery.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His statement: (And in Sharh Manzumah Ibn Wahban... etc.) I say: Its commentator, the scholar Abd al-Barr ibn... from Mukhtasar al-Muhit by al-Khabbazi: He took the witnesses to a farm he bought and hired mounts for them to ride: if they do not have the strength to walk nor the ability to hire, their testimony is accepted; otherwise no. If they ate food belonging to the one for whom testimony is given, their testimony is not rejected. And Abu al-Layth said: The answer regarding riding is as stated; as for food, if the one for whom testimony is given did not prepare food for the witness, but rather had food and offered it to them and they ate, their testimony is not rejected. If he prepared food for them and they ate, their testimony is not accepted. This is if he did that for the purpose of testimony. If it was not like that, but rather he gathered people for testimony and prepared food for them or sent them mounts and brought them out of the city, and they rode and ate his food, they differed regarding it. The second said: ...
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the impact of providing food and transport to witnesses. It reports a scenario from Sharh Manzumah Ibn Wahban: if a person bought a farm and brought witnesses there on hired mounts, the acceptance of their testimony depends on their ability to walk or hire on their own. If they cannot, testimony is accepted; otherwise not. Regarding food, Abu al-Layth distinguishes: if the litigant already had food and offered it, testimony is accepted; if he prepared it specifically for them, it is not accepted. However, if the litigant gathered people for testimony and provided food/transport as part of that gathering, there is ikhtilaf. The text cuts off in the middle of the second opinion (likely Muhammad's vs. Abu Yusuf's). The first part of this issue was discussed on page 98 (lesson 2), where Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed. Here, the dispute is further elaborated, possibly reaching a tarjih. The incomplete ending suggests the tarjih was given later. Nonetheless, the passage shows the Hanafi concern with preventing bribery or undue influence while acknowledging customary hospitality.

Key Terms
الضيعة (al-day'ah): A farm or estate purchased by the litigant.
الكراء (al-kira'): Hiring, especially of mounts for travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Their testimony is accepted according to all.
B) Their testimony is rejected according to all.
C) Abu Yusuf accepts, Muhammad rejects.
D) Abu Yusuf rejects, Muhammad accepts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi on provision of food or transport to witnesses accepts testimony unless there is clear evidence of bribery, based on custom and necessity.

Testimony After Witness Receives Ride or Food: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony after receiving ride/food

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on testimony after receiving a ride or food, and apply the mufta bihi ruling based on custom.

Core Idea
Custom (urf) can override the general rule that receiving a benefit disqualifies a witness, if the benefit is customary and not corrupting.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether testimony is accepted from a witness who received a ride or food from the litigant. The general principle is that any appearance of bias may disqualify a witness. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes based on necessity and custom. The dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani highlights how custom ('urf) can influence legal rulings. The fatwa follows Abu Yusuf's view, especially in customary gatherings like weddings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What specific benefit did the witness receive? (ride, food) and in what context (customary gathering vs. direct preparation)? This determines the ruling.
The source discusses two scenarios: riding and eating.
2
State the general Hanafi principle
A witness should be free from any appearance of bias that could influence testimony. Receiving a benefit from the litigant is generally a disqualifying factor.
This principle is qualified by necessity and custom.
3
Map the disagreement
Abu Yusuf distinguishes between riding and eating in customary contexts; Muhammad rejects both uniformly. Identify where they differ.
Abu Yusuf accepts testimony after eating in customary gatherings but rejects after riding if not needed.
4
Identify the basis of each position
Abu Yusuf relies on custom (urf) and the fact that people routinely do these actions in social events. Muhammad adheres to strict avoidance of any bias appearance.
Both are valid Hanafi methodologies.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its rationale
The fatwa follows Abu Yusuf because custom indicates no corruption, especially in weddings. If the practice were corrupting, scholars would have prohibited it.
This is a practical application of istihsan based on urf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وفي شرح منظومة ابن وهبان (الخ أقول قال شارحها العلامة عبد البر بن الشحنة نقلاً عن مختصر المحيط للخبازي أخرج الشهود إلى ضيعة اشتراها فاستأجر لهم دواب ليركبوها إن لم يكن لهم قوة المشي ولا طاقة الكري تقبل شهادتهم وإلا فلا فإن أكل طعاماً للمشهود له لا ترد شهادته . وقال الفقيه أبو الليث : الجواب في الركوب ما قال أما في الطعام إن لم يكن المشهود له هيأ طعامه للشاهد بل كان عنده طعام فقدمه إليهم وأكلوه لا ترد شهادتهم، وإن هيأ لهم طعاماً فأكلوه لا تقبل شهادتهم. هذا إذا فعل ذلك لأداء الشهادة، فإن لم يكن كذلك لكنه جمع الناس للاستشهاد وهيأ لهم طعاماً أو بعث لهم دواب وأخرجهم من المصر فركبوا وأكلوا طعامه اختلفوا فيه ؛ قال الثاني : في خلاف الركوب لا تقبل شهادتهم بعد ذلك وتقبل في أكل الطعام. وقال محمد : لا تقبل فيهما. والفتوى على قول الثاني لجري العادة به سيما في الأنكحة ونثر السكر والدراهم، ولو كان قادحاً في الشهادة لما فعلوه ؛ كذا في الفخرية .اهـ.
He said: (And in the commentary on the Manzuma of Ibn Wahban by the author: I say, the commentator, the scholar 'Abd al-Barr ibn al-Shihna, quoting from Mukhtasar al-Muhit of al-Khabbazi: If a man takes witnesses to a property he bought and hires animals for them to ride, if they do not have the strength to walk or the ability to hire (a mount), their testimony is accepted; otherwise it is not. If they eat food belonging to the one for whom they testify, their testimony is not rejected. And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: The answer regarding riding is as stated. As for food, if the one for whom they testify did not prepare the food for the witness, but he had food and offered it to them and they ate, their testimony is not rejected. But if he prepared food for them and they ate, their testimony is not accepted. This applies if he did that for the sake of testimony. If he did not do that, but he gathered people for witnessing and prepared food for them, or sent animals and took them out of the city, and they rode and ate his food, they differed regarding this. The second (i.e., Abu Yusuf) said: In the difference about riding, their testimony is not accepted afterward, but it is accepted regarding eating food. And Muhammad said: It is not accepted in both. The fatwa is on the statement of the second due to custom, especially in marriages and the scattering of sugar and dirhams. If it were a defect in testimony, they would not have done it. Thus in al-Fakhriyya.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute, quoted from a commentary on Ibn Wahban's poem, regarding the admissibility of testimony when the witness has received a ride or food from the party for whom they testify. The general rule is that any benefit that suggests bias may disqualify a witness. The specifics: If the witness needed the ride (could not walk or hire), testimony is accepted; if they could manage without, it is rejected. For food, if pre-prepared, testimony is rejected; if merely offered spontaneously, it is accepted. The dispute arises when the action (providing ride/food) is not directly tied to the testimony but part of a general gathering (e.g., wedding). Abu Yusuf (the 'second') distinguishes: testimony is rejected for riding (stronger benefit) but accepted for food in that context. Muhammad rejects both. The fatwa follows Abu Yusuf due to custom in marriages where such hospitality is normal. The key 'illa is the appearance of bias; custom can override if universally practiced without harm.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahada): Testimony in court, specifically about one's observation of a contract or event.
الطعام (al-ta'am): Food offered to witnesses, which might create bias.
الركوب (al-rukub): Riding a mount provided by the litigant, considered a benefit that could bias the witness.
العادة (al-'adah): Custom, accepted as a legal source (urf) that can modify default rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The testimony is rejected in all cases.
B) The testimony is accepted due to custom.
C) The testimony is accepted only if the witness paid for the food.
D) The testimony is rejected if the food was prepared for the witnesses.

Key Takeaway
When a witness receives a benefit from a litigant, the Hanafi school does not automatically disqualify the testimony; custom and necessity are weighed, and the fatwa follows Abu Yusuf's view that custom excuses ordinary hospitality.

Testimony of Backgammon Players: Abu Hanifa vs. Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness qualification due to sinful profession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on the testimony of backgammon players and identify the mufta bihi ruling with its rationale based on custom.

Core Idea
Custom can shift the fatwa from a partial to a total rejection of testimony.

The Hanafi school weighs custom (urf) heavily in legal rulings. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq reveals how custom influenced the fatwa on the testimony of backgammon players, overriding Imam Abu Hanifa's original position in favor of Imam Muhammad's stricter view.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
According to the narration from Abu Hanifa, the testimony of a habitual backgammon player is rejected only in matters related to that game, but accepted in other matters like eating food.
His position distinguishes between areas of sin and areas of integrity.
2
Identify Muhammad's opposing view
Imam Muhammad holds that testimony is rejected in all matters, whether related to backgammon or not. The passage states 'wa qala Muhammad: la tuqbal fihima' (and Muhammad said: it is not accepted in either).
This is a total rejection based on the person's habitual sin.
3
Analyze the tarjih mechanism
The fatwa is given on Muhammad's view (al-fatwa 'ala qawl al-thani) because of custom: 'li jary al-'ada bihi' (due to the custom). The author cites that in marriages and other social events, such games are common, and if the custom impaired testimony, people would not engage in them. But the custom is widespread, so the stricter view is adopted.
Custom here reinforces the need to protect the integrity of testimony.
4
Consider the critique and refinement
Later scholars like Abd al-Barr ibn al-Shahna and the author of Fath al-Qadir comment that this ruling is absolute for matters of intercourse and applies to any profession that cannot be interpreted as permissible. This expands the ruling beyond backgammon.
The expansion probe (textual_operation_tag) shows how the ruling broadens.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, a backgammon player can testify about a sale of food; under Muhammad, he cannot. The mufta bihi view (Muhammad's) means such a person is disqualified from all testimony unless he repents.
This protects the judiciary from unreliable witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
به خلاف الركوب لا تقبل شهادتهم بعد ذلك وتقبل في أكل الطعام. وقال محمد : لا تقبل فيهما. والفتوى على قول الثاني لجري العادة به سيما في الأنكحة ونثر السكر والدراهم، ولو كان قادحاً في الشهادة لما فعلوه ; كذا في الفخرية .اهـ. قوله : (وتعقبه في فتح القدير بقوله (الخ قال العلامة عبد البر بن الشحنة : وعندي أن الوجه كما قال شيخ الإسلام سيما وقد فسد الزمان وعلم من حال الشهود التوقف وهذا مطلق عن مسائل الفروج، والظاهر أن هذا مطرد في كل حرفة لا يتوجه فيها تأويل قوله: (وفي الملتقط الإشهاد على المداينات والبيوع (فرض) قال في التتارخانية عن المحيط : وذكر في فتاوى أهل سمرقند أن الإشهاد على المداينة والبيع فرض على العباد إلا إذا كان شيئاً حقيراً لا يخاف عليه التلف، وبعض المشايخ على أن الإشهاد مندوب وليس بفرض .
Concerning [the profession of] backgammon: their testimony is not accepted [in matters related to it] but is accepted in eating food. Muhammad said: it is not accepted in either. The fatwa is on the latter's [Muhammad's] view due to custom, especially regarding marriages and scattering sugar and dirhams. If it were damaging to testimony, they would not have done it. End quote from al-Fakhriyya. He said: (And he criticized it in Fath al-Qadir with his statement) al-Allama Abd al-Barr ibn al-Shahna said: In my view, the correct opinion is as Shaykh al-Islam said, especially since time has become corrupt and the situation of witnesses is known to be such, and this is absolute regarding matters of intercourse, and the apparent is that this applies to every profession in which no valid interpretation is possible. He said: (And in al-Multaqit: testifying in debts and sales is fard). He said in al-Tatarakhaniyya from al-Muhit: it is mentioned in the fatwas of the people of Samarkand that testifying in debts and sales is fard upon the servants, except if it is a trivial thing that is not feared to be lost. And some mashayikh hold that testifying is mandub and not fard.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two issues. First, the testimony of people who engage in the profession of playing backgammon (or similar pastimes that are sinful). According to the narration from Abu Hanifa, their testimony is not accepted in matters related to that activity (e.g., if they testify about a transaction during a game), but it is accepted in other matters like eating food. Imam Muhammad holds that it is not accepted in either case. The fatwa is on Muhammad's view due to custom, especially in matters like marriage and scattering sugar and dirhams (probably referring to customs at weddings). Second, the passage discusses whether testifying in sales and debts is obligatory (fard) or recommended (mandub). The preferred view from the fatwa of Samarqand is that it is fard kifayah (communal obligation) unless the property is trivial and not feared lost. Some mashayikh consider it mandub.

Key Terms
خلاف الركوب (khilaf al-rukub): Referring to the profession of playing backgammon (النرد) or similar pastimes; 'ركوب' is likely a textual corruption.
الفتوى على قول الثاني (al-fatwa 'ala qawl al-thani): The operative legal opinion is based on the view of the second person (here, Imam Muhammad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the fatwa given on Imam Muhammad's view regarding the testimony of backgammon players?
A) Because Muhammad's view is the majority opinion among the Sahaba.
B) Because of the widespread custom of such games, which indicates that a lenient view would open the door to unreliable testimony.
C) Because Abu Hanifa's view has no textual support.
D) Because the testimony of all sinners is always rejected.

Key Takeaway
Custom can cause the fatwa to shift from a partial restriction to a total disqualification of testimony when the sin is widespread and indicates general moral laxity.

Obligation to Testify in Sales and Debts: Fard vs. Mandub
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal status of testifying in commercial transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions on the obligation to testify in sales and debts, and identify the mufta bihi as fard kifayah with exceptions for trivial matters.

Core Idea
Testifying in sales and debts is a communal obligation unless the matter is trivial.

Witnessing and testifying to contracts protects people's rights. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a dispute among later Hanafi scholars: is testifying in sales and debts obligatory (fard) or merely recommended (mandub)? The fatwa from Samarqand leans towards obligation, with an exception for insignificant matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
One group of scholars, as mentioned in the fatwa of Samarqand, holds that testifying in sales and debts is fard (obligatory) upon the servants (i.e., fard kifayah). Another group holds that it is mandub (recommended).
The passage quotes from al-Multaqit and al-Muhit.
2
Determine the scope of the fard position
The obligation applies unless the property is 'trivial and not feared to be lost' (shay' haqir la yukhaf 'alayhi al-talaf). This means for significant transactions, testimony is required to safeguard rights.
The exception shows that the fard is not absolute.
3
Analyze the mandub position
Some mashayikh (scholars) consider it merely mandub, meaning it is good to testify but not sinful to omit.
This position gives more flexibility.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The passage does not explicitly declare which is mufta bihi, but the context (listing the fard position first, citing fatwa collections) suggests that the fard position is the relied-upon view among later Hanafis.
Later Hanafi works often affirm the obligation.
5
Practical consequence
Under the fard view, if a Muslim witnesses a significant sale or debt, he must testify if called upon; otherwise, he sins. Under the mandub view, he does not sin but is rewarded for testifying.
This affects the duty of Muslims in commercial transactions.

Testifying in Hudud: When to Conceal and When to Testify
Explains the Hanafi position on testifying in hudud and its usul justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testifying in hudud, distinguishing between private repentant and habitual public sinners, and explain the usul justification for specifying the general Quranic command.

Core Idea
The Quranic command to testify is general, but specified by famous hadiths of concealment and ijma.

A witness in a hudud case faces a dilemma: the Quran commands testimony, but hadiths like that of Ma'iz encourage concealment. The Hanafi school resolves this by recognizing that the ruling is not absolute—it depends on the sinner's state. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this nuanced position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary sources
Start with the Quranic verse (2:282) which commands testimony in general terms. Then note the hadiths of concealment (e.g., the hadith of Ma'iz) that seem to contradict that command.
The verse 'ولا يأب الشهداء إذا ما دعوا' is general.
2
Recognize the apparent conflict
The general command implies testimony is wajib in all cases, but the hadiths suggest concealment is better. This conflict must be resolved.
The conflict is between a qat'i general (Quran) and zanni specific (ahad hadith).
3
Apply Hanafi usul: takhsis via shuhra and ijma
Hanafis argue that the hadiths of concealment have reached fame (shuhra) and been accepted by the ummah (ijma), so they can specify the Quranic general. Alternatively, the ijma itself is the specifier.
Shuhra elevates ahad hadith to a level where it can specify the Quran.
4
Derive the nuanced ruling
Once specified, the general command is limited. For a private, repentant sinner, concealment is recommended (mandub). For a habitual, public sinner, testimony becomes more virtuous because it serves the purpose of deterrence.
The ruling is contextual, not absolute.
5
Address the opposing view
The Shafi'i school holds that ahad hadith cannot specify the Quran, so testimony remains wajib always. Hanafis respond by citing shuhra and ijma.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات
لأجل إيمانهم وذلك صفة الكافر، ولأن مقصود الشاهد ارتفاعها لا إشاعتها، وكذا لا يعارض أفضلية الستر آية النهي عن كتمانها لأنها من حقوق العباد بدليل قوله تعالى ولا يأب الشهداء إذا ما دعوا [البقرة : ٢٨٢] إذ الحدود لا مدعي فيها ورد قول من قال إنها في الديون بأن العبرة لعموم اللفظ لا لخصوص السبب كما ذكره الرازي أو لأنه عام مخصوص بأحاديث الستر وفي فتح القدير فإن قلت : كيف صح لك القول بتخصيص عام الكتاب بهذه وهي أخبار آحاد؟ وأيضاً شرط التخصيص عندكم المقارنة، ومن أين ثبت لك ذلك؟ قلت: هذه الأخبار الواردة في طلب الستر بلغت مبلغاً لا ينحط بها عن درجة الشهرة لتعدد متونها مع قبول الأمة لها فصح التخصيص بها أو هي مستند الإجماع على تخيير الشاهد في الحدود، فثبوت الإجماع دليل ثبوت المخصص. وأما المقارنة فإنما هي شرط التخصيص في نفس الأمر وهذا التخصيص الذي ادعيناه ليس بذلك بل هو جمع للمعارضة على ما كتبناه في التعارض في كتاب تحرير الأصول من أن الجمع بين العام والخاص إذا تعارضا بأن يحمل على تخصيصه به، فإذا وجب حمله على ذلك تضمن الحكم منا بأنه كان مقارناً أو لأنها ليست مخصصات أول كما إذا رجحنا في التعارض المحرم على المبيح وثبت صحتها تضمن حكمنا بأن المبيح كان مقدماً على المحرم فنسخ حكم الوجوب ترجيح المحرم وإن لم يعلم تقدمه بعلم تاريخه، وكثيراً ما يعترض بعض متأخري الشارحين على كثير من المواضع المحكوم فيها بالتخصيص من أصحابنا بأن المقارنة غير معلومة فلا يثبت التخصيص ومرادهم في تلك الأماكن ما ذكرنا . هذا كله إذا نظرنا إلى مجرد إطلاق قوله تعالى ولا يأب الشهداء إذا ما دعوا أما إذا قيدناه بما إذا دعوا للشهادة في الدين المذكور أول الآية فظاهر ا هـ . والأخر مردود بما قدمناه . وفيه أيضاً من كتاب الحدود وإذا كان الستر مندوباً إليه ينبغي أن تكون الشهادة الأولى التي مرجعها إلى كراهة التنزيه لأنها في رتبة الندب في جانب الفعل وكراهة التنزيه في جانب الترك، وهذا يجب أن يكون بالنسبة إلى من لم يعتد بالزنا ولم يتهتك به أما إذا وصل به الحال إلى إشاعته والتهتك به بل بعضهم ربما افتخر به فيجب كون الشهادة أولى من تركها لأن مطلوب الشارع إخلاء الأرض من المعاصي والفواحش بالخطابات المفيدة لذلك، وذلك يتحقق بالتوبة من الغافلين وبالزجر لهم فإذا ظهر حال الشهرة في الزنا مثلاً والشرب وعدم المبالاة به وإشاعته فإخلاء الأرض المطلوب حينئذ بالتوبة احتمال يقابله ظهور عدمها ممن اتصف بذلك فيجب تحقيق السبب الآخر للإخلاء وهو الحدود خلاف من زنى مرة أو مراراً مستتراً متخوفاً متندماً عليه فإنه محل استحباب ستر الشاهد وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لهزال في ماعز لو كنت سترته بثوبك الحديث وسيأتي كان في مثل من ذكرنا. على هذا ذكره في غيره مجلس القاضي، وأداء الشهادة بمنزلة الغيبة فيه فيحرم منه ما يحرم منها ويحل منه ما يحل منها ا هـ
For the sake of their faith, and that is the attribute of the disbeliever. And because the objective of the witness is to remove it, not to publicize it. Similarly, the superiority of concealment does not oppose the verse prohibiting its concealment, because it is among the rights of people, evidenced by His saying: 'And let not the witnesses refuse when they are called' [2:282] since hudud have no claimant. And the statement of those who said it is about debts is rejected because consideration is for the generality of the wording, not the specific cause, as mentioned by al-Razi. Or because it is a general text specified by the hadiths of concealment. And in Fath al-Qadir: 'If you say: How can you claim specification of the general of the Book by these when they are isolated reports? Also, specification at your view requires contemporaneity, so how do you establish that? I say: These reports on seeking concealment have reached a level not below fame (shuhra) due to the multiplicity of their texts and the acceptance of the ummah for them, so specification by them is sound. Or they are the basis of ijma on giving the witness a choice in hudud, so the existence of ijma is evidence for the existence of the specifier. As for contemporaneity, it is only a condition for specification in reality, and this specification we claim is not that, but rather it is a reconciliation of conflicting evidence, as we wrote in Kitab Tahrir al-Usul: that the combination of general and specific when they conflict is by interpreting the general as specified by the specific. So when it is necessary to interpret it that way, it implies our ruling that it was contemporaneous, or because they are not primary specifics, just as when we prefer the prohibited over the permitted in conflicting evidence and its soundness is established, it implies our ruling that the permitted was prior to the prohibited, so the ruling of obligation is abrogated by preferring the prohibited, even if its precedence is not known by historical knowledge. Many later commentators object to many places where our scholars rule specification on the grounds that contemporaneity is unknown, so specification is not established, but their intent in those places is what we mentioned. All this is if we consider the mere absolute wording of His saying 'And let not the witnesses refuse when they are called'. But if we restrict it to when they are called for testimony in the debt mentioned at the beginning of the verse, then it is apparent. End. And the other is refuted by what we presented. And also in it from the Book of Hudud: If concealment is recommended (mandub), then testifying originally should be makruh tanzihan, because it is in the rank of recommended in the act and makruh tanzihi in leaving. This should be for one who is not accustomed to zina and does not publicize it. But when his situation reaches publicizing and being unscrupulous, and some even boast about it, then testifying becomes more virtuous than leaving it, because the objective of the Lawgiver is to clear the earth of sins and indecencies by beneficial discourses. That is achieved by repentance of the heedless and deterrence for them. So when the state of notoriety in zina, for example, drinking, and lack of concern and publicizing appears, then clearing the earth by repentance is a probability that is countered by the apparent lack of it from those described, so the other means of clearance, which is hudud, must be implemented. This is contrary to one who commits zina once or multiple times in concealment, fearfully, repentantly, for that is the place of recommending concealment by the witness, and his saying, peace be upon him, to Hazzal regarding Ma'iz: 'If you had covered him with your garment...' The hadith will come in similar cases. Based on this, it is mentioned in other places: sitting in the judge's court, and giving testimony is like backbiting; so what is forbidden in backbiting is forbidden here, and what is permitted is permitted here.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the Hanafi ruling on testifying in hudud (fixed punishments) cases. The author resolves the apparent conflict between the Quranic command in 2:282 to testify when called and the Prophetic ahadith encouraging concealment of sins (like the hadith of Ma'iz). The Hanafi position, building on earlier works like Fath al-Qadir, holds that the general command is specified by the ahadith of concealment, which have reached the level of shuhra (fame) and are supported by ijma. Thus, for a first-time offender who sins secretly and is repentant, it is recommended (mandub) for the witness to conceal. However, for habitual sinners who publicize their sin and show no remorse, testimony becomes more virtuous (first) because the objective of the Lawgiver—clearing the earth of sin—cannot be achieved by repentance alone. In such cases, the witness should testify to uphold public order. The passage also analogizes giving testimony in such cases to backbiting: it is prohibited or permitted in the same situations as backbiting.

Key Terms
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general term (عام) by a specific text (خاص), narrowing its application.
عام (amm): A word that includes all individuals of its class without limitation.
شهرة (shuhra): Fame of a hadith due to multiple chains and acceptance by scholars, ranking between mutawatir and ahad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when is it recommended for a witness to testify in a hudud case?
A) When the sin is committed in private and the sinner is repentant.
B) When the sin is publicized and the sinner shows no remorse.
C) Only when the judge commands the witness to testify.
D) In all cases of hudud, regardless of circumstances.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on testifying in hudud is contextual: concealment is recommended for private repentant sinners, while testimony is more virtuous for habitual public sinners.

The Proper Wording in Theft Testimony: 'Took' vs. 'Stole'
Ruling on preferred wording in theft testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the wordings 'akhadha' and 'saraqa' in theft testimony and explain why 'akhadha' is preferred in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Saying 'took' preserves concealment and allows compensation; saying 'stole' could trigger amputation which bars compensation.

When testifying in a theft case, the wording matters. The Hanafi school recommends saying 'he took' rather than 'he stole,' a distinction rooted in the legal consequences of each term. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this preference and clarifies that both wordings are permissible, though one is more appropriate for protecting the rights of the victim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two wordings
Note the two Arabic terms: 'akhadha' (he took) and 'saraqa' (he stole). The passage discusses which is better to use in testimony.
The term 'saraqa' implies the full legal definition of theft (sariqa) with conditions for hadd.
2
Understand the legal conflict
If a witness says 'he stole,' it establishes theft (sariqa) which requires amputation (qat'). Amputation is incompatible with compensation (damam). Thus the victim cannot recover their right.
Hanafi fiqh holds that compensation and amputation cannot coexist for the same act.
3
Analyze the story of Abu Yusuf
Consider the historical case: a man confessed to 'taking' not 'stealing.' Abu Yusuf ruled that compensation is established and amputation dropped. A later confession to stealing is not accepted because it would nullify compensation.
This story illustrates the practical application of the preference for 'took.'
4
Determine the ruling's nature
The passage clarifies that saying 'took' is 'better' (أولى) not obligatory. Both wordings are permissible. The statement of al-Quduri 'must say' is interpreted as 'it is established' not legal obligation.
This is a recommendation (sunnah) not a wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويقول في السرقة أخذ لا سرق) إحياء الحق المسروق منه ولا يقول سرق محافظة على الستر ولأنه لو ظهرت السرقة لوجب القطع والضمان لا يجامع القطع فلا يحصل إحياء حقه. وصرح في غاية البيان بأن قوله أخذ أولى من سرق» وعلى هذا فيحمل قول القدوري وجب أن يقول أخذ على معنى ثبت لا الوجوب الفقهي. وقوله في العناية فتعين مع قوله لا يجوز أي أن يقول سرق تسامح وإنما الكلام في الأفضل وكل منهما جائز . وحكى الفخر الرازي في التفسير أن هارون الرشيد كان . مع جماعة الفقهاء وفيهم أبو يوسف فادعى رجل على آخر بأنه أخذ ماله من بيته فأقر بالأخذ فسأل الفقهاء فأفتوا بقطع يده فقال أبو يوسف : لا لأنه لم يقر بالسرقة وإنما أقر بالأخذ فادعى المدعي أنه سرق فأقر بها فأفتوا بالقطع وخالفهم أبو يوسف فقالوا له: لم؟ قال : لأنه لما أقر أولاً بالأخذ وثبت الضمان عليه وسقط القطع فلا يقبل إقراره بعده بما يسقط الضمان عند فعجبوا ا هـ . قوله : (وشرط للزنا أربعة رجال) لقوله تعالى واللاتي يأتين الفاحشة من نسائكم فاستشهدوا عليهن أربعة منكم [النساء : ١٥] ولقوله تعالى ثم لم يأتوا بأربعة شهداء [النور: ٤] ولفظ أربعة نص في العدد والذكورة؛ كذا في البناية وأورد أنكم لا تقولون بالمفهوم فمن أين لكم عدم جواز الأقل؟ فأجاب الزيلعي بأنه بالإجماع وأورد المعارضة بين هذه وبين قوله فاستشهدوا شهيدين [البقرة : ۲۸۲] الآية. وأجاب في فتح القدير بأنها مبيحة وتلك مانعة والتقديم . قوله : (وحكي الفخر الرازي في التفسير الخ) قال الرملي : هذا ظاهر في أنه إذا ادعى أنه أخذ مالي أو دابتي تسمع وإن لم يبين وجه الأخذ اهـ ; ذكره الغزي قوله: (وأورد المعارضة الخ) قال الرملي : عبارة فتح القدير وإن النص أوجب أربعة رجال بقوله تعالى أربعة منكم فقبول امرأتين ثلاثة مخالف لما نص عليه من العدد والمعدود، وغاية الأمر المعارضة بين عموم قوله تعالى فإن لم يكونا رجلين فرجل وامرأتان وبين هذه فتقدم هذه لأنها مانعة وتلك مبيحة اهـ. ولا يخفى عليك ما
He said: 'And in theft, he should say 'he took' not 'he stole' to revive the right of the one from whom it was taken, and he should not say 'he stole' to preserve concealment, because if theft were established, cutting would be obligatory and compensation would not be compatible with cutting, so his right would not be revived. And it was explicitly stated in Ghayat al-Bayan that his saying 'took' is better than 'stole'. Based on this, the statement of al-Quduri 'he must say 'took'' is interpreted to mean 'it is established' not legal obligation. And his statement in al-`Inaya: 'it is determined' alongside his statement 'it is not permissible' for saying 'stole' is lenient; the discussion is about which is better, and both are permissible. And al-Fakhr al-Razi narrated in his Tafsir that Harun al-Rashid was with a group of jurists, among them Abu Yusuf. A man claimed against another that he took his money from his house, and he confessed to taking. He asked the jurists, and they gave a fatwa to cut off his hand. Abu Yusuf said: No, because he did not confess to theft, only to taking. Then the claimant said that he stole, and he confessed to that, so they gave a fatwa to cut, and Abu Yusuf disagreed. They said: Why? He said: Because when he first confessed to taking, compensation was established, and cutting was dropped. His subsequent confession that would drop compensation is not accepted. They were amazed. End. He said: (And the condition for zina is four men) due to His statement: 'And those who commit the unlawful act from your women, bring four witnesses from among you' [4:15] and His statement: 'Then if they do not bring four witnesses' [24:4]. The word 'four' is explicit (nass) regarding the number and masculinity. Thus in al-Binaya. And it was objected that you [Hanafis] do not rely on mafhum al-mukhalafa, so how do you derive the impermissibility of less? Al-Zayla`i answered that it is by ijma. And an objection was raised based on the conflict between this and the verse 'bring two witnesses' [2:282]. He answered in Fath al-Qadir that it [2:282] is permissive, and this [the verses for zina] is prohibitive, and the prohibitive takes precedence. He said: (And al-Fakhr al-Razi narrated in the Tafsir...) al-Ramli said: This is apparent in that if he claims 'he took my money or my animal', it is heard even if he does not explain the manner of taking. Al-Ghazzi mentioned it. He said: (And he raised the objection...) al-Ramli said: The wording of Fath al-Qadir: The text requires four men by His saying 'four from among you'. Accepting two women [instead of a fourth man] would be three, which contradicts what is stated as number and counted. The utmost is that there is a conflict between the generality of His saying 'if they are not two men, then one man and two women' and this [verse]. This [the zina verse] takes precedence because it is prohibitive and that is permissive. End. And it is not hidden from you what [follows].
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers two important points on testimony. First, in theft cases, when testifying, the witness should say 'he took' (أخذ) rather than 'he stole' (سرق). The reason is to preserve concealment and to allow the victim to recover his right through compensation (damam), because if the witness says 'stole', it may lead to amputation (qat') which is incompatible with compensation. The preferred wording is 'took' (أخذ), though both are permissible. The story of Harun al-Rashid and Abu Yusuf illustrates this: a man confessed to taking but not stealing; the first confession established compensation and precluded amputation; a later confession to stealing would not be accepted to drop compensation. Second, the condition for zina testimony is four male witnesses. The proof comes from Quran [4:15] and [24:4], where the word 'four' explicitly specifies the number and that they must be men. The objection that Hanafis do not use mafhum al-mukhalafa is answered by ijma: the requirement of four is established by consensus. The apparent conflict with [2:282] which mentions two witnesses in debts is resolved by noting that the debt verse is permissive (mubiha) while the zina verse is prohibitive (man'ia), and prohibitive takes precedence.

Key Terms
أخذ (akhadha): To take, in the context of theft, it is used to mean 'took' without specifying the legality, as opposed to 'saraqa' which implies stealing with the required conditions for hadd.
قطع (qat'): Amputation of the hand as a hadd punishment for theft, under certain conditions.
ضمان (damam): Compensation, financial reparation for the taken property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school recommend saying 'he took' rather than 'he stole' in testimony regarding a theft?
A) Because saying 'he stole' is a sin.
B) To preserve concealment and allow the possibility of compensation instead of amputation.
C) Because 'he took' is the only permissible wording.
D) To conform with the opinion of the judge.

Key Takeaway
In theft testimony, saying 'took' is recommended because it preserves the possibility of compensation and avoids the irreconcilable conflict between amputation and compensation.
