The Word 'Ashhad' and Specification in Testimony
Stating the conditions of the witness's utterance and the need for specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two indispensable conditions for valid testimony in Hanafi fiqh and distinguish the relied-upon position from the Iraqi Hanafi view on women's testimony.

Core Idea
Testimony requires the explicit word 'Ashhad' and specification of the claim; without both, the testimony is invalid.

In this passage, the commentator explains the essential components of formal testimony. He clarifies that the witness must utter the specific word 'Ashhad' (I bear witness) and must clearly specify what they are testifying about. He also addresses a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school regarding whether women's testimony requires the same formulation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition
Locate where the passage states that the utterance of 'Ashhad' in the present tense is a rukn (integral) of testimony. Note that no other word suffices.
The author uses 'shart' loosely to include both rukn and shart.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute on women's testimony
Find the sentence that explains the disagreement with the Iraqi Hanafis. Understand their argument that women's statements are mere reports, and the rebuttal that testimony requires freedom and is given in the judge's court.
The relied-upon view is that 'Ashhad' is required for all.
3
Identify the second condition
Extract the requirement of specification (tafsir). The passage gives examples of ambiguous expressions that are rejected unless clarified.
The mufta bihi is that the witness must specify the claim, e.g., 'for this claimant against this defendant'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on ambiguous testimony
Distinguish between the position of al-Khassaf (rejects ambiguous 'like the testimony of my companion') and the majority (accepts if the witness can clarify). Understand the tarjih by al-Uzjandi.
The operative fatwa follows al-Uzjandi's conditional acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (للكل لفظ الشهادة والعدالة أي وشرط الجميع أنواعها لفظ (أشهد بالمضارع فلا يقوم غيره مقامه لما قدمناه أولها، وقدمنا أن لفظها ركن فالمراد بالشرط هنا ما لا بد منه ليشمل الركن والشرط، وقد أفاد أنه لا بد من لفظها في شهادة النساء أيضاً وهو المعتمد خلافاً للعراقيين لأنهم يجعلونها من باب الأخبار لا الشهادة والصحيح الأول لأنها شهادة يشترط لها الحرية في مجلس القاضي. ولا بد من شرط آخر لجميع أنواعها وهو التفسير حتى لو قال أشهد بمثل شهادته لا تقبل، ولو قال أشهد مثل شهادة صاحبي لا تقبل عند الخصاف، وعند عامة مشايخنا تقبل. وقيده الأوزجندي بما إذا قال لهذا المدعي على هذا المدعى عليه وبه يفتي؛ كذا في الخلاصة.
His statement: (For all, the utterance of testimony and integrity) i.e., the condition for all its types is the utterance of 'Ashhad' in the present tense, so nothing else takes its place due to what we presented at its beginning. And we presented that the utterance is an integral part (rukn), so what is meant by condition here is what is indispensable, to include the integral and the condition. And he has stated that there must be the utterance in the testimony of women as well, and that is the relied-upon position, contrary to the Iraqis because they make it from the category of reports (akhbar) not testimony, and the correct is the first because it is testimony for which freedom is required in the judge's court. And there must be another condition for all its types, which is specification (tafsir), so if he says 'I testify like his testimony' it is not accepted, and if he says 'I testify like the testimony of my companion' it is not accepted according to al-Khassaf, and according to the generality of our scholars it is accepted. And al-Uzjandi restricted it to when he says 'for this claimant against this defendant,' and with it fatwa is given; thus in al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage discusses two conditions for the performance of testimony. First, the witness must utter the word 'Ashhad' (I bear witness) in the present tense; no other word suffices. This is considered an integral (rukn) of testimony, and it applies to women's testimony as well, contrary to the Iraqi Hanafis who regarded women's statements as mere reports. The correct view is that women must also use 'Ashhad' because their testimony is subject to the condition of freedom in the judge's court. Second, the witness must specify (tafsir) what he is testifying to. If he says 'I testify like his testimony' (ambiguous) it is not accepted. If he says 'I testify like the testimony of my companion,' al-Khassaf rejects it, but most Hanafi scholars accept it, provided the witness clarifies the claim (e.g., 'for this claimant against this defendant'). This is the operative position for fatwa.

Key Terms
أشهد (Ashhad): The first-person present tense verb meaning 'I bear witness', considered the essential utterance (rukn) for formal testimony in court.
التفسير (al-tafsir): Specification in testimony: the witness must clarify the exact claim he is testifying to, e.g., 'for this claimant against this defendant'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because the word 'Ashhad' is present.
B) No, because it is ambiguous.
C) Yes, but only if the witness clarifies the claim (e.g., 'for this claimant against this defendant').
D) No, because it does not specify the claimant.

Key Takeaway
For valid testimony in Hanafi fiqh, the witness must say 'Ashhad' and must specify the claim; the mufta bihi requires specification even when using expressions like 'like the testimony of my companion'.

Women's Testimony in Apostasy Cases
Ruling on women's testimony for apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's testimony in apostasy cases and explain the rationale based on analogy to hudud and qisas.

Core Idea
Women's testimony is rejected in apostasy because the penalty can be execution, analogous to hudud and qisas.

The testimony of women is generally accepted in financial transactions but not in hudud or qisas. Why does apostasy fall under the same restriction? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that apostasy, if proven, can lead to execution, making it analogous to hudud and qisas, and thus women's testimony is rejected. However, an exception exists for a woman converting to Islam, where the testimony of one man and two women is accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State that women's testimony is not accepted in apostasy cases for a male defendant.
The passage explicitly rejects women's testimony for apostasy of a Muslim.
2
Understand the rationale
Recognize that the ruling is based on analogy to hudud and qisas because apostasy can lead to execution if the person persists.
Women's testimony is generally not accepted in hudud and qisas due to the severity of punishment.
3
Identify the exception
Note that for a woman converting to Islam, testimony of one man and two women is accepted.
This is from al-Bazzaziyyah: the ruling applies only to males when testifying about someone's Islam.
4
Apply the summary distinction
Distinguish between testifying about a male's Islam (reject women) and testifying about a female's Islam (accept women with a man).
The passage concludes with a clear summary of both cases.

This passage is a ruling on the acceptance of women's testimony regarding apostasy and conversion to Islam. The author presents the rule that women's testimony is not accepted in cases of apostasy (riddah) because apostasy, if proven, can lead to execution for a male who persists. This makes it analogous to hudud and qisas, where women's testimony is generally rejected. However, if a woman is converting to Islam, testimony of one man and two women is accepted. The summary clarifies: for a male being testified as Muslim (i.e., he was an apostate but now claims Islam?), women's testimony is not accepted, nor that of disbelievers. For apostasy of a Muslim, women's testimony is not accepted.

Key Terms
الردة (ar-riddah): Apostasy, leaving Islam.
التكفير (at-takfir): Declaring someone a disbeliever; here refers to expressions that constitute apostasy.

Requirement of Formal Testimony Wording and Interpretation
Ruling on lafz and tafsir in testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two essential requirements for the validity of testimony in Hanafi fiqh: the formal wording (lafz al-shahada) and explanation (tafsir), and identify the relied-upon position regarding their application.

Core Idea
Testimony requires the phrase 'I testify' and a specification of the claim; vague references are insufficient per the majority.

In Hanafi fiqh, testimony (shahada) is a weighty legal act with strict formalities. This lesson examines two critical conditions: the specific wording 'ashhadu' (I testify) and the necessity of explaining the subject matter. The passage presents the relied-upon Hanafi view and records disagreements among later scholars on how detailed the explanation must be.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that testimony is being ruled upon. The passage clarifies that the wording 'ashhadu' (present tense) is a pillar (rukn) of testimony, not merely a condition.
The author uses 'shart' loosely to include the pillar.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof for requiring lafz is not quoted here but referred to as 'what we presented at the beginning'. Understand that the requirement is based on earlier textual evidence (likely from the Quran and Sunnah).
The proof is implicitly accepted; this lesson focuses on applying the rule.
3
Apply the rule to women's testimony
Note that the same wording requirement applies to women, contrary to some Iraqi scholars who consider their statements as mere reports (akhbar). The relied-upon view treats it as testimony requiring lafz.
This is a cross-madhhab disagreement.
4
Understand the condition of tafsir
The second requirement is explanation: the witness must specify the claim or parties. Vague statements like 'I testify like his testimony' are generally rejected, especially by al-Khassaf. The majority accept if the witness adds 'for this plaintiff against this defendant'.
Al-Uzjandi's restriction is the mufta bihi.
5
Examine nuanced positions
Al-Halwani distinguishes between eloquent and non-Arab witnesses; al-Sarakhsi gives discretion to the judge if dishonesty is sensed. These show flexibility in applying the tafsir condition.
The fatwa is on al-Uzjandi's view for clarity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (للكل لفظ الشهادة والعدالة أي وشرط الجميع أنواعها لفظ (أشهد بالمضارع فلا يقوم غيره مقامه لما قدمناه أولها، وقدمنا أن لفظها ركن فالمراد بالشرط هنا ما لا بد منه ليشمل الركن والشرط، وقد أفاد أنه لا بد من لفظها في شهادة النساء أيضاً وهو المعتمد خلافاً للعراقيين لأنهم يجعلونها من باب الأخبار لا الشهادة والصحيح الأول لأنها شهادة يشترط لها الحرية في مجلس القاضي. ولا بد من شرط آخر لجميع أنواعها وهو التفسير حتى لو قال أشهد بمثل شهادته لا تقبل، ولو قال أشهد مثل شهادة صاحبي لا تقبل عند الخصاف، وعند عامة مشايخنا تقبل. وقيده الأوزجندي بما إذا قال لهذا المدعي على هذا المدعى عليه وبه يفتي؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وقال الحلواني : إن كان فصيحاً لا يقبل منه الإجمال وإن كان عجمياً يقبل بشرط أن يكون بحال إن استفسر بين. وقال السرخسي : إن أحس القاضي بخيانته كلفه التفسير وإلا لا. وفي البزازية وقال الحلواني لو أقر المدعي أو وكيله فقال الشاهد أشهد بما ادعاه هذا المدعي على هذا المدعى عليه أو قال المدعي في يده بغير حق يصح عندنا ا هـ.
His saying: 'For all, the wording of testimony and integrity.' That is, all its types require the wording 'I testify' in the present tense; nothing else takes its place due to what we presented at the beginning. We have stated that its wording is a pillar, so what is meant by 'condition' here is what is indispensable, to include the pillar and condition. He has conveyed that this wording is necessary for women's testimony as well, and that is the relied-upon position, contrary to the Iraqis because they consider it a matter of reporting (akhbar) not testimony. The correct is the first because it is testimony which requires freedom in the judge's court. And there is another condition for all its types: explanation (tafsir). So if he says 'I testify like his testimony' it is not accepted. If he says 'I testify like the testimony of my companion' it is not accepted according to al-Khassaf, but according to the general body of our scholars it is accepted. Al-Uzjandi restricted it to when he says 'for this plaintiff against this defendant' and that is what is given fatwa; thus in al-Khulasa. Al-Halwani said: if he is eloquent, his general statement is not accepted; if he is a non-Arab, it is accepted on condition that if asked he can explain. Al-Sarakhsi said: if the judge senses dishonesty, he requires explanation; otherwise no. In al-Bazzaziyyah, al-Halwani said: if the plaintiff or his agent admits, and the witness says 'I testify to what this plaintiff claimed against this defendant' or he said 'the plaintiff has in his hand without right', it is valid according to us.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the formal requirements for testimony. The author explains that the phrase 'I testify' (أشهد) in the present tense is necessary for all types of testimony, including women's testimony, contrary to the Iraqi scholars who view it as mere reporting. This wording is a pillar of testimony. Additionally, an explanation (tafsir) is required: the witness must specify what he is testifying about. Vague statements like 'I testify like his testimony' are not accepted by al-Khassaf, but most Hanafi scholars accept it if the witness specifies 'for this plaintiff against this defendant'. Different scholars have nuanced opinions: al-Halwani distinguishes between eloquent and non-Arab witnesses, while al-Sarakhsi gives discretion to the judge. The preferred opinion is that if the witness says 'I testify to what this plaintiff claimed', it suffices.

Key Terms
لفظ الشهادة (lafz ash-shahada): The specific phrase 'I testify' (ashhadu) in present tense, considered a pillar of testimony.
التفسير (at-tafsir): Explanation or specification of the subject matter of testimony, required for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is required for a witness's testimony to be accepted regarding the subject matter?
A) The witness must say 'I testify that I know the truth'
B) The witness must specify 'for this plaintiff against this defendant'
C) The witness must repeat the exact words of the plaintiff
D) No specification is needed; any general statement suffices

Key Takeaway
Hanafi fiqh requires both the formal wording 'ashhadu' and an explanation of the claim for testimony to be valid; vague testimony is rejected unless the judge exercises discretion.

Must a Judge Investigate Witnesses? Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Explains Hanafi positions on whether the judge must investigate witnesses' character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on witness investigation (tazkiya) and state the mufta bihi rule that the judge must inquire secretly and openly.

Core Idea
A judge must investigate witnesses secretly and openly; relying on apparent justice alone is sinful in our time.

This lesson delves into a classic dispute within the Hanafi school: must a judge always investigate the character of witnesses, or may he rely on their apparent justice? The answer affects the validity of court rulings. We explore the arguments of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and learn which view is relied upon in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the precise legal question being debated? Is it about the obligation of tazkiya or its effect on validity?
The dispute is about whether the judge must actively investigate witnesses (tazkiya) in all cases, not just when an objection is raised.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that a judge may rely on apparent justice unless the opposing party objects. His evidence includes the hadith 'People are just one to another except for one who has been flogged for slander' and the principle that outward conduct suffices.
Certainty is unattainable in most cases, so the apparent is sufficient.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require investigation secretly and openly in all rights, because the judiciary is based on evidence from just witnesses (shahadat al-udul).
They consider this a safeguard against invalid rulings.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa, a judgment without investigation is valid but the judge is sinful. Under the Sahibayn, the judgment is still valid but the judge is sinful if he fails to investigate. The difference is in obligation, not nullity.
Both agree that the ruling is not overturned even if witnesses later prove faulty.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its application
The later fatwa (al-Hidayah, al-Sirajiyya) follows the Sahibayn: investigation is wajib when the judge is ignorant of the witnesses' state. However, the judgment remains valid even if investigation is omitted, but the judge bears sin.
In times of widespread corruption, some judges resorted to administering oaths to witnesses as a practical alternative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات
الشهود سراً وعلناً في سائر الحقوق وتعديل الخصم لا يصح والواحد يكفي للتزكية
ولهذا قال في الهداية : لو قضى القاضي بشهادة الفاسق صح عندنا. زاد في فتح القدير : وكان القاضي عاصياً قال : وعن أبي يوسف أن الفاسق إذا كان وجيهاً في الناس كمباشري السلطان والمكسة وغيرهم تقبل شهادته لأنه لا يستأجر لشهادة الزور لوجاهته ويمتنع عن الكذب لمروءته والأول أصح لأن هذا تعليل لمقابلة النص فلا يقبل ا هـ. وفسر في العناية الوجيه بأن يكون ذا قدر وشرف، وفسر المروءة بالإنسانية قال : والهمزة وتشديد الواو فيهما لغتان ا هـ. وعلى هذا فما في القنية شارب الخمر يستحي ويرتدع إذا زجر فللقاضي أن يقبل شهادته إن كان ذا مروءة وتحرى في مقالته فوجده صادقاً ا.هـ. محمول على ما روي عن أبي يوسف .
قوله: (وسأل عن الشهود سراً وعلناً في سائر الحقوق أي وسأل القاضي عنهم في السر والعلانية وهو قول أبي يوسف ومحمد لأن القضاء مبني على الحجة وهي شهادة العدول فيتعرف عن العدالة، وفيه صون قضائه عن البطلان وقال أبو حنيفة : يقتصر الحاكم على ظاهر العدالة في المسلم ولا يسأل حتى يطعن الخصم لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «الناس عدول بعضهم على بعض إلا محدوداً في قذف ومثل ذلك عن عمر رضي الله عنه، ولأن الظاهر هو الانزجار عما هو محرم دينه وبالظاهر كفاية إذ لا وصول إلى القطع إلا في الحدود والقصاص فإنه يسأل عنهم للاحتيال في إسقاطها فيستقصي ولأن الشبهة فيها دارئة . والحاصل أنه إن طعن الخصم سأل عنهم في الكل وإلا سأل في الحدود والقصاص وفي غيرها محل الاختلاف وقيل هذا اختلاف عصر وزمان والفتوى على قولهما في هذا الزمان؛ في الهداية. ومحل السؤال على قولهما عند جهل القاضي بحالهم ولذا قال في الملتقط : القاضي إذا عرف الشهود بجرح أو عدالة لا يسأل اهـ. ولم يذكر المؤلف صفة السؤال وصرح في الهداية بأنه لا بد منه ولم يبين أنه شرط أو لا . وفي الملتقط قال أبو حنيفة : التزكية بدعة. وقال أبو يوسف : لو قضى القاضي بغير تزكية الشهود أجزأت ا فأفاد أن السؤال كذا عنهم ، هـ.
قوله : (لو قضى القاضي بشهادة الفاسق صح عندنا قال الرملي وفي جامع الفتاوى : وأما شهادة الفاسق فإن تحري القاضي الصدق في شهادته تقبل وإلا فلا قوله : (وقال أبو حنيفة يقتصر الحاكم على ظاهر العدالة) قال الرملي : أي يجوز له الاقتصار على سبيل الجواز لا الوجوب قوله : (ولا يسأل حتى يطعن الخصم) قال الرملي : ولو بالجرح المجرد ولا ينافيه قوله فيما يأتي ولا . يسمع القاضي الشهادة على جرح مجرد لأن عدم سماعها لعدم دخوله تحت الحكم وإلا فالخبر عن فسق الشهود يمنع القاضي عن قبول شهادتهم والحكم بها فالطعن به مسموع منه قبل التزكية وسيظهر من مسائل الطعن والله تعالى أعلم. قوله : (وقال أبو يوسف لو قضى القاضي بغير تزكية الشهود أجزأت) قال الرملي : عبارة القدوري وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد لا بد يسأل عنهم في السر والعلانية، ومقتضاه أن

عندنا
ليس بشرط صحة عندهما خصوصاً قدمنا عن الهداية أنه لو قضى بشهادة الفاسق يصح من غير حكاية خلاف فكيف إذا قضى بشهادة المستور فلو قضى ثم ظهر أن الشهود فسقة لم ينقض القضاء، وفي المحيط البرهاني من الحدود: لو قضى بالحد ببينه ثم ظهر أنهم فساق بعد ما رجم فإنه لا ضمان على القاضي لأنه لم يظهر الخطأ بيقين ا هـ . وهذا يدل على أن القاضي لو قضى في الحدود قبل السؤال بظاهر العدالة فإنه يصح وإن كان آثماً، فقوله في الهداية يشترط الاستقصاء معناه يجب، ومعنى قول الإمام يقتصر الحاكم يجوز اقتصاره لا أنه يجب اقتصاره. وفي التهذيب للقلانسي: وفي زماننا لما تعذرت التزكية بغلبة الفسق اختار القضاة كما اختار ابن أبي ليلى استحلاف الشهود لغلبة الظن ا هـ . قلت ولا يضعفه ما في الكتب المعتمدة كالخلاصة والبزازية من أنه لا يمين على الشاهد لأنه عند ظهور عدالته والكلام عند خفائها خصوصاً في زماننا أن الشاهد مجهول الحال، وكذا المزكي غالباً والمجهول لا يعرف المجهول. وفي | الملتقط محمد المروزي قال : قدمت الكوفة قاضياً عليها فوجدت فيها مائة وعشرين عدلاً فطلبت أسرارهم فرددتهم إلى ستة ثم أسقطت أربعة، فلما رأيت ذلك استعفيت واعتزلت قال الفقيه لو استقصى القاضي مثل ذلك لضاق الأمر ولا يوجد مؤمن بغير عيب كما قيل:
اهـ.

غسان بن
فلست بمستبق أخاً لا تلمه على شعث أي الرجال المهذب
وقال عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه : إن الله تعالى تولى منكم السرائر وذوى عنكم بالبينات ثم التزكية في السر أن يبعث المستورة إلى المعدل فيها النسب والحلي والمصلي ويردها المعدل كل ذلك في السر كي لا يظهر فيخدع أو يقصد. وفي الخانية : لا بد من أن يجمع بين المعدل والشاهد لتنتفي شبهة تعديل غيره وقد كانت العلانية وحدها في الصدر الأول ووقع الاكتفاء بالسر في زماننا تحرزاً عن الفتنة، ويروى عن محمد تزكية العلانية بلاء وفتنة ثم قيل: لا بد أن يقول المعدل هو عدل جائز الشهادة لأن العبد قد يعدل وقيل يكتفى بقوله هو لأن الحرية ثابتة بأصل الدار وهذا أصح كما في الهداية وفي السراجية : والفتوى على أنه
عدل
القاضي يأثم بترك السؤال ولا ينافيه إلا جزاء تأمل قوله : وفي التهذيب للقلانسي الخ) قال العلامة المقدسي بعد ذكر ما في التهذيب : لا يخفى أنه مخالف لما في الكتب المعتمدة، ولا يقال يجب العمل به لأن الشاهد مجهول كالمزكي غالباً والمجهول لا يعرف المجهول لأنا نقول الأمر كذلك لكن قال الفقيه : لو استقصى مثل ذلك لضاق الأمر ولا يوجد مؤمن بغير عيب كما قيل :
كفى المرء نبلاً أن تعد معايبه ذا الذي ترضی سجاياه كلها ومن نقله بعض الفضلاء.
قوله : (وفي السراجية والفتوى على أنه يسأل في السر) قال القهستاني : وعن محمد أن تزكية
Book of Testimonies. [Investigation of] witnesses secretly and openly in all rights, and the rectification of the opposing party is not valid, and one person is sufficient for tazkiya (character certification). For this reason, it is stated in al-Hidaya: If the judge passes judgment based on the testimony of a fasiq (sinner), it is valid according to us. In Fath al-Qadir, it adds: And the judge was disobedient. It said: And from Abu Yusuf that if the fasiq is influential among the people, like those managing the sultan's affairs and the tax collectors and others, his testimony is accepted because he would not hire himself to give false testimony due to his influence, and he refrains from lying due to his chivalry. The first opinion is more correct because this reasoning counters the textual evidence, so it is not accepted. End quote. In al-Inaya, 'al-wajih' is explained as having status and honor, and 'al-muru'a' as humanity. He said: The hamza and the doubled waw in both are two dialects. End quote. Based on this, what is in al-Quniya [regarding] a wine drinker who is ashamed and refrains when rebuked, the judge may accept his testimony if he has muru'a and investigates his speech and finds him truthful. End quote. It is interpreted according to what is transmitted from Abu Yusuf.
His statement: (And he asked about the witnesses secretly and openly in all rights) i.e., the judge asks about them in secret and in public, and this is the statement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad because the judiciary is based on evidence, which is the testimony of just persons, so he must ascertain justice, and in this is safeguarding his judgment from invalidity. Abu Hanifa said: The judge limits himself to the apparent justice of a Muslim and does not ask until the opposing party objects, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'People are just one to another except for one who has been flogged for slander', and similar [is transmitted] from Umar, may Allah be pleased with him. And because what is apparent is abstention from what is unlawful by one's religion, and the apparent is sufficient since there is no way to certainty except in hudud and qisas, for he asks about them out of caution to drop them, and he thoroughly investigates, and because doubts repel them. The conclusion is: if the opposing party objects, he asks about them in all cases; otherwise he asks in hudud and qisas, and in other cases it is subject to disagreement. And it is said this is a difference of era and time, and the fatwa is according to the two of them in this time; in al-Hidaya. The place of inquiry according to the two of them is when the judge is ignorant of their state. For this reason it is stated in al-Multaqat: The judge, if he knows the witnesses to be discredited or just, does not ask. End quote. The author did not mention the description of the inquiry, and it is explicitly stated in al-Hidaya that it is necessary, but he did not clarify whether it is a condition or not. In al-Multaqat: Abu Hanifa said: Tazkiya is an innovation. Abu Yusuf said: If the judge passes judgment without tazkiya of the witnesses, it suffices. So this indicates that the inquiry about them is [not a condition]... End quote.
His statement: (If the judge passes judgment based on the testimony of a fasiq, it is valid according to us) al-Ramli said: In Jami' al-Fatawa: As for the testimony of a fasiq, if the judge investigates truthfulness in his testimony, it is accepted; otherwise not. His statement: (Abu Hanifa said: The judge limits himself to apparent justice) al-Ramli said: i.e., it is permissible for him to limit himself in the sense of permissibility, not obligation. His statement: (And he does not ask until the opposing party objects) al-Ramli said: Even if by a mere accusation of dishonesty, and this does not contradict his following statement: 'the judge does not hear testimony about a mere accusation of dishonesty' because the non-hearing is because it does not fall under the ruling; otherwise, the information about the witnesses' sinfulness prevents the judge from accepting their testimony and judging by it, so objection is heard from him before tazkiya, and this will become clear from the issues of objection. Allah knows best. His statement: (Abu Yusuf said: If the judge passes judgment without tazkiya of the witnesses, it suffices) al-Ramli said: The text of al-Quduri: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He must ask about them in secret and in public. Its implication is that [according to us] it is not a condition of validity according to the two of them, especially since we have presented from al-Hidaya that if he passes judgment based on the testimony of a fasiq, it is valid without citing any disagreement, so what if he passes judgment based on the testimony of one whose character is unknown? So if he passes judgment and then it appears that the witnesses were sinners, the judgment is not overturned. In al-Muhit al-Burhani, from the section on hudud: If he passes judgment on a hadd punishment with evidence, then it appears that they were sinners after he was stoned, then there is no liability on the judge because the error has not been conclusively established. End quote. This indicates that if the judge passes judgment in hudud before inquiry based on apparent justice, it is valid even if he is sinful. So his statement in al-Hidaya that thorough investigation is required means it is obligatory, and the meaning of the Imam's statement 'the judge limits himself' is that his limiting himself is permissible, not that it is obligatory. In al-Tahdhib by al-Qalanisi: In our time, since tazkiya has become difficult due to the prevalence of sinfulness, the judges have chosen, as Ibn Abi Layla chose, to administer an oath to the witnesses due to the preponderance of probability. End quote. I [the author] say: This is not weakened by what is in the reliable books such as al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya that there is no oath upon the witness because that is when his justice is apparent, but the discussion is when it is hidden, especially in our time when the witness is of unknown state, and likewise the certifier often [is unknown], and the unknown cannot know the unknown. In al-Multaqat: Muhammad al-Marwazi said: I came to Kufa as a judge there, and I found one hundred and twenty just men, so I sought their hidden states and reduced them to six, then dropped four. When I saw that, I sought dismissal and withdrew. The jurist said: If the judge were to investigate like that, the matter would become difficult, and there is no believer without fault, as it has been said:
End quote. From Ghassan ibn [incomplete]
And I will not keep a brother whom you do not blame for some fault; how many men are faultless?
And Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, said: Indeed, Allah has taken charge of your inner secrets and shielded you through legal evidence. Then tazkiya in secret is that he sends the one whose character is being investigated to the certifier regarding lineage, appearance, and prayer, and the certifier returns it all in secret so that he does not become apparent and thus be deceived or targeted. In al-Khaniyya: It is necessary to bring together the certifier and the witness so as to remove the suspicion of certifying another. Open tazkiya alone was [done] in the early period, but reliance on secret tazkiya has occurred in our time to avoid discord. It is narrated from Muhammad that open tazkiya is a trial and tribulation. Then it is said: The certifier must say 'he is just, permissible of testimony' because a slave may be just; and it is said that his saying 'he is [just]' is sufficient because freedom is established by the original principle (dar al-Islam), and this is more correct as in al-Hidaya. In al-Sirajiyya: And the fatwa is that the judge is sinful by abandoning the inquiry, and nothing contradicts this except [careful consideration?]. End quote. Consider his statement: (In al-Tahdhib by al-Qalanisi etc.) al-Maqdisi said after mentioning what is in al-Tahdhib: It is not hidden that this contradicts what is in the reliable books, and it cannot be said that it must be acted upon because the witness is unknown like the certifier often, and the unknown cannot know the unknown; we say it is so, but the jurist said: If he were to investigate like that, the matter would become difficult and there is no believer without fault, as it has been said:
A man's nobility suffices that his faults are counted; He whose nature is entirely pleasing, and some scholars have transmitted this.
His statement: (In al-Sirajiyya: And the fatwa is that he asks in secret) al-Qahistani said: And from Muhammad that tazkiya [in secret]
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is from ‘Al-Bahr al-Ra’iq’, a commentary on ‘Kanz al-Daqa’iq’, discussing the ruling on whether a judge must investigate the character of witnesses (tazkiya) before accepting their testimony. The passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school between Imam Abu Hanifa on one side and his two disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) on the other. The author quotes several sources to explain each position.

The central issue is: should a judge ask about the witnesses’ integrity secretly and openly in all types of cases? According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the judge must ask about them both secretly and openly in all rights because judgment is based on evidence (ḥujja), which requires that witnesses be just (‘udul). The judge must ascertain their justice to safeguard his ruling from invalidity. However, Abu Hanifa holds that the judge may rely on the apparent justice of a Muslim and does not need to ask until the opposing party lodges an objection. Abu Hanifa’s evidence is the hadith: ‘People are just one to another except for one who has been flogged for slander.’ A similar report is from ‘Umar. The rationale is that the Muslim’s apparent conduct reflects religious restraint, and the outward is sufficient because certainty is unattainable except in hudud and qisas cases, where caution demands thorough investigation because punishments are warded off by doubts.

The author clarifies the application: if the opposing party objects, the judge must ask in all cases; if not, the judge asks only in hudud and qisas, and in other cases there is disagreement. Some scholars consider this a difference according to era; the fatwa in later times follows the Sahibayn’s view that inquiry is required. However, if the judge knows the witnesses’ state, he need not ask.

The passage also discusses the ruling if a judge accepts the testimony of a fasiq (sinner). According to al-Hidaya, the judgment is valid but the judge is sinful. There is a transmission from Abu Yusuf that if the fasiq is influential and possesses muru’a (chivalry/decency), his testimony may be accepted. But the preferred opinion rejects this as it contradicts the primary textual evidence.

Further, the text examines the necessity of tazkiya as a condition for judgment. Abu Yusuf reportedly said that if a judge rules without tazkiya, it is permissible (yujzi’). This indicates that tazkiya is not a condition of validity according to the Sahibayn, because even if the witnesses later prove to be sinners, the judgment is not overturned. The author quotes from al-Muhit al-Burhani that in hudud, if a penalty is executed and the witnesses are later found to be sinners, the judge incurs no liability.

The passage concludes with practical considerations for later times: when widespread sin makes tazkiya difficult, some judges adopted administering an oath to witnesses to strengthen probability. However, this contradicts reliable Hanafi works that state no oath is required of the witness when his justice is apparent; but when the witness is unknown, the matter is more complex. The secret method of tazkiya is described: the judge sends someone to the certifier (‘ādil) to inquire in confidence. In earlier times, open tazkiya sufficed, but later, secret tazkiya became the norm to avoid discord. The fatwa in al-Sirajiyya is that the judge is sinful if he abandons inquiry.

In summary, the passage teaches that while the ideal is to investigate witnesses, the Hanafi school provides flexibility: a judge may rely on apparent justice if no objection is raised, but in practice, especially in times of corruption, inquiry is necessary. The unity of the school is preserved: even if a judgment is based on a flawed testimony, it is not automatically overturned, but the judge bears responsibility.

Key Terms
تزكية (tazkiya): The process of investigating and certifying the integrity (justice) of a witness; character verification.
عدالة (adalā): Justice; the quality of being upright and trustworthy in testimony, avoiding major sins and minor sins vulgarly.
سراً وعلناً (sirran wa ‘alaniyatan): Secretly and publicly; refers to the manner of inquiry about witnesses: in private (sirran) and in open court (alaniyatan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa in the Hanafi school, what must a judge do regarding witnesses when their character is unknown?
A) He must ask about them only in hudud and qisas cases.
B) He must ask about them secretly and openly in all rights.
C) He may rely on their apparent justice without inquiry until an objection is raised.
D) He must administer an oath to the witnesses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the relied-upon position requires judges to investigate witnesses secretly and openly, but a judgment rendered without investigation is still valid, though the judge sins.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Istiqsa': Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on investigation of witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Imam Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on the obligation to investigate witnesses (istiqsa') and state the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
A judge's judgment is valid based on apparent justice, but whether he must investigate witnesses divides the founders.

This passage addresses a critical procedural question in Islamic court procedure: must a judge thoroughly investigate the moral character of witnesses before accepting their testimony, or may he rely on their apparent uprightness? The answer determines not only the validity of the judgment but also the judge's own sinfulness. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The passage clarifies that the judgment itself remains valid and is not overturned even if witnesses later turn out to be sinners, but the judge's obligation to investigate differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on judgment validity
First, note that the passage states a judgment based on testimony of a fasiq (sinner) or mastur (unknown) is valid and not overturned if later found sinful. This is the common ground between the positions.
This applies even to hudud cases, as shown in the example from al-Muhit al-Burhani.
2
Distinguish the two positions on istiqsa'
The Sahibayn hold that istiqsa' (thorough investigation) is obligatory (wajib). Imam Abu Hanifa holds it is permissible for the judge to limit himself to apparent justice; investigation is not obligatory.
The text clarifies: 'the meaning of the Imam's statement... is that his restriction is permissible, not that it is obligatory.'
3
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the judge does not investigate, according to Abu Hanifa the judgment is valid and the judge is not sinful. According to the Sahibayn, the judgment is still valid but the judge is sinful for omitting a wajib.
Later Hanafi fatwa prefers the Sahibayn's view due to the prevalence of corruption.
4
Analyze the case of hudud
The passage uses a hadd case to illustrate that even in severe punishments, if the witnesses later turn out sinful, the judge bears no liability because the error was not certain at the time of judgment.
This reinforces the validity of judgments based on apparent justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عندنا ليس بشرط صحة عندهما خصوصاً قدمنا عن الهداية أنه لو قضى بشهادة الفاسق يصح من غير حكاية خلاف فكيف إذا قضى بشهادة المستور فلو قضى ثم ظهر أن الشهود فسقة لم ينقض القضاء، وفي المحيط البرهاني من الحدود: لو قضى بالحد ببينه ثم ظهر أنهم فساق بعد ما رجم فإنه لا ضمان على القاضي لأنه لم يظهر الخطأ بيقين ا هـ . وهذا يدل على أن القاضي لو قضى في الحدود قبل السؤال بظاهر العدالة فإنه يصح وإن كان آثماً، فقوله في الهداية يشترط الاستقصاء معناه يجب، ومعنى قول الإمام يقتصر الحاكم يجوز اقتصاره لا أنه يجب اقتصاره.
According to us, it is not a condition of validity according to the two. Particularly we have previously reported from al-Hidayah that if he judged based on the testimony of a sinner, it is valid without any narration of dispute, so how about if he judged based on the testimony of an unknown? So if he judged and then it appeared that the witnesses were sinners, the judgment is not overturned. And in al-Muhit al-Burhani from the chapter of hudud: If he judged the hadd punishment with evidence and then it appeared that they were sinners after stoning, then there is no liability on the judge because the error has not become manifest with certainty. This indicates that if the judge judged in hudud before asking based on apparent justice, it is valid although he is sinful. So his statement in al-Hidayah that thorough investigation is required means it is obligatory, and the meaning of the Imam's statement that the judge restricts himself is that his restriction is permissible, not that it is obligatory.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the judge's obligation to investigate the moral character of witnesses. The text first establishes that a judgment based on testimony of a sinful person (fasiq) or an unknown person (mastur) is valid and not overturned even if the witnesses later become known as sinners. This is supported by a case from hudud where no liability falls on the judge if the witnesses turn out to be sinners after the punishment was carried out. The author then draws the conclusion that a judge may judge in hudud based on apparent justice (zahir al-adala) without prior inquiry, but he is sinful for doing so. This leads to the core dispute: what does 'istiqsa' (thorough investigation) mean? According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), investigation is obligatory (wajib). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the judge may limit himself to apparent justice; it is permissible for him to restrict his inquiry, not obligatory. The text clarifies that the statement in al-Hidayah requiring istiqsa' is to be understood as obligation, while the Imam's position is permissibility. The mufta bihi is not explicitly stated here, but the fact that the judge is described as sinful (athim) for not investigating aligns with the Sahibayn's view.

Key Terms
الاستقصاء (al-istiqsa'): Thorough investigation into the moral character of witnesses, including inquiring about their justice and background.
المستور (al-mastur): A witness whose moral status is unknown—neither clearly just nor clearly sinful.
العدالة (al-adala): Moral uprightness and trustworthiness required for a witness's testimony to be accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a judge passes a hadd punishment based on testimony from witnesses who are later discovered to be sinners?
A) The punishment is invalid and the judge is liable for compensation
B) The punishment is valid and the judge is not liable
C) The punishment is valid but must be rescinded
D) The punishment is invalid but the judge is not liable

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a judgment based on apparent justice is valid and not overturned even if witnesses are later found sinful; the judge's obligation to investigate (istiqsa') is disputed, with the mufta bihi being that it is wajib.

Secret Tazkiya and the Mastura Note
Describes the practice of secret tazkiya and the meaning of al-mastura.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the procedure of secret tazkiya, explain the term al-mastura, and apply the mu'addil's responses according to the Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
Secret tazkiya avoids fitna; the mastura note conceals the inquiry, and the mu'addil's response varies by the witness's known character.

In Hanafi fiqh, evaluating the character of witnesses (tazkiya) is essential for accepting testimony. This passage explains the shift from public to secret tazkiya, the use of a confidential note called al-mastura, and the specific wording the mu'addil (evaluator) should write based on his knowledge of the witness. Understanding this procedure is crucial for scholars and judges dealing with court testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the ruling on how tazkiya should be conducted according to the mufta bihi (relied-upon fatwa).
The fatwa is that the judge asks in secret.
2
Parse the definition of al-mastura
Understand the term al-mastura and its function as a sealed note sent secretly to the mu'addil.
It is called mastura because it is hidden from the public.
3
Understand the mu'addil's response categories
Learn what the mu'addil writes for different levels of knowledge about the witness: just, unknown (mastur), or fasiq.
The response varies to protect the witness's privacy and avoid fitna.
4
Note the ikhtilaf between public and secret tazkiya
Recognize that earlier practice allowed public tazkiya, but later fatwa favors secrecy to avoid fitna.
Imam Muhammad reported that public tazkiya is a tribulation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم التزكية في السر أن يبعث المستورة إلى المعدل فيها النسب والحلي والمصلي ويردها المعدل كل ذلك في السر كي لا يظهر فيخدع أو يقصد. وفي الخانية : لا بد من أن يجمع بين المعدل والشاهد لتنتفي شبهة تعديل غيره وقد كانت العلانية وحدها في الصدر الأول ووقع الاكتفاء بالسر في زماننا تحرزاً عن الفتنة، ويروى عن محمد تزكية العلانية بلاء وفتنة ثم قيل: لا بد أن يقول المعدل هو عدل جائز الشهادة لأن العبد قد يعدل وقيل يكتفى بقوله هو لأن الحرية ثابتة بأصل الدار وهذا أصح كما في الهداية وفي السراجية : والفتوى على أنه يسأل في السر قال القهستاني : وعن محمد أن تزكية يسأل في السر وقد تركت التزكية في العلانية في زماننا كي لا يخدع المزكي ولا يخون ا هـ . فقد علمت أن ما في المتن على خلاف المفتى به وهو الاقتصار على السر، ويدل عليه ما في الهداية أيضاً والمستورة اسم الرقعة التي يكتبها القاضي ويبعثها سراً بيد أمينه إلى المزكي سميت المستورة لأنها تستر عن نظر العوام كذا في النهاية فمن عرف الشاهد بالعدالة كتب تحت اسمه هو عدل جائز الشهادة، ومن لم يعرفه بشيء كتب هو مستور، ومن عرفه بالفسق لم يصرح بل يسكت احترازاً عن هتك الستر أو يكتب الله أعلم به إلا إذا عدله غيره وخاف أنه لو لم يصرح بذلك يقضي القاضي بشهادته فحينئذ يصرح بذلك؛ كذا في غاية البيان.
Then tazkiya in secret is that he sends the al-mastura (the sealed note) to the one who conducts tazkiya (al-mu'addil), containing the lineage, physical description, and behavior; and the mu'addil returns it, all in secret, so that it does not become apparent and he might be deceived or targeted. And in al-Khaniya: It is necessary to bring together the mu'addil and the witness to negate the suspicion of tazkiya by someone else. Public tazkiya alone was sufficient in the early period, but reliance on secret tazkiya occurred in our time to avoid fitna. It is reported from Muhammad that public tazkiya is a tribulation and fitna. Then it was said: The mu'addil must say 'he is just, admissible testimony' because a slave may be just. And it was said: it suffices to say 'he is' because freedom is established by the original rule of the abode, and this is more correct as in al-Hidayah. And in al-Sirajiyya: The fatwa is that he asks in secret. Al-Qahastani said: It is reported from Muhammad that tazkiya is asked about in secret, and public tazkiya has been abandoned in our time so that the mu'addil is not deceived or betraying. So you know that what is in the text (al-Matn) is contrary to the mufta bihi, which is confining to secret tazkiya, and al-Hidayah also indicates that. Al-Mastura is the name of the note that the judge writes and sends secretly via his trustee to the mu'addil. It is called al-mastura because it is hidden from the view of the common people, as in al-Nihaya. The one who knows the witness to be just writes under his name: 'He is just, admissible testimony.' The one who does not know anything about him writes: 'He is mastur.' The one who knows him to be a fasiq does not declare openly but remains silent to avoid tearing the veil, or writes: 'Allah knows best about him,' except if someone else has declared him just and he fears that if he does not declare, the judge will rule on his testimony, then he declares; as in Ghayat al-Bayan.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage defines the method of secret tazkiya (investigation of witnesses' character) and the technical term 'al-mastura' (the sealed note). The author explains that the judge sends a secret note to a reliable person (mu'addil) containing details about the witness's lineage, physical description, and behavior. The mu'addil returns it confidentially to avoid public exposure leading to deception or harm. According to al-Khaniya, it is necessary to bring together the mu'addil and the witness to prevent suspicion of someone else's endorsement. In early Islam, public tazkiya sufficed, but in later times, secret tazkiya became the practice to avoid fitna. It is reported from Imam Muhammad that public tazkiya is a tribulation. There is a discussion about the wording of the mu'addil: must he explicitly say 'he is just, admissible testimony' or is it sufficient to say 'he is'? The more correct view is that the word 'is' suffices because freedom is presumed in the abode of Islam. The fatwa in al-Sirajiyya is that the judge asks in secret. Al-Qahastani quotes Muhammad that tazkiya is done in secret, and public tazkiya has been abandoned to avoid deceiving the mu'addil or him being treacherous. Thus, the author concludes that the text of the matn (which likely mentioned public tazkiya) is contrary to the mufta bihi, which is exclusive reliance on secret tazkiya. The term 'al-mastura' is then defined: it is the note the judge writes secretly to the mu'addil. The mu'addil writes specific responses: if he knows the witness is just, he writes 'He is just, admissible testimony'; if unknown, he writes 'He is mastur'; if he knows he is a sinner, he remains silent or writes 'Allah knows best,' unless someone else has declared him just and he fears the judge will accept his testimony, then he must disclose.

Key Terms
المستورة (al-mastura): A secret note sent by the judge to the tazkiya evaluator, containing the witness's details and requesting assessment of his character.
التزكية في السر (al-tazkiya fi al-sirr): The process of evaluating a witness's justice in secret, as opposed to public tazkiya.
المعدل (al-mu'addil): The person entrusted with evaluating the witness's character; he returns the sealed note with his assessment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He is just
C) He remains silent or writes 'Allah knows best'

Key Takeaway
Secret tazkiya via the mastura note is the Hanafi fatwa to protect the process from fitna, and the mu'addil's responses are tailored to the witness's known character.

The Judge's Inquiry: Asking about 'Adala, Not Freedom or Islam
Ruling on the scope of judicial inquiry into witness qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the judge's inquiry about witnesses is limited to justice ('adala) unless freedom or Islam is disputed.

Core Idea
The judge asks only about 'adala; freedom and Islam are presumed unless challenged.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a key procedural rule in Hanafi testimony law. While a witness's 'adala is always investigated, his freedom and Islam are taken as given unless the opposing party raises a valid objection. This distinction stems from the nature of these attributes: 'adala is a matter of moral character not subject to litigation, whereas freedom and slavery are rights between people that require proof only when contested.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge's questioning of witnesses. The ruling is that asking about 'adala is obligatory (wajib); asking about freedom and Islam is only required if the opponent disputes them.
This is derived from the text's statement: 'he does not ask about freedom and Islam unless the opponent disputes it.'
2
Locate the dalil
The text references al-Jami' and al-Quduri. Al-Jami' states that in cases of testimony, hudud, qisas, and 'aql, apparent freedom is not sufficient; the judge must ask. However, this is interpreted as conditional on the opponent's challenge, as al-Quduri restricted it.
The author uses this to reconcile apparent conflict between the general rule and the specific exceptions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The distinction is based on whether the attribute is subject to litigation (huquq al-ibad). Freedom and slavery are rights that can be contested in court, so they require proof only when disputed. 'Adala is a religious condition not litigiable, so it is established by inquiry.
This is from al-Mabsut: 'as for justice, litigation does not occur in it, so it can be known by asking about his condition.'
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some later Hanafi texts may consider asking about freedom obligatory in all cases. The author here follows al-Quduri's restriction, which limits the inquiry to when the opponent challenges.
The intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is resolved by preferring the restriction, as per al-Ramli and the author.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that asking about 'adala is wajib, and asking about freedom/Islam is only wajib if disputed. This is supported by al-Quduri's restriction and the reasoning that freedom is a right of people.
Al-Ramli confirms that the negation of asking about freedom is limited to when there is no challenge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأراد بقوله ويسأل عن الشهود أي عن عدالتهم على حذف مضاف وإنما قدرناه لأنه لا يسأل عن حرية الشاهد وإسلامه ما لم ينازعه الخصم وما ذكره في الجامع من أن الناس أحرار إلا في الشهادة والحدود والقصاص والعقل فإنه لا يكتفي بظاهر الحرية في هذه المواضع بل يسأل محمول على ما إذا طعن الخصم بالرق كما قيده القدوري رحمه الله؛ كذا ذكر الشارح وثبوت حرية الشاهد إما بإقامة البينة عليها أو بالإخبار للقاضي كالعدالة والأول أحب وأحسن لأن الأهلية للشهادة لا تثبت إلا بالحرية وتثبت بدون العدالة، ولأن الحرية والرق من حقوق العباد تجري فيها الخصومة وطريق الإثبات في مثلها للبيئة، فأما العدالة فلا تجري فيها الخصومة فيمكن معرفتها بالسؤال عن حاله ؛ كذا في المبسوط . وفي القنية : قال المدعى عليه في الشاهد إنه كافر بالله تعالى فللقاضي أن يسأله عن الإيمان إن اتهمه بذلك وإن كان يشهد بوحدانية الله تعالى ورسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم تقبل شهادته، وكذا لو قال أنا مسلم ولست بكافر، ولو سأله الحاكم فذكر في خلال سؤاله ما لا يجوز على الله للتجربة فهذا جهل من القاضي وحمق وقد أساء فيما فعل، ولو جوز هذا كان وبالاً على جميع المسلمين خصوصاً في قضاة أهل الرساتيق فلو أنه تحمق وفعل لا يقبل شهادته ا هـ . وأطلق في السؤال عن الشهود فشمل المسلم والكافر فيسأل عن النصراني إذا شهد على مثله . وفي فتاوى عمر قارئ الهداية تزكية الذمي أن يزكيه بالأمانة في دينه ولسانه ويده وأنه صاحب يقظة ا هـ . وقد أخذه فتاوى الولوالجي. وفي الملتقط : نصراني عدل ثم أسلم قبلت شهادته ا هـ. وفيه : إذا سكر الذمي لا تقبل شهادته ا هـ . وشمل السؤال عنه إذا شهد حين بلغ وهو ظاهر الخانية. وفي الملتقط : احتلم لا أقبل شهادته ما لم أسأل عنه ولا بد من صبي العلانية بلاء وفتنة. وتزكية السر أحدثها شريح وعليه الفتوى كما في المضمرات وغيره. ويشكل ما في الاختيار أنه يسئل سراً وعلانية وعليه الفتوى اهـ قلت يمكن إرجاعه إلى قوله يسأل أي لا يكتفي بالعدالة الظاهرة فهو ترجيح لقولهما تأمل قوله : (وإنما قدرناه لأنه لا يسأل عن حرية الشاهد وإسلامه الخ) قال الرملي : قدمنا أن سؤاله عن العدالة على سبيل الوجوب فنفي سؤاله عن الحرية
And he meant by his statement 'and he asks about the witnesses' i.e., about their justice, by omission of a genitive. And we only interpreted it thus because he does not ask about the witness's freedom and Islam unless the opponent disputes it. And what is mentioned in al-Jami' that people are free except in testimony, hudud, qisas, and aql, then apparent freedom is not sufficient in these matters, rather he asks, is interpreted as when the opponent challenges slavery, as al-Quduri restricted it. Thus the commentator mentioned. And the establishment of the witness's freedom is either by providing evidence on it or by informing the judge like justice, and the first is more beloved and better, because eligibility for testimony is only established by freedom and is established without justice, and because freedom and slavery are among the rights of people in which litigation occurs, and the method of proof in such matters is evidence; as for justice, litigation does not occur in it, so it can be known by asking about his condition; as in al-Mabsut. And in al-Quniyya: If the defendant says about the witness that he disbelieves in Allah, then the judge may ask him about faith if he accuses him of that, and if he testifies to the oneness of Allah and the message of Muhammad (PBUH), his testimony is accepted. Similarly, if he says 'I am a Muslim and not a disbeliever'. If the judge asks him and during his questioning he mentions what is not permissible concerning Allah by way of experimentation, this is ignorance and stupidity of the judge, and he has done wrong. If this is permitted, it would be a calamity for all Muslims, especially among the judges of the rural areas. So if he acts foolishly and does so, his testimony is not accepted. And he made the questioning about witnesses general, including Muslim and non-Muslim, so he asks about the Christian if he testifies regarding his like. And in the fatwas of Umar Qari' al-Hidaya: Tazkiya of a dhimmi is that he evaluates him based on trustworthiness in his religion, speech, and hand, and that he is vigilant. And it is taken from Fatawa al-Walwaliji. And in al-Multaqat: A Christian who is just then converts to Islam, his testimony is accepted. And in it: If a dhimmi becomes intoxicated, his testimony is not accepted. And the questioning about him applies if he testifies when he reaches puberty, and this is apparent in al-Khaniya. And in al-Multaqat: A boy who has had a wet dream, I do not accept his testimony until I ask about him, and there must be a boy's public [tazkiya] is a trial and fitna. And secret tazkiya was initiated by Shuraih, and the fatwa is on it as in al-Mudmarat and others. And what is in al-Ikhtiyar, that he asks secretly and publicly and the fatwa is on it, is problematic. I say: it can be referred to his statement 'he asks' i.e., he does not suffice with apparent justice, so it is a preference for the view of the two [Sahibayn]. Consider his statement: (And we only interpreted it because he does not ask about the witness's freedom and Islam, etc.) Al-Ramli said: We have established that his questioning about justice is on the way of obligation, so the negation of his questioning about freedom [means...]
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage addresses the scope of the judge's inquiry about witnesses. The author explains that when the text says 'the judge asks about the witnesses,' it means he asks about their justice ('adala), not about their freedom or Islam, because the latter are only inquired into if the opposing party disputes them. However, in certain cases like testimony, hudud, qisas, and 'aql, al-Jami' states that apparent freedom is not sufficient; the judge must ask. But this is interpreted as applying when the opponent challenges the witness's freedom, as al-Quduri restricted. The passage then discusses the method of establishing freedom: either by evidence or by informing the judge, similar to justice, but evidence is preferred because freedom is a right of people subject to litigation. Then it addresses cases where the witness is accused of disbelief: if the defendant claims the witness is a disbeliever, the judge may question him about faith. If he testifies to the oneness of Allah and prophethood, his testimony is accepted. But if the judge engages in inappropriate questioning, it is foolish. The ruling covers Muslim and non-Muslim witnesses: a Christian may testify regarding another Christian. There are specific rules for tazkiya of a dhimmi: evaluating his trustworthiness in his religion, speech, and actions. A just Christian who later converts to Islam has his testimony accepted. A dhimmi who becomes intoxicated has his testimony rejected. The passage also mentions that secret tazkiya was initiated by Shuraih and is the fatwa, although al-Ikhtiyar mentions both secret and public. The author resolves this by interpreting 'he asks' as not being content with apparent justice, thus favoring the view of the two Sahibayn. The final note from al-Ramli confirms that questioning about justice is obligatory, but not about freedom.

Key Terms
العدالة (al-adala): Moral uprightness of a witness; the judge is obligated to ask about it.
الحرية (al-hurriyya): Freedom from slavery; a condition for testimony according to Hanafis, but only inquired into if disputed.
الإيمان (al-iman): Faith in Islam; the judge may ask about it if the witness is accused of disbelief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The judge's prima facie duty is to investigate 'adala; freedom and Islam are presumed unless put in issue by the opposing party.

Testimony of Non-Muslims and Tazkiya of Dhimmis
Rulings on non-Muslim witnesses and tazkiya of dhimmis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi rulings on the testimony of non-Muslims and the method of tazkiya for dhimmis.

Core Idea
A non-Muslim witness may testify against another non-Muslim, but his credibility depends on his trustworthiness in his own religion.

This passage extends the discussion of witness qualifications to non-Muslims. It clarifies that a Christian (or dhimmi) can testify in cases involving another dhimmi, and his tazkiya (validation) assesses his trustworthiness according to his religion's standards. The passage also addresses special cases: a just dhimmi who later converts to Islam retains his testimony, while an intoxicated dhimmi's testimony is rejected. Additionally, the rule of secret tazkiya (initiated by Shuraih) is affirmed as the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on non-Muslim witnesses
The text states that questioning about witnesses is general and includes Muslims and non-Muslims. Specifically, a Christian can testify against another Christian (or dhimmi). The rule is: testimony between dhimmis is accepted if they are of the same religion.
The term 'non-Muslim' here refers to dhimmis (protected non-Muslims).
2
Determine the method of tazkiya for a dhimmi
Tazkiya (validation) of a dhimmi is based on his trustworthiness in his religion, speech, and actions. This means evaluating his honesty and moral conduct according to the standards of his own faith, not Islamic standards.
This is from Fatawa Umar Qari' al-Hidaya and Fatawa al-Walwaliji.
3
Note the effects of change of status
If a Christian who was just (adl) in his religion converts to Islam, his testimony is accepted. Also, if a dhimmi becomes intoxicated, his testimony is rejected.
These rulings show that the witness's state at the time of testimony matters, and justice is tied to religious adherence.
4
Understand the rule on secret tazkiya
Secret tazkiya (private inquiry) was initiated by the famous judge Shuraih and is the operative fatwa according to al-Mudmarat and other works. This means the judge may investigate witnesses discreetly, not necessarily in open court.
Al-Ikhtiyar mentions both secret and public, but the author resolves it by interpreting 'he asks' as not being content with apparent justice, thus favoring the view of the two Sahibayn.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
In a modern court with non-Muslim citizens, the Hanafi rule would require the judge to assess the witness's credibility based on his or her own community standards, not Islamic ones, for cases between non-Muslims.
This maintains consistency with the principle of 'sovereignty of the dhimmi in his own matters.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأراد بقوله ويسأل عن الشهود أي عن عدالتهم على حذف مضاف وإنما قدرناه لأنه لا يسأل عن حرية الشاهد وإسلامه ما لم ينازعه الخصم وما ذكره في الجامع من أن الناس أحرار إلا في الشهادة والحدود والقصاص والعقل فإنه لا يكتفي بظاهر الحرية في هذه المواضع بل يسأل محمول على ما إذا طعن الخصم بالرق كما قيده القدوري رحمه الله؛ كذا ذكر الشارح وثبوت حرية الشاهد إما بإقامة البينة عليها أو بالإخبار للقاضي كالعدالة والأول أحب وأحسن لأن الأهلية للشهادة لا تثبت إلا بالحرية وتثبت بدون العدالة، ولأن الحرية والرق من حقوق العباد تجري فيها الخصومة وطريق الإثبات في مثلها للبيئة، فأما العدالة فلا تجري فيها الخصومة فيمكن معرفتها بالسؤال عن حاله ؛ كذا في المبسوط . وفي القنية : قال المدعى عليه في الشاهد إنه كافر بالله تعالى فللقاضي أن يسأله عن الإيمان إن اتهمه بذلك وإن كان يشهد بوحدانية الله تعالى ورسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم تقبل شهادته، وكذا لو قال أنا مسلم ولست بكافر، ولو سأله الحاكم فذكر في خلال سؤاله ما لا يجوز على الله للتجربة فهذا جهل من القاضي وحمق وقد أساء فيما فعل، ولو جوز هذا كان وبالاً على جميع المسلمين خصوصاً في قضاة أهل الرساتيق فلو أنه تحمق وفعل لا يقبل شهادته ا هـ . وأطلق في السؤال عن الشهود فشمل المسلم والكافر فيسأل عن النصراني إذا شهد على مثله . وفي فتاوى عمر قارئ الهداية تزكية الذمي أن يزكيه بالأمانة في دينه ولسانه ويده وأنه صاحب يقظة ا هـ . وقد أخذه فتاوى الولوالجي. وفي الملتقط : نصراني عدل ثم أسلم قبلت شهادته ا هـ. وفيه : إذا سكر الذمي لا تقبل شهادته ا هـ . وشمل السؤال عنه إذا شهد حين بلغ وهو ظاهر الخانية. وفي الملتقط : احتلم لا أقبل شهادته ما لم أسأل عنه ولا بد من صبي العلانية بلاء وفتنة. وتزكية السر أحدثها شريح وعليه الفتوى كما في المضمرات وغيره. ويشكل ما في الاختيار أنه يسئل سراً وعلانية وعليه الفتوى اهـ قلت يمكن إرجاعه إلى قوله يسأل أي لا يكتفي بالعدالة الظاهرة فهو ترجيح لقولهما تأمل قوله : (وإنما قدرناه لأنه لا يسأل عن حرية الشاهد وإسلامه الخ) قال الرملي : قدمنا أن سؤاله عن العدالة على سبيل الوجوب فنفي سؤاله عن الحرية
And he meant by his statement 'and he asks about the witnesses' i.e., about their justice, by omission of a genitive. And we only interpreted it thus because he does not ask about the witness's freedom and Islam unless the opponent disputes it. And what is mentioned in al-Jami' that people are free except in testimony, hudud, qisas, and aql, then apparent freedom is not sufficient in these matters, rather he asks, is interpreted as when the opponent challenges slavery, as al-Quduri restricted it. Thus the commentator mentioned. And the establishment of the witness's freedom is either by providing evidence on it or by informing the judge like justice, and the first is more beloved and better, because eligibility for testimony is only established by freedom and is established without justice, and because freedom and slavery are among the rights of people in which litigation occurs, and the method of proof in such matters is evidence; as for justice, litigation does not occur in it, so it can be known by asking about his condition; as in al-Mabsut. And in al-Quniyya: If the defendant says about the witness that he disbelieves in Allah, then the judge may ask him about faith if he accuses him of that, and if he testifies to the oneness of Allah and the message of Muhammad (PBUH), his testimony is accepted. Similarly, if he says 'I am a Muslim and not a disbeliever'. If the judge asks him and during his questioning he mentions what is not permissible concerning Allah by way of experimentation, this is ignorance and stupidity of the judge, and he has done wrong. If this is permitted, it would be a calamity for all Muslims, especially among the judges of the rural areas. So if he acts foolishly and does so, his testimony is not accepted. And he made the questioning about witnesses general, including Muslim and non-Muslim, so he asks about the Christian if he testifies regarding his like. And in the fatwas of Umar Qari' al-Hidaya: Tazkiya of a dhimmi is that he evaluates him based on trustworthiness in his religion, speech, and hand, and that he is vigilant. And it is taken from Fatawa al-Walwaliji. And in al-Multaqat: A Christian who is just then converts to Islam, his testimony is accepted. And in it: If a dhimmi becomes intoxicated, his testimony is not accepted. And the questioning about him applies if he testifies when he reaches puberty, and this is apparent in al-Khaniya. And in al-Multaqat: A boy who has had a wet dream, I do not accept his testimony until I ask about him, and there must be a boy's public [tazkiya] is a trial and fitna. And secret tazkiya was initiated by Shuraih, and the fatwa is on it as in al-Mudmarat and others. And what is in al-Ikhtiyar, that he asks secretly and publicly and the fatwa is on it, is problematic. I say: it can be referred to his statement 'he asks' i.e., he does not suffice with apparent justice, so it is a preference for the view of the two [Sahibayn]. Consider his statement: (And we only interpreted it because he does not ask about the witness's freedom and Islam, etc.) Al-Ramli said: We have established that his questioning about justice is on the way of obligation, so the negation of his questioning about freedom [means...]
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage addresses the scope of the judge's inquiry about witnesses. The author explains that when the text says 'the judge asks about the witnesses,' it means he asks about their justice ('adala), not about their freedom or Islam, because the latter are only inquired into if the opposing party disputes them. However, in certain cases like testimony, hudud, qisas, and 'aql, al-Jami' states that apparent freedom is not sufficient; the judge must ask. But this is interpreted as applying when the opponent challenges the witness's freedom, as al-Quduri restricted. The passage then discusses the method of establishing freedom: either by evidence or by informing the judge, similar to justice, but evidence is preferred because freedom is a right of people subject to litigation. Then it addresses cases where the witness is accused of disbelief: if the defendant claims the witness is a disbeliever, the judge may question him about faith. If he testifies to the oneness of Allah and prophethood, his testimony is accepted. But if the judge engages in inappropriate questioning, it is foolish. The ruling covers Muslim and non-Muslim witnesses: a Christian may testify regarding another Christian. There are specific rules for tazkiya of a dhimmi: evaluating his trustworthiness in his religion, speech, and actions. A just Christian who later converts to Islam has his testimony accepted. A dhimmi who becomes intoxicated has his testimony rejected. The passage also mentions that secret tazkiya was initiated by Shuraih and is the fatwa, although al-Ikhtiyar mentions both secret and public. The author resolves this by interpreting 'he asks' as not being content with apparent justice, thus favoring the view of the two Sahibayn. The final note from al-Ramli confirms that questioning about justice is obligatory, but not about freedom.

Key Terms
الذمي (al-dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under the protection of an Islamic state, whose testimony is accepted in cases involving his coreligionists.
التزكية السر (al-tazkiya al-sirr): Secret tazkiya: private inquiry into a witness's character, initiated by Judge Shuraih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) By requiring him to convert to Islam first
D) By public questioning in court only

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's testimony is valid between dhimmis, and his credibility is assessed by his own religious and ethical standards, not Islamic ones.

Secret Tazkiya and the Mastura Document
Explaining the ruling on secret tazkiya and the conventions of the mastura document

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on secret tazkiya and apply the conventions for writing in the mastura document.

Core Idea
Secret tazkiya is the operative fatwa; the mastura protects both the verifier and the witness.

In Hanafi fiqh, verifying a witness's integrity (tazkiya) is a critical step before accepting testimony. While early texts may imply open inquiry, later Hanafi practice settled on secret investigation to prevent manipulation and harm. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the relied-upon ruling and explains the conventions of the mastura—the secret document used by the judge. Understanding this procedure ensures that justice is served without compromising reputations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling: secret vs open tazkiya
The passage states that the mufta bihi is secret inquiry (يسأل في السر), contrary to what the matn might imply. Understand that this is the operative practice.
The rationale is to protect the verifier from deception and the witness from betrayal.
2
Define the mastura and its purpose
The mastura is the secret document sent by the judge to the verifier. It is hidden from public view to maintain confidentiality.
The term 'mastura' literally means 'covered'.
3
Distinguish the three categories of witnesses
For a witness known to be just, write 'he is just, his testimony is admissible'. For an unknown witness, write 'he is mastur'. For a known sinner, remain silent or write 'Allah knows best', unless there is a risk of the judge accepting his testimony based on silence.
The verifier must avoid exposing the sinner's fault unless necessary.
4
Recognize the exception for explicit declaration
If another person has declared the witness just and the verifier fears that his silence will lead the judge to accept the testimony, then he must explicitly state the witness's unfitness.
This balances between protecting privacy and ensuring justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يسأل في السر وقد تركت التزكية في العلانية في زماننا كي لا يخدع المزكي ولا يخون ا هـ . فقد علمت أن ما في المتن على خلاف المفتى به وهو الاقتصار على السر، ويدل عليه ما في الهداية أيضاً والمستورة اسم الرقعة التي يكتبها القاضي ويبعثها سراً بيد أمينه إلى المزكي سميت المستورة لأنها تستر عن نظر العوام كذا في النهاية فمن عرف الشاهد بالعدالة كتب تحت اسمه هو عدل جائز الشهادة، ومن لم يعرفه بشيء كتب هو مستور، ومن عرف رفه بالفسق لم يصرح بل يسكت احترازاً عن هتك الستر أو يكتب الله أعلم به» إلا إذا عدله غيره وخاف أنه لو لم يصرح بذلك يقضي القاضي بشهادته فحينئذ يصرح بذلك؛ كذا في غاية البيان.
He asks in secret, and open tazkiya has been abandoned in our time to prevent the verifier from being deceived or betraying. So you know that what is in the Matn is contrary to the relied-upon fatwa, which is restricting to secret inquiry. And there is evidence for it in al-Hidayah as well. Al-Mastura is the name of the document that the judge writes and sends secretly with his trustee to the verifier. It is called mastura because it is hidden from the sight of the common people. So: whoever knows the witness to be just writes under his name: 'He is just, his testimony is admissible.' Whoever does not know anything about him writes: 'He is unknown (mastur).' Whoever knows clearly that he is a sinner does not state explicitly but remains silent to avoid exposing him, or writes: 'Allah knows best about him.' Except if someone else has declared him just and he fears that if he does not state it, the judge will rule based on his testimony, then he states it explicitly. From Ghayat al-Bayan.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical issue in the court system: how should the judge verify the integrity (tazkiya) of witnesses? The text states that the current practice (in the author's time) is to do so secretly, not openly, to protect both the verifier and the witness from manipulation. This is contrary to what the Matn (the base text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) might imply, but the commentator clarifies that the fatwa is upon restricting to secret inquiry. He then explains the mastura, a secret document sent to the verifier. The judge writes specific phrases: for a known just witness, he writes 'he is just, his testimony is admissible'; for an unknown witness, he writes 'he is mastur' (meaning his condition is hidden); for a known sinful witness, he avoids direct slander and either remains silent or writes 'Allah knows best'. However, if there is a risk that the judge might admit the witness's testimony based on silence, the verifier must then explicitly declare his unfitness. This shows the care taken to balance justice and avoiding harm to reputation.

Key Terms
المستورة (al-mastūrah): The secret document that the judge sends to the verifier to gather information about a witness's integrity, hidden from the public.
التزكية (al-tazkiyah): The process of verifying the integrity ('adalah) of a witness.
عدل (ʿadl): A witness who is just, possessing moral integrity (not a fasiq), and thus his testimony is admissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should the judge write about a witness whose integrity is known to be good?
A) He writes 'he is mastur'.
B) He remains silent.
C) He writes 'he is just, his testimony is admissible'.
D) He writes 'Allah knows best about him'.

Key Takeaway
Secret tazkiya using the mastura is the Hanafi mufta bihi, and verifiers must carefully phrase their responses to balance justice and privacy.
