Scope of Inquiry: When Must the Judge Ask About Witness's Freedom?
Clarifying the scope of judicial inquiry into witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the judge's duty to investigate 'adala and the presumption of freedom and Islam, and apply the rule that the judge only questions freedom or Islam when contested.

Core Idea
The judge asks about 'adala by default; freedom and Islam are presumed until challenged.

In the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, Ibn Nujaym clarifies a critical procedural point: the matn's instruction 'and he asks about the witnesses' does not mean the judge must verify every condition of witness eligibility. Rather, the inquiry is specifically about 'adala (moral integrity). Freedom and Islam are presumed, and the judge only investigates them if the opposing party raises the issue. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its practical implications for court procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object of the judge's inquiry
The matn says 'and he asks about the witnesses.' The commentator explains that this means asking about their 'adala, not about freedom or Islam. Understand that 'adala is the default subject of investigation.
The Arabic uses حذف مضاف – a deleted genitive construction – so 'an al-shuhud' actually means 'an 'adala al-shuhud'.
2
Recognize the default presumptions
People are presumed free (asl al-ḥurriyya) and presumed Muslim (asl al-Islam) in Hanafi law. Therefore, the judge does not need to ask about these unless the opponent contest them.
This presumption applies in most legal contexts; exceptions exist for specific serious matters.
3
Note the exceptions and their trigger
In testimony, hudud, qisas, and 'aql, the presumption of freedom is weaker – but even then, the judge only asks if the opponent specifically alleges slavery. The text from al-Jami' is qualified by al-Quduri's condition.
The trigger is ‘if the opponent alleges slavery’ (إذا طعن الخصم بالرق).
4
Understand the method of establishing freedom vs. 'adala
Freedom is established by evidence (bayyinah) or by the judge's own information, like 'adala. However, the preferred method is evidence because freedom involves litigation (khūṣūma) between parties. 'Adala is not litigated, so it can be known by asking about the witness's condition.
This distinction explains why evidence is more beloved (أحب وأحسن) for freedom.
5
Apply the rule
In practice: when a witness appears, the judge verifies 'adala through inquiry (e.g., reputation). The judge does not ask 'Are you free?' or 'Are you Muslim?' unless the opposing party has raised a specific challenge. If challenged, the judge requires proof of freedom and/or Islam.
This preserves the presumption while allowing due process for challenges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأراد بقوله ويسأل عن الشهود أي عن عدالتهم على حذف مضاف وإنما قدرناه لأنه لا يسأل عن حرية الشاهد وإسلامه ما لم ينازعه الخصم وما ذكره في الجامع من أن الناس أحرار إلا في الشهادة والحدود والقصاص والعقل فإنه لا يكتفي بظاهر الحرية في هذه المواضع بل يسأل محمول على ما إذا طعن الخصم بالرق كما قيده القدوري رحمه الله؛ كذا ذكر الشارح وثبوت حرية الشاهد إما بإقامة البينة عليها أو بالإخبار للقاضي كالعدالة والأول أحب وأحسن لأن الأهلية للشهادة لا تثبت إلا بالحرية وتثبت بدون العدالة، ولأن الحرية والرق من حقوق العباد تجري فيها الخصومة وطريق الإثبات في مثلها للبيئة، فأما العدالة فلا تجري فيها الخصومة فيمكن معرفتها بالسؤال عن حاله ؛ كذا في المبسوط .
He (al-Quduri) meant by his saying 'and he asks about the witnesses'—that is, about their integrity ('adala), with a deleted genitive construction. And we only interpreted it thus because he does not ask about the freedom of the witness or his Islam unless the opponent contests it. And what he mentioned in al-Jami' that people are free except in testimony, hudud, qisas, and 'aql—that one is not satisfied with the apparent freedom in these places, but rather asks—is interpreted as when the opponent alleges slavery, as al-Quduri qualified it. Thus the commentator stated. The establishment of the witness's freedom is either by presenting evidence on it or by informing the judge, like 'adala. The first is more beloved and better, because eligibility for testimony is only established by freedom and is established without 'adala, and because freedom and slavery are among the rights of people in which litigation occurs, and the method of proof in such cases is by evidence. As for 'adala, no litigation occurs in it, so it can be known by asking about his condition. From al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage clarifies the meaning of the phrase 'questioning witnesses' in the matn. The author explains that it refers specifically to questioning about their 'adala (moral integrity). The judge does not need to ask about a witness's freedom or Islam unless the opposing party raises those issues. This is because people are presumed free ('asl al-hurriya) except in certain serious cases (testimony, hudud, qisas, 'aql) where the presumption may be set aside if the opponent claims the witness is a slave. Even then, the judge only asks if the opponent specifically contests freedom. Establishing freedom can be done by evidence (bayyinah) or by the judge's own knowledge, but the preferred method is evidence because freedom affects eligibility for testimony, and litigation over freedom/ slavery occurs between parties. In contrast, 'adala is not litigated; it is a matter for the judge to investigate through inquiry.

Key Terms
العدالة (al-ʿadālah): The moral integrity of a witness, which is the subject of the judge's inquiry.
الحرية (al-ḥurriyyah): Freedom from slavery; a prerequisite for being a witness (along with Islam and 'adala).
الخصم (al-khaṣm): The opposing party in litigation; the one who may contest a witness's freedom or Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the judge required to ask about a witness's freedom?
A) In every case involving testimony.
B) Only when the opponent specifically claims the witness is a slave.
C) Only in hudud cases.
D) Never; freedom is always presumed.

Key Takeaway
The judge's duty to ask about a witness's 'adala is constant; inquiry into freedom and Islam is triggered only by the opponent's challenge.

Judge's Inquiry When Witness Accused of Kufr
Ruling on the judge's questioning of a witness accused of kufr by the defendant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Hanafi judge may question a witness accused of kufr, and identify when such questioning invalidates the testimony.

Core Idea
The judge's inquiry into a witness's faith is limited to confirming basic belief; excessive theological probing invalidates the testimony.

When a defendant accuses a witness of disbelief, the judge faces a delicate situation. He must protect the integrity of testimony without turning the courtroom into a theological debate. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling from al-Qunyah on how to proceed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the trigger is the defendant's accusation that the witness is a kāfir (disbeliever).
2
Determine the judge's permission
The judge may ask the witness about his faith only if he suspects the defendant's accusation is false (i.e., the defendant is lying).
If no suspicion, the judge should not ask; the witness's simple denial suffices.
3
Identify the witness's required response
The witness's testimony is accepted if he affirms belief in the oneness of Allah (tawḥīd) and the prophethood of Muḥammad (risāla).
A mere 'I am Muslim' is also accepted.
4
Recognize prohibited judicial conduct
The judge must not ask theological questions beyond the simple affirmation, such as inquiries into divine attributes 'by way of experimentation'.
Such conduct is described as ignorance and foolishness.
5
State the consequence of excess
If the judge engages in such excessive questioning, the witness's testimony is not accepted, even if the witness answers correctly.
The author warns this is especially harmful in rural areas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية : قال المدعى عليه في الشاهد إنه كافر بالله تعالى فللقاضي أن يسأله عن الإيمان إن اتهمه بذلك وإن كان يشهد بوحدانية الله تعالى ورسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم تقبل شهادته، وكذا لو قال أنا مسلم ولست بكافر، ولو سأله الحاكم فذكر في خلال سؤاله ما لا يجوز على الله للتجربة فهذا جهل من القاضي وحمق وقد أساء فيما فعل، ولو جوز هذا كان وبالاً على جميع المسلمين خصوصاً في قضاة أهل الرساتيق فلو أنه تحمق وفعل لا يقبل شهادته ا هـ .
In al-Qunyah: The defendant said about the witness that he is a disbeliever in Allah. So the judge may ask him about faith if he suspects him of that. And if he testifies to the oneness of Allah and the message of Muhammad (peace be upon him), his testimony is accepted. Similarly, if he says 'I am Muslim, not a disbeliever.' And if the ruler asks him and during his questioning he mentions what is not permissible regarding Allah by way of experimentation, then this is ignorance and foolishness on the judge's part, and he has committed a wrong. And if he permits this, it would be a calamity upon all Muslims, especially among the judges of the rural areas. So if he behaves foolishly and does so, his testimony is not accepted.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage from al-Qunyah addresses a specific scenario: the defendant accuses a witness of being a kafir. The judge may ask the witness about his faith, but only if he suspects the defendant's accusation to be aimed at harming the witness (iftira'). If the witness affirms belief in tawhid and risala, his testimony is accepted. The judge must not engage in theological probing beyond what is necessary; asking questions about God's attributes for the sake of testing is considered ignorant and harmful. Such behavior from a judge renders the witness's testimony inadmissible. The author warns that this is especially dangerous in rural areas where judges may be less learned. The overall principle is that the judge should restrict his inquiry to what is needed to determine the witness's probity, not delve into speculative theology.

Key Terms
الكافر (al-kāfir): A person who disbelieves in Allah; used here as an accusation by the defendant to disqualify the witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should the judge do if the defendant accuses the witness of being a kafir?
A) Immediately reject the witness's testimony.
B) Ask the witness to recite the shahada and accept if he does.
C) Ask about faith only if he suspects the accusation is false, and not exceed necessary questions.
D) Cross-examine the witness on theological matters.

Key Takeaway
A witness's testimony is accepted upon simple affirmation of tawhid and risala; the judge must not exceed into theological probing, or the testimony is invalidated.

Tazkiya of Dhimmi Witnesses and Scope of Inquiry
Expansion on questioning witnesses and tazkiya of dhimmi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rules for questioning non-Muslim witnesses and state the criteria for tazkiya of a dhimmi.

Core Idea
A dhimmi’s witness is evaluated by his own community’s standards, not Islamic 'adalah.

The previous ruling on inquiring about witnesses is absolute—it applies to both Muslims and non-Muslims. When a Christian testifies against another Christian, the judge must ask about his character. But how do we verify a dhimmi's integrity? Hanafi fiqh provides a distinct standard: trustworthiness in his own religion, speech, and conduct.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scope of 'witness inquiry'
The passage states that the phrase 'about the witnesses' is absolute, covering Muslim and non-Muslim. So when a dhimmi testifies, the judge may ask about him just as he would a Muslim.
2
Identify the tazkiya criteria for a dhimmi
The tazkiya of a dhimmi is based on trustworthiness (amana) in three areas: his religion (i.e., he is not a liar or cheat), his tongue (truthful speech), and his hand (honest in handling property), plus being vigilant (yaqiz).
This is taken from the Fatawa of 'Umar Qari' al-Hidayah.
3
Apply the effects of conversion and intoxication
If a dhimmi was just (adl) and then converts to Islam, his testimony is accepted. But if he becomes intoxicated, his testimony is rejected because it shows lack of reliability.
Both rulings are from al-Multaqat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق في السؤال عن الشهود فشمل المسلم والكافر فيسأل عن النصراني إذا شهد على مثله . وفي فتاوى عمر قارئ الهداية تزكية الذمي أن يزكيه بالأمانة في دينه ولسانه ويده وأنه صاحب يقظة ا هـ . وقد أخذه فتاوى الولوالجي. وفي الملتقط : نصراني عدل ثم أسلم قبلت شهادته ا هـ. وفيه : إذا سكر الذمي لا تقبل شهادته ا هـ .
And the phrase 'about the witnesses' is absolute, so it includes the Muslim and the disbeliever. Thus he asks about the Christian if he testifies against his like. And in Fatawa of 'Umar Qari' al-Hidayah: The tazkiya of a dhimmi is that he verifies him as trustworthy in his religion, his tongue, and his hand, and that he is a vigilant person. And this is taken from Fatawa al-Walwaliji. In al-Multaqat: A Christian just (adl) then accepts Islam, his testimony is accepted. And therein: If a dhimmi becomes intoxicated, his testimony is not accepted.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage extends the earlier ruling on questioning witnesses to include non-Muslims. The judge may ask about a Christian witness when he testifies against another Christian (since non-Muslims may testify against each other in Hanafi fiqh). The tazkiya of a dhimmi is not based on Islamic standards of 'adalah but on trustworthiness in his own community: he should be reliable in his religion (i.e., not a liar or cheat), honest in speech, and trustworthy with property. Additionally, if a dhimmi later converts to Islam, his prior records as a just witness in dhimmi status are considered, and his testimony is accepted. However, if a dhimmi becomes intoxicated, his testimony is rejected because it indicates lack of reliability.

Key Terms
الذمي (al-dhimmī): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of an Islamic state, whose testimony may be accepted in certain cases.
التزكية (al-tazkiyah): Verification of a witness's integrity; for a dhimmi, it includes trustworthiness in his religion and actions.
قارئ الهداية (Qāri' al-Hidāyah): A title given to 'Umar, a Hanafi scholar known for his commentary on al-Hidayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Based on Islamic standards of 'adala, like a Muslim.
B) Based on trustworthiness in his religion, tongue, and hand.
C) Based on his personal declaration of Islam.
D) He is automatically considered trustworthy.

Key Takeaway
The tazkiya of a dhimmi relies on his own religious and moral standards, not Islamic 'adalah, and his testimony is void if he becomes intoxicated at the time of testifying.

Testimony After Childhood Observation: Conditions and Procedure
Ruling on testimony of a witness who observed as a minor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for accepting testimony from a witness who observed an event as a minor and identify the required procedure after puberty.

Core Idea
A child's testimony becomes valid only after puberty and community verification of his 'adala.

In this passage, the author discusses a specific scenario: a person witnessed an event while still a child, before reaching puberty. After reaching puberty, he wishes to testify about what he saw. The text explains that his testimony is not automatically accepted; rather, the judge must investigate his character, and the witness must wait until his community can attest to his reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and act
The act is testifying about an event witnessed during childhood. The subject is a witness who reached puberty after the observation.
2
Extract the ruling
The text states that the judge must ask about the witness's character (i.e., investigate 'adala) and requires a delay after puberty for the community to form an opinion about his righteousness.
3
List the conditions
Two conditions emerge: (1) the judge must inquire about the witness, and (2) the witness must wait a sufficient period after puberty for his reputation to be known.
4
Understand the default principle
The text indicates that the default for a child is lack of 'adala (justice), so verification is needed. This contrasts with a Christian convert, whose prior accepted testimony is not invalidated by conversion.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Consider a boy who witnessed a theft at age 10 and now wants to testify at age 16. The judge must ask neighbours about his character, and the boy must have resided long enough for a reputation to form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشمل السؤال عنه إذا شهد حين بلغ وهو ظاهر الخانية. وفي الملتقط : احتلم لا أقبل شهادته ما لم أسأل عنه ولا بد من أن يتأنى بعد البلوغ بقدر ما يقع في قلوب أهل مسجده ومحلته كما في الغريب أنه صالح أو وفرق في الظهيرية بينهما بأن النصراني كان له شهادة مقبولة قبل إسلامه بخلاف الصبي، وهذا يدل على أن الأصل عدم العدالة
And the questioning includes him when he testifies, having reached puberty—this is apparent from al-Khaniyah. And in al-Multaqat: If he has had a wet dream, I do not accept his testimony until I ask about him. And it is necessary that he delays after puberty for as long as it takes for the people of his mosque and his locality to form an opinion about him being righteous. And al-Dhahiriyyah differentiated between them: the Christian had acceptable testimony before his Islam, unlike the boy. And this indicates that the default is lack of 'adala.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage deals with a witness who witnessed an event as a child and then reached puberty (ihtalam). The judge must ask about his condition after puberty to determine if he is now just. The witness must wait after puberty until his reputation is established among his community. This is unlike a Christian who converts to Islam, because the Christian had prior status as a just witness in his own community, so his conversion does not erase that. The principle drawn is that for a child, the default is lack of 'adala (so verification is needed).

Key Terms
البلوغ (al-bulūgh): Puberty; the age at which a person becomes legally responsible and can be a witness.
العدالة (al-'adāla): Justice or moral probity; a required quality for a witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Wording of Tazkiya and Three Ranks of Verifiers
Explaining what the verifier says when asked and the three ranks of tazkiya response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three ranks of verifiers in Hanafi law and identify the preferred wording for tazkiya according to the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The verifier must explicitly state the witness's testimony is admissible; 'he is just' alone may be insufficient.

In Islamic courts, the integrity of witnesses (tazkiya) is crucial. The exact wording the verifier (muzakki) uses can determine whether a witness's testimony is accepted. This passage surveys various opinions within the Hanafi school and establishes a hierarchy of verification statements, culminating in a preferred ruling that prioritizes clarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Understand that the matn (original text) did not specify the exact wording for tazkiya because it varies. The commentator now provides guidance from multiple sources.
2
Recognize the range of acceptable phrasings
List the different statements considered valid: 'he is just' (huwa 'adl), 'I know nothing but good' (la a'lam illa khayr), 'there is no harm in him' (la ba's), and others. Note that each source may have its own preference.
Abu Yusuf and others accept simpler phrasings.
3
Understand al-Sarakhsi's objection
Al-Sarakhsi argues that saying 'he is just' (huwa 'adl) is insufficient because a person who has received hadd punishment and repented is just in religiousness but his testimony may still be rejected. Therefore, explicit mention of admissibility (jā'iz al-shahādah) is needed.
This is a key intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Learn the three ranks of verifiers
The passage divides verifiers into three ranks according to their declaration: highest is 'admissible testimony' or 'just' (with the ranking preference), second is 'reliable' (thiqah - trustworthy but may have minor issues), third is 'unknown' (mastur - whose condition is not known or who is considered fasiq).
The thiqah rank is weaker than 'adl; two thiqah witnesses may equal one 'adl.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text states that al-Sarakhsi's view (requiring 'jā'iz al-shahādah') should be preferred (يَنْبَغِي تَرْجِيحُهُ). Thus, for fatwa, the verifier should explicitly state that the witness's testimony is admissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المؤلف ما يقوله المزكي إذا سئل لأنه يختلف باختلاف الناس، وقدمنا أنه يقول هو عدل وفي البزازية : وينبغي أن يعدل قطعاً ولا يقول هم عدول عندي لإخبار الثقات ،به ولو قال لا أعلم منهم إلا خيراً فهو تعديل في الأصح. وفي النوازل التعديل أن يقول هم عدول عندي جازت شهادتهم. وفي المنتقى : إذا قال المزكي أعلم فيه إلا خيراً يكفي وإذا جرح الجارح الشهود يقول القاضي للمدعي زدني شهوداً أو يقول لم تحمد شهودك ويكتب القاضي أسماء الشهود أولاً ثم اسم من عدل ا هـ. أبي يوسف : التزكية أن يقول لا أعلم منه إلا خيراً. وعن أبي يوسف أنه لو سلمة أن يقول هذا عدل رضي جائز الملتقط وفي عن قال لا بأس فقد عدله . به وعن محمد بن عن قال لا بأس فقد عدله . به وعن محمد بن عندي قذف بعد الشهادة ا.هـ. واختار السرخسي أنه لا يكتفى بقوله هو عدل لأن المحدود في التوبة عدل غير جائز الشهادة، وكذا الأب إذا شهد لابنه فلا بد من زيادة جائز الشهادة كما في الظهيرية، وينبغي ترجيحه وفي الظهيرية من كتاب الشروط : جواب المزكي على ثلاث مراتب أعلاها جائز الشهادة أو عدل خلافاً للسرخسي في الثاني. والثانية ثقة وهو من لا تقبل شهادته لا لفسقه ولكن لغفلة أو نحوها وبعض القضاة يقيمون كل ثقتين مقام علل : كذا ذكر الشيخ الإمام الحاكم السمرقندي والمرتبة الثالثة مستور والمستور هو الفاسق وفي عرف مشايخنا من لا يعرف حاله ا.هـ.
The author did not mention what the verifier says when asked because it differs according to people. We have stated that he says 'he is just'. In al-Bazzaziyyah: He should definitely declare him just and not say 'they are just according to me' due to reports from reliable sources. If he says 'I know nothing but good about them', that is a ta'dil in the most correct view. In al-Nawazil: Ta'dil is to say 'they are just according to me, their testimony is permissible.' In al-Muntaqa: If the verifier says 'I know nothing but good about him', it suffices. And if the disparager disparages the witnesses, the judge tells the plaintiff to produce more witnesses or says 'you have not praised your witnesses'. The judge writes the names of the witnesses first, then the name of the one who declared him just. Abu Yusuf: Tazkiya is to say 'I know nothing but good about him.' From Abu Yusuf: If one says 'this is a just and satisfactory witness', his testimony is permissible. In al-Multaqat: If one says 'there is no harm in him', he has declared him just. From Muhammad: ... after testimony? Al-Sarakhsi chose that saying 'he is just' is not sufficient, because the one who has been punished with hadd after repentance is just but not admissible as a witness. Similarly, the father testifying for his son requires the addition 'admissible testimony'. This should be preferred. In al-Dhahiriyyah from Kitab al-Shurut: The verifier's response is of three ranks: the highest is 'admissible testimony' or 'just', contrary to al-Sarakhsi regarding the second. The second is 'reliable (thiqah)', meaning one whose testimony is not accepted not due to sin but due to carelessness or the like. Some judges consider two reliable persons equivalent to one just. The third rank is 'unknown (mastur)', and mastur is the fasiq, and in the terminology of our scholars, the one whose condition is unknown.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This long passage discusses the precise wording a verifier (muzakki) should use when asked about a witness. The author notes that the original text did not specify the wording because it varies. Common practice is to say 'he is just'. Various sources provide different acceptable phrasings: 'I know nothing but good', 'there is no harm in him', etc. Al-Sarakhsi insists that the phrase 'he is just' alone is insufficient because a person who received hadd punishment for qadhf (false accusation) and repented is just in piety but his testimony may still be rejected. Thus, the verifier should explicitly say 'his testimony is admissible' or similar. The passage concludes by categorizing verifiers into three ranks: (1) 'adl/jā'iz al-shahādah – highest, (2) thiqah – reliable but may have minor flaws like forgetfulness, (3) mastur – unknown or fasiq. This ranking helps judges evaluate the weight of the verification.

Key Terms
المزكي (al-muzakkī): The person who verifies the integrity of a witness, usually a knowledgeable person in the community.
ثقة (thiqah): A verifier's statement that the witness is trustworthy but not necessarily up to the level of 'adl; his testimony may be weaker.
مستور (mastūr): An unknown person; in tazkiya, it refers to a witness whose condition is not known, or a fasiq (sinner) by default.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what should the verifier say to properly declare a witness just?
A) 'He is just' alone.
B) 'He is just, his testimony is admissible' or 'jā'iz al-shahādah'.
C) 'He is reliable' (thiqah).
D) 'I know nothing but good about him'.

Key Takeaway
The verifier must explicitly state that the witness's testimony is admissible; al-Sarakhsi's more stringent view is the mufta bihi.

Silence of a Righteous Scholar as Tazkiya
Ruling that silence from a qualified scholar can be a valid tazkiya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a verifier's silence qualifies as tazkiya in Hanafi law and apply this ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Silence from a righteous scholar can be the loudest verification of a witness.

In Hanafi court procedure, a judge must ensure witnesses are trustworthy. While explicit verification of a witness is standard, this lesson explores an exceptional case: when a qualified scholar remains silent, their very silence can legally serve as tazkiya. This principle, grounded in the character of the verifier, is illustrated by historical anecdotes from Hanafi judicial practice.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and identify the act
The ruling is that 'silence from people of knowledge and righteousness is sufficient' to serve as tazkiya. The act is the verifier's silence in response to an inquiry about a witness.
2
Identify the conditions for the ruling
The silence must come from a person who is both knowledgeable ('alim) and righteous (salih). These qualifications ensure the person would not remain silent if the witness were unfit.
3
Examine the narrative evidence
Analyze the two anecdotes: (1) Judge al-Layth ibn Musawir's visit to the ill verifier, where repeated silence was accepted as tazkiya. (2) The messenger's inquiry about Abu Muti' to Ya'qub al-Qari, where the ambiguous response was deemed acceptable due to Ya'qub's stature.
The text uses these as precedents for the rule.
4
Distinguish from the general rule
Normally, tazkiya requires explicit wording. This is a specific exception that applies only to verifiers of high scholarly and moral standing.
5
Apply to a contemporary scenario
Consider a judge consulting a respected mufti about a witness. If the mufti remains silent despite being asked, a Hanafi judge may treat that silence as tazkiya.
The mufti must be known for his knowledge and piety.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكتفي بالسكوت من أهل العلم والصلاح فيكون سكوته تزكية للشاهد لما في الملتقط : وكان الليث بن مساور قاضياً فاحتاج إلى تعديل شاهد وكان المزكي مريضاً فعاده القاضي وسأله عن الشاهد فسكت المعدل ثم سأله فسكت فقال أسألك ولا تجيبني فقال المعدل أما يكفيك من مثلي السكوت ولما استقضى أبو مطيع أرسل إلى يعقوب القارئ يشاوره فسأله الرسول في الطريق عن أبي مطيع فقال يعقوب أبو مطيع أبو مطيع قال محمد بن سلمة : إذا كان المعدل مثل يعقوب القارئ فلا بأس بمثل هذا التعديل ا هـ .
And silence from people of knowledge and righteousness is sufficient, so their silence is a tazkiya for the witness. As in al-Multaqat: Al-Layth ibn Musawir was a judge and needed to verify a witness. The verifier was ill, so the judge visited him and asked about the witness. The verifier remained silent, then the judge asked again, and he remained silent. The judge said, 'I ask you and you do not answer me.' The verifier said, 'Is silence from the likes of me not sufficient for you?' When Abu Muti' was appointed as judge, he sent to Ya'qub al-Qari to consult him. The messenger asked on the way about Abu Muti'. Ya'qub said, 'Abu Muti' is Abu Muti'.' Muhammad ibn Salamah said: If the verifier is like Ya'qub al-Qari, then such a verification is acceptable.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage addresses a rare but important point: the silence of a respected scholar can be interpreted as a positive verification (tazkiya) of a witness. The anecdote of Judge Layth ibn Musawir illustrates this: when he visited a verifier (muzakki) who was ill and asked about a witness, the verifier's silence was taken as approval because his status was such that he would not remain silent if the witness were unfit. Similarly, Ya'qub al-Qari's ambiguous repetition of Abu Muti's name was accepted as tazkiya because of his known integrity. This shows that in Hanafi procedure, the form of tazkiya is not rigid; context and the character of the verifier matter. The rule is qualified: silence suffices only from those who are scholars and righteous ('ahl al-'ilm wa al-salah).

Key Terms
السكوت (al-sukūt): Silence in response to a question about a witness; in this context, it can be a form of tazkiya from a qualified person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the silence of a learned and righteous person can legally serve as a positive verification of a witness.

Forms and Conditions of Tazkiyah for Witnesses
Explaining various statements that constitute valid tazkiyah and the three ranks of integrity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish valid forms of tazkiyah from insufficient ones, explain the three ranks of witness integrity in Hanafi law, and apply the rules to evaluate witness testimony in a court setting.

Core Idea
Tazkiyah must be explicit about integrity; silence suffices only from the truly righteous.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqā'iq, delves into the procedural details of tazkiyah – the process of validating a witness's moral integrity ('adala). It presents various statements that qualify as valid tazkiyah, reveals intra-Hanafi disagreements on the matter, and introduces a three-tier ranking of witness credibility. Understanding these nuances is essential for judges and legal practitioners to ensure proper testimony admission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the forms of tazkiyah
Read the passage and list the various statements that Hanafi sources consider valid for tazkiyah: 'I know only good from him', 'they are upright in my view', 'there is no harm', etc. Note the differences across sources like al-Bazzaziyya, al-Nawazil, al-Muntaqa.
2
Map the intra-Hanafi differences
Determine the positions of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and al-Sarakhsi. Abu Yusuf accepts 'I know only good' and 'he is upright with me, approved'. Muhammad accepts 'there is no harm'. Al-Sarakhsi rejects 'he is 'adl' alone and requires the addition of 'jā'iz al-shahādah'.
Note that al-Sarakhsi's concern is that a person punished for a hadd may be 'adl after repentance but still ineligible to testify.
3
Understand the three-rank system
From al-Zahiriyyah: Highest rank is 'jā'iz al-shahādah' or ''adl'; second is 'thiqah' (trustworthy, but testimony not accepted due to negligence, not fisq); third is 'mastur' (in common usage = fasiq, in scholarly usage = unknown status).
This system helps judges classify witnesses quickly.
4
Analyze the silence exception
The passage relates stories where silence from a known righteous person (like al-Layth ibn Musawir and Ya'qub al-Qari') was accepted as tazkiyah. This is not general permission; it relies on the validator's reputation.
Contrast with the earlier statement from Ghayat al-Bayan that silence may be used to avoid disclosing someone's fisq.
5
Apply the rules to a practical scenario
Given a validator's statement, determine whether it suffices for tazkiyah according to the mufta bihi position and explain why.
Remember the preference for explicit 'jā'iz al-shahādah' or ''adl' per the three-rank system.

الشهادة ا.هـ. واختار السرخسي أنه لا يكتفى بقوله هو عدل لأن المحدود في التوبة عدل غير جائز الشهادة، وكذا الأب إذا شهد لابنه فلا بد من زيادة جائز الشهادة كما في الظهيرية، وينبغي ترجيحه وفي الظهيرية من كتاب الشروط : جواب المزكي على ثلاث مراتب أعلاها جائز الشهادة أو عدل خلافاً للسرخسي في الثاني. والثانية ثقة وهو من لا تقبل شهادته لا لفسقه ولكن لغفلة أو نحوها وبعض القضاة يقيمون كل ثقتين مقام علل : كذا ذكر الشيخ الإمام الحاكم السمرقندي والمرتبة الثالثة مستور والمستور هو الفاسق وفي عرف مشايخنا من لا يعرف حاله ا.هـ. ويكتفى بالسكوت من أهل العلم والصلاح فيكون سكوته تزكية للشاهد لما في الملتقط : وكان الليث بن مساور قاضياً فاحتاج إلى تعديل شاهد وكان المزكي مريضاً فعاده القاضي وسأله عن الشاهد فسكت المعدل ثم سأله فسكت فقال أسألك ولا تجيبني فقال المعدل أما يكفيك من مثلي السكوت ولما استقضى أبو مطيع أرسل إلى يعقوب القارئ يشاوره فسأله الرسول في الطريق عن أبي مطيع فقال يعقوب أبو مطيع أبو مطيع قال محمد بن سلمة : إذا كان المعدل مثل يعقوب القارئ فلا بأس بمثل هذا التعديل ا هـ .

میر
والإسلام ينفي الوجوب أيضاً حتى لو سأله عنهما كان حسناً تأمل قوله: (وفرق في الظهيرية بينهما الخ) قال الرملي : أي بين النصراني إذا أسلم وكان عدلاً حيث تقبل وبين الصبي إذا بلغ حيث لا تقبل حتى يسأل عنه ويتأنى بقدر ما يقع في قلوب أهل مسجده ومحلته أنه صالح.
قوله : (ويكتفي بالسكوت من أهل العلم والصلاح فيكون سكوته تزكية للشاهد مخالف لما قدمه عن غاية البيان من قوله ومن عرفه بالفسق لم يصرح به بل يسكت احترازاً . هتك الستر أو عن يكتب الله أعلم به الخ ) ثم رأيت بخط ثقة معزياً إلى المقدسي بعد ذكر ما في الملتقط قال أبو نصر :
Book of Testimonies. ... That he waits after puberty to the extent that it occurs in the hearts of the people of his mosque and his neighborhood that he is righteous. And he differentiated in al-Zahiriyyah between them: that the Christian had acceptable testimony before his Islam, unlike the child. This indicates that the original principle is lack of integrity. And the author did not mention what the validator says when asked, because it differs according to people. And we have said: he says 'he is upright'. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: he should definitely declare uprightness and not say 'they are upright in my view' due to informing the trustworthy. And if he says 'I know only good from them', it is a valid validation according to the most correct. In al-Nawazil: validation is that he says 'they are upright in my view', and their testimony is permissible. In al-Muntaqa: if the validator says 'I know only good in him', it suffices. And if the impugner impugns the witnesses, the judge says to the plaintiff: 'add more witnesses' or says 'your witnesses are not praised'. And the judge writes the names of the witnesses first, then the name of the one who validated them. From Abu Yusuf: tazkiyah is that he says 'I know only good from him'. From Abu Yusuf that if he says 'this is upright with me, approved', it is permissible. And from Muhammad: if he says 'there is no harm', he has validated him. And al-Sarakhsi chose that his saying 'he is upright' alone is not sufficient, because the one punished in repentance is upright but not permissible to testify. Similarly, the father when he testifies for his son, there must be the addition 'permissible to testify' as in al-Zahiriyyah. And it should be given preference. And in al-Zahiriyyah from the Book of Conditions: the answer of the validator is on three levels: the highest is 'permissible to testify' or 'upright', contrary to al-Sarakhsi regarding the second. The second is 'trustworthy', and he is one whose testimony is not accepted not due to his immorality, but due to negligence or the like. And some judges deem every two trustworthy persons equivalent to the cause? Thus stated the chief scholar al-Hakim al-Samarqandi. The third level is 'mastur', and mastur is the immoral person, and in the custom of our scholars, it is one whose condition is unknown. And silence from people of knowledge and righteousness suffices, so their silence is a validation of the witness, as in al-Multaqat: al-Layth ibn Musawir was a judge and needed validation of a witness, and the validator was ill. The judge visited him and asked about the witness. The validator remained silent. Then he asked him again and he remained silent. He said: I ask you and you do not answer. The validator said: Is not silence from the likes of me sufficient? And when Abu Muti' was appointed judge, he sent to Ya'qub al-Qari' to consult him. The messenger asked him on the road about Abu Muti', and Ya'qub said: 'Abu Muti' Abu Muti'. Muhammad ibn Salamah said: If the validator is like Ya'qub al-Qari', then such validation is fine. [End of quote]. (Then commentary:) And Islam negates the obligation also, so if he asked about them it would be good. Contemplate his words: 'And he differentiated in al-Zahiriyyah...' al-Ramli said: Between the Christian when he becomes Muslim and was upright, it is accepted, and the child when he reaches puberty, it is not accepted until he is asked about and waits to the extent that it occurs in the hearts of the people of his mosque and neighborhood that he is righteous. His words: 'And silence suffices from people of knowledge and righteousness, so their silence is validation of the witness.' This contradicts what was presented from Ghayat al-Bayan from his words: 'And whoever knows him to be immoral does not declare it explicitly, but remains silent to avoid disclosing the private matter or to avoid saying 'Allah knows best about him'.' Then I saw in the handwriting of a trustworthy person, attributing to al-Maqdisi, after mentioning what is in al-Multaqat: said Abu Nasr:
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, expanding on rulings related to tazkiyah (validation) of witnesses in Hanafi fiqh. It begins with a comparison between a Christian who converts to Islam and a child who reaches puberty: the Christian's prior testimony as a non-Muslim is accepted if he becomes Muslim and is upright, while a child's testimony upon puberty requires further inquiry into his integrity. This shows the default assumption is lack of 'adala until proven. The text then details the forms of tazkiyah when a judge asks about a witness. The author states that earlier it was said that the validator should say 'he is upright', but then presents variations from different sources: al-Bazzaziyyah says he should absolutely declare uprightness and not say 'they are upright in my view' because that relies on others' reports. If he says 'I know only good from them', it is valid. Al-Nawazil says saying 'they are upright in my view' suffices. Al-Muntaqa says saying 'I know only good in him' suffices. From Abu Yusuf, tazkiyah is saying 'I know only good from him', and also that saying 'he is upright with me, approved' is permissible. From Muhammad, saying 'there is no harm' is considered ta'dil. Al-Sarakhsi, however, chose that saying 'he is upright' alone is insufficient because a person punished for a hadd offense may be upright in repentance but his testimony is not accepted. Similarly, a father testifying for his son must be explicitly stated as 'jā'iz al-shahādah' (permissible to testify). The text then presents the three ranks of tazkiyah from al-Zahiriyyah: highest is 'jā'iz al-shahādah' or 'adl', second is 'thiqah' (trustworthy) – one whose testimony is not accepted due to negligence, not fisaq – and third is 'mastur', which in common usage means fasiq, but in the custom of our scholars means one whose condition is unknown. The passage then discusses a special case: silence from a person of knowledge and righteousness can be considered tazkiyah, as exemplified by the story of al-Layth ibn Musawir and the silent validator, and the case of Ya'qub al-Qari' saying 'Abu Muti' Abu Muti'. This is accepted if the validator is of such caliber. The commentary that follows discusses nuances: that Islam does not obligate inquiry, and refines the distinction between the Christian convert and the child, and reconciles the silence ruling with earlier statements from Ghayat al-Bayan.

Key Terms
تزكية (tazkiyah): The process of validating a witness's integrity ('adala) by a qualified person, typically through a statement or silence.
تعديل (ta'dil): The act of declaring a witness as 'adl (upright) as part of tazkiyah.
عدل ('adl): A person with integrity ('adala) who avoids major sins and is not known for minor sins; his testimony is accepted.
ثقة (thiqah): Trustworthy, but not necessarily 'adl; one whose testimony is not accepted due to negligence or similar, not fisaq.
مستور (mastur): One whose condition is unknown (not known to be fasiq) – in common Hanafi usage, it can also mean fasiq, but technically the term is applied when the person's 'adala is not revealed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the three-rank system presented in the passage, which is the highest level of witness integrity?
A) 'Adl
B) Thiqah
C) Mastur
D) Fasiq

Key Takeaway
Tazkiyah requires explicit declaration of 'adala or 'jā'iz al-shahādah'; silence only suffices from individuals of known righteousness.

Conflict Between Jarh and Ta'dil: Precedence of Jarh
Detailing rules when witnesses are both validated and impugned, and the priority of jarh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for resolving conflict between jarh and ta'dil in witness assessment, distinguishing the views of Imamayn and Muhammad, and identifying exceptions such as partisanship.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, jarh takes precedence over ta'dil when numbers conflict, except in cases of partisanship.

When assessing a witness's integrity, a judge may receive conflicting reports of validation (ta'dil) and impugnment (jarh). How does the court decide which testimony to accept? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lays out the Hanafi procedural rules, including an intra-madhhab difference between the two Imams and Muhammad. Understanding these rules is essential for any scholar or judge dealing with witness credibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict scenario
Determine that there are at least two statements about the witness: one validating (ta'dil) and one impugning (jarh). The judge must resolve the conflict.
The conflict may involve different numbers of witnesses on each side.
2
Apply the initial rule from al-Bazzaziyyah
If one validates and one impugns, they conflict as if no one was asked. A third opinion decides: if third validates, ta'dil wins; if third impugns, jarh wins.
This rule establishes that with equal numbers, a tie-breaking opinion is needed.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute for one vs. one
Al-Sadr reports that according to Imamayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), one jarh outweighs one ta'dil, so jarh is preferred. Muhammad holds that the testimony is suspended until additional information is sought.
The mufta bihi is the view of Imamayn.
4
Apply the numerical hierarchy
Based on examples: one jarh vs. two ta'dil → ta'dil preferred. Two jarh vs. ten ta'dil → jarh preferred. The relative numbers matter, but jarh generally carries more weight.
The rule is not a simple majority; jarh has inherent priority unless ta'dil has a clear majority.
5
Consider exceptions and procedural nuances
If partisanship exists, jarh is not accepted. Also, secret jarh is accepted while open jarh may be rejected due to the impugners' own fisaq. A stranger witness may write to his hometown judge for validation.
These exceptions protect against bias and preserve the integrity of testimony.

وسيأتي في مسائل الطعن في الشاهد عند بيان الجرح المجرد وغيره ولكن يحتاج هنا إلى بیان مسائل تعارض الجرح والتعديل فإذا سأل القاضي عن الشاهد ولم يزك طلب غيره فإن زكاه واحد وجرحه واحد فقد تعارضا فقال في البزازية : فإن عدله أحدهما وجرحه الآخر تعارضا كأنه لم يسأل أحداً، وإن عدله الثالث فالتعديل أولى، وإن جرحه الثالث فالجرح أولى. وذكر الصدر: إذا جرح واحد وعدل واحد فعند الإمامين الجرح أولى كما لو كانا اثنين. وعند محمد ما لم يتم بالواحد توقف الشهادة ولا يجيز حتى يسأل الآخر، فإن جرحه تم الجرح، وإن عدله تم التعديل فإن جرحه واحد وعدله اثنان فالتعديل أولى عندهم، وإن اثنان وعدله عشرة فالجرح أولى، فلو قال المدعي بعد الجرح أنا أجيء بقوم صالحين يعدلونهم. قال في العيون قبل ذلك وفي النوادر أنه لا يقبل وهو اختيار ظهير الدين وعلى قول من يقبل إذا جاء بقوم ثقة يعدلونهم فالقاضي يسأل الجارحين فلعلهم جرحوا بما لا يكون جرحاً عند القاضي لا يلتفت إلى جرحهم ؛ هذا ألطف الأقاويل. ولو عدل الشهود سراً فقال الخصم أجيء في العلانية بمن يبين فيهم ما ترد به شهادتهم لا تقبل مقالته إلى أن قال أن الجرح أولى إلا إذا كان بينهم تعصب فإنه لا يقبل جرحهم لأن أصل الشهادة لا تقبل عند التعصب فالجرح أولى ا وقد ظهر من إطلاق كلامهم هنا أن الجرح يقدم على التعديل، سواء كان مجرداً أو لا عند سؤال القاضي عن الشاهد والتفصيل الآتي من أنه إن كان مجرداً لا تسمع البينة به أولاً فتسمع إنما هو عند طعن الخصم في الشاهد علانية لكن في الملتقط : فلو عدل فقال قوم إنا رأيناه أمس سكران أو يبايع بالربا أو يشرب الخمر إن كان شيئاً يلزمه فيه حق من حد أو مال يرد على صاحبه ردت شهادته وإلا لا ا هـ . على ما إذا كان علانية، أما إذا أخبروه سراً فلا وسيأتي تمامه إن شاء الله تعالى. وشمل إطلاقه ما إذا كان الشاهد غريباً فإن كان غريباً ولا يجد معدلاً فإنه يكتب إلى قاضي بلده ليخبره عن حاله كما في البزازية. وفي كشف الأسرار شرح أصول فخر الإسلام من بحث المجمل أنه

110. Book of Testimonies. ... And there will come in the issues of attacking the witness, when explaining the mere jarh and others, but here we need to explain issues of conflict between jarh and ta'dil. When the judge asks about the witness and he is not validated, he asks for another. If one validates him and one impugns him, they conflict. Al-Bazzaziyyah said: if one declares him upright and the other impugns him, they conflict as if no one was asked. If the third declares him upright, then ta'dil is preferable. If the third impugns him, then jarh is preferable. And al-Sadr mentioned: if one impugns and one declares upright, according to the two imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), jarh is preferable as if there were two. According to Muhammad, unless it is completed by one, the testimony is suspended and he does not permit until he asks the other. If he impugns, the jarh is completed; if he declares upright, the ta'dil is completed. If one impugns and two declare upright, then ta'dil is preferable according to them. If two impugn and ten declare upright, then jarh is preferable. If the plaintiff says after jarh: 'I will bring righteous people who will declare them upright.' It is said in al-'Uyun before that and in al-Nawadir that it is not accepted, and this is the choice of Zahir al-Din. According to the one who accepts, when he brings trustworthy people who declare them upright, the judge asks the impugners, perhaps they impugned with something that is not jarh according to the judge, so he does not pay attention to their jarh. This is the most subtle opinion. If the witnesses were validated secretly, and the opponent says: 'I will publicly bring those who can show in them what would reject their testimony,' his statement is not accepted, until he said: jarh is preferable unless there is partisanship among them, for then their jarh is not accepted because the original testimony is not accepted in case of partisanship, so jarh is preferable. And it has become clear from the absolute statements here that jarh is given precedence over ta'dil, whether it is bare or not, when the judge asks about the witness. The detailed discussion later that if it is bare, the evidence is not heard first, then it is heard, only when the opponent attacks the witness openly. But in al-Multaqat: if he says, 'Indeed we saw him yesterday drunk, or dealing in usury, or drinking wine,' if it is something that imposes a right upon him of a prescribed punishment or wealth that should be returned to its owner, his testimony is rejected, otherwise not. This is when it is open. As for when they inform secretly, then no. And its completion will come if Allah wills. And its absolute application includes when the witness is a stranger. If he is a stranger and finds no validator, he writes to the judge of his town to inform about his condition, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And in Kashf al-Asrar, commentary on Usul Fakhrislam, from the discussion of al-Mujmal, that the judge hears. And it should be carried that his silence was a attack on the testimony. His words: 'And according to the one who accepts...' is stated firmly in al-Khaniyyah: that he asks about them. If they declare them upright, the judge asks the attackers with what they attack, because they might have attacked with something that is not jarh according to the judge. If they show what is an attack, then jarh is preferable; otherwise, the judge does not pay attention to them and judges with the testimony of the plaintiff's witnesses. Similarly, if the validator declared the witnesses upright and the defendant attacked, and said to the judge: 'So-and-so and so-and-so,' and named people who are suitable. His words: 'When the judge asks about the witness' – he should have added 'or when the opponent attacks and proves it secretly', because it is accepted then, for they did not commit fisaq by manifesting indecency, unlike when he proves openly, his proof is not accepted because his witnesses became fasiq by manifesting indecency, as will come at the end of the next chapter. This clarifies the earlier answer regarding what is in al-Multaqat. Contemplate. His words: 'from the discussion of al-Mujmal' meaning al-Mujmal.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the rules when there is a conflict between jarh (impugnment) and ta'dil (validation) of witnesses. The judge, after asking about a witness, if one person validates and another impugns, they conflict. According to al-Bazzaziyyah, if one declares upright and another impugns, it is as if no one was asked. If a third declares upright, ta'dil is preferred; if a third impugns, jarh is preferred. Al-Sadr (a Hanafi authority) adds details: according to the two Imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), one jarh outweighs one ta'dil as if there were two, while Muhammad holds that with one each the case is suspended until the other is asked; if that second person impugns, jarh is established, if validates, ta'dil is established. If one impugns and two validate, ta'dil is preferred; if two impugn and ten validate, jarh is preferred. The passage then discusses a scenario where after jarh, the plaintiff wants to bring new witnesses to validate. Some (Zahir al-Din) say it is not accepted, while others accept but then the judge should investigate the impugners' reasons – if their jarh is not valid in the judge's view, they are ignored. The text also distinguishes between secret and open jarh: if the opponent brings jarh secretly, it is accepted, because they did not publicly commit indecency; if openly, their own testimony may be rejected due to their own fisaq. The general principle established is that jarh takes precedence over ta'dil, unless there is partisanship. The passage also mentions that for a stranger witness with no validator, he writes to his hometown judge.

Key Terms
جرح (jarh): Impugnment of a witness's integrity, claiming that they are not 'adl, which may lead to rejection of testimony.
تعارض (ta'āruḍ): Conflict between two contradictory pieces of evidence or claims, here between jarh and ta'dil.
أولى (awlā): Preferable; the ruling or evidence that should be given precedence in case of conflict.
تعصب (ta'aṣṣub): Partisanship or bias, which can invalidate jarh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Sadr, what is the ruling when one witness impugns a witness and one validates that same witness?
A) The testimony is rejected immediately.
B) The judge asks for a third opinion.
C) According to the two Imams, jarh is preferred; according to Muhammad, the matter is suspended.
D) The validation takes precedence because there is no confirmed jarh.

Key Takeaway
Jarh is generally preferred over ta'dil in Hanafi law, but the numbers of each and the presence of partisanship can alter the ruling.

Conflict Between Jarh and Ta'dil: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jarh vs. ta'dil precedence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on conflicting jarh and ta'dil, apply the rule of precedence based on numerical weight and the nature of jarh, and distinguish the two Imams' view from Muhammad's.

Core Idea
Jarh reveals hidden defects; thus it generally outweighs ta'dil even when numerically fewer.

When a judge receives conflicting reports about a witness—one person impugning his credibility (jarh) and another accrediting it (ta'dil)—a legal conflict arises. The Hanafi school has a well-known internal disagreement on how to resolve it. This lesson unpacks the views of Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, as well as the broader principles that govern judicial investigation of witness character.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict scenario
Recognize the situation: the judge asks about a witness and gets mixed responses—one jarh and one ta'dil. This triggers the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The key is that the reports are in direct opposition.
2
State the two Imams' position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that jarh is preferred even from a single impugner, as if two had impugned. The reasoning: jar uncovers hidden faults.
3
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani requires waiting for the second person's statement. Until then, testimony is suspended. Once the second speaks, whichever side is complete prevails.
This is a more cautious approach.
4
Apply numerical weight rules
Both sides agree that if there are multiple on one side, the scale may tip. For example, two accredit vs. ten impugn: jarh still wins. But one impugner vs. two accreditors: ta'dil wins.
The principle is that jarh's probative strength is high, but overwhelming ta'dil can overcome it.
5
Understand the judge's investigative duty
The judge should ask impugners for the basis of their jarh. If the basis is legally insufficient (e.g., unspecified or based on bias), the jarh may be disregarded. Also, public vs. secret testimony affects admissibility.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on substance over mere allegation.

Source Text

وسيأتي في مسائل الطعن في الشاهد عند بيان الجرح المجرد وغيره ولكن يحتاج هنا إلى بیان مسائل تعارض الجرح والتعديل فإذا سأل القاضي عن الشاهد ولم يزك طلب غيره فإن زكاه واحد وجرحه واحد فقد تعارضا فقال في البزازية : فإن عدله أحدهما وجرحه الآخر تعارضا كأنه لم يسأل أحداً، وإن عدله الثالث فالتعديل أولى، وإن جرحه الثالث فالجرح أولى. وذكر الصدر: إذا جرح واحد وعدل واحد فعند الإمامين الجرح أولى كما لو كانا اثنين. وعند محمد ما لم يتم بالواحد توقف الشهادة ولا يجيز حتى يسأل الآخر، فإن جرحه تم الجرح، وإن عدله تم التعديل فإن جرحه واحد وعدله اثنان فالتعديل أولى عندهم، وإن اثنان وعدله عشرة فالجرح أولى، فلو قال المدعي بعد الجرح أنا أجيء بقوم صالحين يعدلونهم. قال في العيون قبل ذلك وفي النوادر أنه لا يقبل وهو اختيار ظهير الدين وعلى قول من يقبل إذا جاء بقوم ثقة يعدلونهم فالقاضي يسأل الجارحين فلعلهم جرحوا بما لا يكون جرحاً عند القاضي لا يلتفت إلى جرحهم ؛ هذا ألطف الأقاويل. ولو عدل الشهود سراً فقال الخصم أجيء في العلانية بمن يبين فيهم ما ترد به شهادتهم لا تقبل مقالته إلى أن قال أن الجرح أولى إلا إذا كان بينهم تعصب فإنه لا يقبل جرحهم لأن أصل الشهادة لا تقبل عند التعصب فالجرح أولى ا وقد ظهر من إطلاق كلامهم هنا أن الجرح يقدم على التعديل، سواء كان مجرداً أو لا عند سؤال القاضي عن الشاهد والتفصيل الآتي من أنه إن كان مجرداً لا تسمع البينة به أولاً فتسمع إنما هو عند طعن الخصم في الشاهد علانية لكن في الملتقط : فلو عدل فقال قوم إنا رأيناه أمس سكران أو يبايع بالربا أو يشرب الخمر إن كان شيئاً يلزمه فيه حق من حد أو مال يرد على صاحبه ردت شهادته وإلا لا ا هـ . على ما إذا كان علانية، أما إذا أخبروه سراً فلا وسيأتي تمامه إن شاء الله تعالى. وشمل إطلاقه ما إذا كان الشاهد غريباً فإن كان غريباً ولا يجد معدلاً فإنه يكتب إلى قاضي بلده ليخبره عن حاله كما في البزازية. وفي كشف الأسرار شرح أصول فخر الإسلام من بحث المجمل أنه القاضي يسمع هـ. وينبغي حمله كان سكوته منه طعناً في الشهادة قوله : (وعلى قول من يقبل الخ) جزم به في الخانية حيث قال: فإن ذلك ويسأل عنهم فإن عدلوهم سأل القاضي الطاعنين بم يطعنون لاحتمال أنهم طعنوا بما لا يكون جرحاً عند القاضي، فإن بينوا ما يكون طعناً فإن الجرح أولى وإلا فإن القاضي لا يلتفت إليهم ويقضي بشهاده شهود المدعي. وكذا لو عدل المزكي الشهود وطعن المشهود عليه وقال للقاضي فلاناً وفلاناً وسمى قوماً يصلحون الخ. قوله : (عند سؤال القاضي عن الشاهد) كان ينبغي يزيد أو عند طعن الخصم وبرهن عليه سراً لأنه تقبل حينئذ لأنهم لم يفسقوا بإظهار الفاحشة بخلاف ما إذا برهن علانية لا يقبل برهانه لفسق شهوده بإظهار الفاحشة كما سيأتي آخر الباب الآتي، وحينئذ يظهر الجواب الآتي عما في الملتقط تأمل.
And there will come in the issues of impugning the witness when explaining bare jarh and other matters, but here we need to explain issues of conflict between jarh and ta'dil. So if the judge asks about the witness and does not get tazkiyah, he seeks another. Then if one accredits him and one impugns him, they conflict. He said in al-Bazzaziyyah: if one of them accredits him and the other impugns him, they conflict, as if he had not asked anyone. And if a third accredits him, then ta'dil is preferable. And if a third impugns him, then jarh is preferable. And al-Sadr mentioned: if one impugns and one accredits, then according to the two Imams, jarh is preferable, as if there were two. And according to Muhammad, as long as it is not completed by one, the testimony is suspended, and he does not permit until he asks the other. If he impugns him, the jarh is complete; if he accredits him, the ta'dil is complete. So if one impugns and two accredit, then ta'dil is preferable according to them. And if two impugn and ten accredit, then jarh is preferable. So if the plaintiff says after the jarh, 'I will bring righteous people who will accredit them,' he said in al-Uyun before that, and in al-Nawadir, that it is not accepted, and this is the choice of Zahir al-Din. And according to the one who accepts, if he brings trustworthy people who accredit them, the judge asks the impugners, perhaps they impugned with something that is not jarh according to the judge, so he does not pay attention to their jarh. This is the finest of opinions. And if the witnesses are accredited secretly, and the opponent says, 'I will bring in public those who will show in them what will reject their testimony,' his statement is not accepted, until he said that jarh is preferable, except if there is partisanship among them, then their jarh is not accepted because the basis of testimony is not accepted when there is partisanship, so jarh is preferable. And it has become clear from the absolute nature of their statements here that jarh is given precedence over ta'dil, whether it is bare or not, when the judge asks about the witness, and the upcoming detail that if it is bare, the evidence is not heard with it, or else it is heard, that is only when the opponent impugns the witness publicly. But in al-Multaqat: if he accredits, and a people say, 'We saw him yesterday drunk, or dealing in riba, or drinking wine,' if it is something for which a right of hadd or property is required to be returned to its owner, his testimony is rejected; otherwise not. This is the case when it is public. As for when they inform him secretly, then no, and its completion will come if Allah wills. And his absolute statement includes when the witness is a stranger, for if he is a stranger and cannot find an accreditor, then he writes to the judge of his town to inform him about his situation, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And in Kashf al-Asrar, the commentary on Usul Fakhr al-Islam, from the discussion of the ambiguous, that the judge hears it. And it should be interpreted that his silence was considered an impugnment of the testimony. His statement: (And according to the one who accepts, etc.) is affirmed in al-Khaniyyah where he said: then that is, and he asks about them, and if they accredit them, the judge asks the impugners what they impugn with, because it is possible that they impugned with something that is not jarh according to the judge. If they show something that is an impugnment, then jarh is preferable; otherwise, the judge does not pay attention to them and judges with the testimony of the plaintiff's witnesses. And likewise if the accreditor accredits the witnesses and the defendant impugns them, and says to the judge, 'So-and-so and so-and-so,' and names people who would be suitable, etc. His statement: (when the judge asks about the witness) it would have been better to add 'or when the opponent impugns and proves it secretly' because then it is accepted, since they have not become sinners by manifesting immorality, unlike if they prove it publicly, his proof is not accepted due to the sinfulness of his witnesses by manifesting immorality, as will come at the end of the next chapter. And then the answer that follows from what is in al-Multaqat becomes apparent. Reflect.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the conflict between jarh (impugning) and ta'dil (accrediting) when evaluating witnesses. The author begins by stating that the judge, after seeking information about a witness, may receive conflicting reports. If one person accredits and another impugns, the matter is considered unresolved—as if no inquiry was made. The Bazzaziyyah is cited: if a third party takes one side, that side prevails. Al-Sadr reports a distinction: according to the two Imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), jarh is preferred even with one accuser and one impugner, treating it as if two impugned. However, Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that until the second person's statement is obtained, the testimony is suspended; once obtained, whichever side is complete prevails. Numerical weight is considered: two accusers outweigh one impugner, but two impugners outweigh ten accusers. If the plaintiff promises to bring accusers after jarh, some authorities reject that, but others allow the judge to investigate the impugners' basis. The judge should ask the impugners to specify their reason; if it is legally insufficient, the jarh is disregarded. The passage then distinguishes between secret and public accreditation: secret accreditation is valid, but public impeachment may be rejected if it involves manifesting sin. The ruling also covers stranger witnesses: the judge may write to the witness's hometown to verify his character. Finally, there is a comment on the matn clarifying that the judge's silence can be construed as impugning the testimony. The overall principle is that bare jarh without specification is not sufficient; the judge must ascertain the substance of the impugnment.

Key Terms
الجرح (al-jarh): Impugning a witness's credibility by alleging a legal defect such as lying, immorality, etc.
التعديل (al-ta'dil): Accrediting or declaring a witness upright and trustworthy.
التعارض (al-ta'arud): Conflict or contradiction between two pieces of evidence, here between jarh and ta'dil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two people impugn a witness and ten people accredit him, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) Ta'dil is preferred because accreditors outnumber impugners.
B) Jarh is preferred because it reveals hidden defects, and numerosity does not overcome its weight.
C) The judge must wait for additional testimonies.
D) The witness is automatically considered reliable.

Key Takeaway
Jarh takes precedence over ta'dil in Hanafi law, but the judge must verify the substance of the impugnment, and numerical weight can tip the scale in rare cases.

Conditions and Method of Tazkiyah (Accreditation) of Witnesses
Conditions and method for accrediting witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions required for tazkiyah (accreditation) of witnesses and apply the Hanafi rules on secret versus public accreditation.

Core Idea
Tazkiyah requires intimate personal knowledge and must be done secretly before publicly.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we examine the detailed conditions for accrediting witnesses. The Hanafi school demands rigorous criteria to ensure the integrity of testimony. This lesson walks through the required qualifications of both the accreditor and the witness, including the procedural order of tazkiyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its purpose
Tazkiyah is the accreditation of a witness's uprightness (adalah). It must be performed by someone who knows the witness intimately, not merely by appearance.
The accreditor must have direct, in-depth knowledge.
2
Determine the method of tazkiyah
The passage emphasizes that secret tazkiyah must precede public tazkiyah. This is based on a statement from Abu Yusuf: 'I do not accept public tazkiyah until he gives secret tazkiyah'.
The author uses 'thumma' (then) to indicate sequence.
3
List the conditions for the accreditor and witness
The accreditor must have tested the witness through partnership, transaction, or travel. The witness must be regular in congregational prayer, honest in financial dealings, trustworthy, truthful, avoid major sins, and avoid persistence in minor sins or unbecoming behavior.
There are eight conditions explicitly listed.
4
Understand the effect of absence and rejection
If a witness disappears for a long period (ghaybah munqati'ah), he cannot be automatically re-accredited; he must be re-evaluated. Also, rejection due to accusation (tuhmah) is permanent, while rejection due to doubt (shubhah) can be removed when the doubt disappears.
This distinction affects future testimony.
5
Apply the ruling to examples
Consider cases of a stranger witness, a witness who testifies after many years, and a repentant witness. Apply the conditions and the rules on secret/public tazkiyah.
Practice using the conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (من) بحث المجمل أنه) أي المجمل. على مثال رجل دخل بلدة لا يعرفه أهلها بالتأمل فيه بل بالرجوع إلى أهل بلدته حتى لو شهد لا يحل للقاضي أن يقضي بشهادته ولا للمزكي أن يعدله إلا بالرجوع إلى أهل بلدته ليعرف وظاهر إطلاقه أيضاً أنه يسأل عنهم في كل حادثة شهدوا فيها لكن قالوا: لو عدل في حادثة وقضى به ثم شهد في أخرى فإن بعدت المدة أعيد وإلا لا، وكذا غريب نزل بين ظهراني قوم لا يعدله قبل مضي ذلك الزمان، وكذا إذا تخللت تلك المدة بين والتعديل هل يؤثر في قبول الشهادة الماضية، وكان الإمام الثاني يقول ذلك الزمان ستة أشهر ثم رجع إلى سنة، ومحمد لم يقدره بل على ما يقع في القلوب الوثوق وعليه الفتوى؛ كذا في البزازية. وفيها أيضاً وفي المنتقى : شهدوا بمال فلم يعدلوا فطلب المدعى عليه من القاضي يكتب وثيقة ويحكم بأنه مردود الشهادة حتى لا يقبله قاض آخر حكم وكتب به، وإذا فعل ذلك لا يقبل القاضي الآخر هذه الشهادة، فإن كان الأول لم يحكم برد شهادتهم للثاني أن يقبل إذا عدلوا ا هـ . وفي الملتقط : وإذا أبطل القاضي شهادته في دار فجاء بعد عشرين سنة فشهد بها أيضاً الآخر فشهادته باطلة ا هـ . وفي الخلاصة : من ردت شهادته في حادثة لعلة ثم زالت تلك العلة فشهد لم تقبل إلا في أربعة : الصبي والعبد والكافر على المسلم والأعمى إذا شهدوا فردت ثم زال المانع فشهدوا تقبل ا هـ . ثم اعلم أنه يفرق بين المردود لتهمة وبين المردود لشبهة فالثاني يقبل عند زوال المانع بخلاف الأول فإنه لا يقبل مطلقاً : أشار إليه في النوازل. ولو قال المؤلف سراً ثم علناً بثم دون الواو المكان أولى وإن أمكن حملها عليها ليفيد أنه لا بد من تقديم تزكية السر على العلانية لما في الملتقط عن أبي يوسف : لا أقبل تزكية العلانية حتى يزكي في السر ا وشمل الشاهد الأصلي والفرعي عن الكل ؛ عن أبي يوسف. وعن محمد يسأل عن الأولين فإن زكيا سأل عن الآخرين ؛ كذا في الملتقط. تنبيه : لا تجوز التزكية إلا أن تعرفه أنت أو وصف لك أو عرفت أن القاضي زكاه أو زكي عنده. وقال محمد : كم من رجل أقبل شهادته ولا أقبل تعديله يعني أن الشهادة على الظواهر ولا كذلك التعديل ؛ كذا في الملتقط فيشترط الجوازها شروط : الأول أن تكون الشهادة عند قاض عدل عالم الثاني أن تعرفه وتختبره بشركة أو معاملة أو سفر. الثالث أن تعرف أنه ملازم للجماعة الرابع أن يكون معروفاً بصحة المعاملة في الدينار والدرهم. الخامس أن يكون مؤدّياً للأمانة السادس أن يكون صدوق اللسان. السابع اجتناب الكبائر . الثامن أن تعلم منه اجتناب الإصرار على الصغائر وما يخل بالمروءة، والكل في شرح أدب القضاء للخصاف وفي النوازل من قال لا أدري أنا مؤمن أم غير مؤمن لا تعدله ولا تصلي خلفه ا هـ. وفي البزازية : عرف فسق الشاهد فغاب غيبة منقطعة ثم قدم ولا يدري منه إلا الصلاح لا يجرحه المعدل ولا يعدله ولو كان معروفاً بالصلاح فغاب غيبة منقطعة ثم حضر فهو على العدالة والشاهدان لو عدلا بعد ما تابا يقضى بشهادتهما، وكذا لو غابا ثم عدلاً.
His statement: (from the discussion of the ambiguous) i.e., the ambiguous. On the example of a man who entered a town whose people do not know him through reflection but through reference to the people of his town, so if he testifies, it is not permissible for the judge to judge by his testimony, nor for the accreditor to accredit him except by reference to the people of his town to know him. And the apparent absolute nature of it also indicates that he asks about them in every incident in which they testify, but they said: if he accredits in an incident and judges by it, then testifies in another, if the period is long, it is renewed; otherwise not. Likewise, a stranger who settles among a people is not accredited before the passage of that time. Likewise, if that period intervened between the accreditation and the acceptance of the past testimony, does it affect? The second Imam used to say that period is six months, then he retracted to a year. Muhammad did not define it but [goes by] what gives confidence to the hearts, and on that is the fatwa. Thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. And in it as well as in al-Muntaqa: they testified regarding property but were not accredited; the defendant asked the judge to write a document and rule that his testimony is rejected so that another judge does not accept it. He ruled and wrote it. If he does that, the other judge does not accept this testimony. If the first did not rule on rejecting their testimony, the second can accept if they are accredited. In al-Multaqat: if the judge invalidates his testimony in a place, then after twenty years he comes and testifies by it as well, his testimony is invalid. In al-Khulasa: whoever's testimony is rejected in an incident due to a cause, then that cause is removed, he testifies [again], it is not accepted except in four: a minor, a slave, a disbeliever against a Muslim, and a blind person—if they testify and are rejected, then the impediment is removed, then they testify, it is accepted. Then know that there is a distinction between one rejected due to accusation and one rejected due to doubt: the second is accepted when the impediment is removed, unlike the first, which is not accepted at all. This is indicated in al-Nawazil. And if the author said 'secretly then publicly' with 'thumma' without 'waw', the place is preferable, even if it can be interpreted with it, to indicate that secret tazkiyah must precede public tazkiyah, because in al-Multaqat from Abu Yusuf: I do not accept public tazkiyah until he gives secret tazkiyah. And it includes the original witness and the sub-witness from all; from Abu Yusuf. And from Muhammad: he asks about the first two; if they are accredited, he asks about the others. Thus in al-Multaqat. Note: tazkiyah is not permissible unless you know him personally, or he is described to you, or you know that the judge accredited him or he was accredited before him. And Muhammad said: How many a man I accept his testimony but do not accept his ta'dil, meaning that testimony is based on outward appearances, but ta'dil is not so. Thus in al-Multaqat. Therefore, for its permissibility, conditions are required: first, that the testimony be before a just, knowledgeable judge; second, that you know him and test him through partnership, transaction, or travel; third, that you know he is regular in attending the congregation; fourth, that he be known for soundness in dealing in dinars and dirhams; fifth, that he be trustworthy; sixth, that he be truthful; seventh, avoidance of major sins; eighth, that you know from him avoidance of persistence in minor sins and matters that detract from manliness. All of this is in Sharh Adab al-Qada' for al-Khassaf. And in al-Nawazil: whoever says 'I do not know whether I am a believer or not', do not accredit him and do not pray behind him. In al-Bazzaziyyah: if the witness's sin is known, then he disappears for a long absence, then returns, and nothing but righteousness is known of him, the accreditor does not impugn him nor accredit him. And if he was known for righteousness, then disappeared for a long absence, then returned, he remains upon the state of integrity. And two witnesses, if they become just after having repented, their testimony is accepted. Likewise, if they disappeared and then became just.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions and procedures for tazkiyah (accreditation) of witnesses. The author begins by explaining the case of a stranger witness: the judge cannot rely on local knowledge alone; he must refer to the witness's hometown. The accreditation is specific to each case; if a witness is accredited in one case but later testifies in another, the old accreditation lapses if sufficient time has passed. There is a difference of opinion on the length of time: the Second Imam (Abu Yusuf) initially said six months, then one year; Muhammad left it to the judge's discretion based on confidence. The passage then discusses the effect of a judge's ruling on rejection: if a judge rules that a witness's testimony is rejected, another judge cannot accept that witness unless the first judge did not rule on rejection. Even if twenty years pass, the rejection stands. However, if the cause of rejection is a removable impediment (like being a minor, slave, etc.), once the impediment is removed, the testimony is accepted. A key distinction is made between rejection due to accusation (like lying) and rejection due to a doubt: the latter can be removed, the former cannot. Secret tazkiyah (done privately) must precede public tazkiyah. The conditions for valid tazkiyah are enumerated: the accreditor must know the witness through personal interaction (partnership, transaction, travel), the witness must be regular in congregational prayer, honest in financial dealings, trustworthy, truthful, avoid major sins, and avoid persistence in minor sins or unbecoming behavior. There is a note that even if a witness appears righteous but had a past of sin, after a long absence he cannot be automatically re-accredited. The passage concludes with a ruling on repentance: if two witnesses repent after sinning, their testimony is accepted, as sin is a removable impediment.

Key Terms
التزكية (al-tazkiyah): The act of accrediting a witness by declaring him upright and trustworthy.
الغيبوبة المنقطعة (al-ghaybah al-munqati'ah): A long absence during which the witness's condition is unknown.
المردود لتهمة (al-mardud li-tuhmah): A witness rejected due to accusation (e.g., proven lying), whose rejection is permanent even after the impediment appears removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what must be the order of tazkiyah (accreditation) for it to be valid?
A) Public tazkiyah before secret tazkiyah.
B) Secret tazkiyah must precede public tazkiyah.
C) Only public tazkiyah is required.
D) Only secret tazkiyah is sufficient.

Key Takeaway
Tazkiyah requires secret accreditation before public, based on personal knowledge and specific conditions.
