Adjusting Stranger Witnesses and the Validity of Tazkiyah Over Time
Ruling on stranger witness verification and the validity period of tazkiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for adjusting a stranger witness, identify the mufta bihi position on the validity period of tazkiyah, and distinguish between rejection for tuhmah and shubhah.

Core Idea
Stranger witness must be verified from hometown; tazkiyah expiry depends on judge's confidence, not a fixed time.

When a stranger from another town comes to testify, the judge cannot rely on local knowledge. He must send inquiries to the witness's hometown to verify his probity (tazkiyah). But once a witness is adjusted, for how long does that adjustment remain valid? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq records a critical intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, with the latter's view becoming the relied-upon position. It also clarifies the crucial distinction between permanent rejection (tuhmah) and curable rejection (shubhah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the judge's acceptance of testimony from a stranger witness. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) for the judge to seek verification from the witness's hometown before accepting his testimony.
The text says: 'لا يحل للقاضي أن يقضي بشهادته ولا للمزكي أن يعدله إلا بالرجوع إلى أهل بلدته' – it is not permissible to rule or modify without reference.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage does not quote a specific Quranic verse or hadith, but the ruling is based on the principle of verifying probity ('adalah) to avoid false testimony. The implicit dalil is the general command to investigate witnesses (cf. Quran 65:2).
The ruling is derived from the need for certainty in judicial decisions.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa initially set the validity period of tazkiyah at six months, then retracted to one year. Imam Muhammad, however, refused to fix a duration, instead relying on the judge's confidence. The mufta bihi (operative position) is Imam Muhammad's view.
The text explicitly states: 'وعليه الفتوى' (upon it is the fatwa).
4
Distinguish between rejection types
The passage later distinguishes between a witness rejected for tuhmah (suspicion) and one rejected for shubhah (doubt). The former is permanent and irreparable; the latter can be cured when the doubt is removed.
This distinction appears in the final part of the passage from al-Nawazil.
5
Apply the exceptions
For four specific categories (minor, slave, disbeliever, blind), if their testimony was rejected due to an impediment and that impediment later ceases, their subsequent testimony is accepted. This is an exception to the general rule.
The text from al-Khulasa lists these exceptions explicitly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات. حالة: الشهادة على مثال رجل دخل بلدة لا يعرفه أهلها بالتأمل فيه بل بالرجوع إلى أهل بلدته حتى لو شهد لا يحل للقاضي أن يقضي بشهادته ولا للمزكي أن يعدله إلا بالرجوع إلى أهل بلدته ليعرف. وظاهر إطلاقه أيضاً أنه يسأل عنهم في كل حادثة شهدوا فيها لكن قالوا: لو عدل في حادثة وقضى به ثم شهد في أخرى فإن بعدت المدة أعيد وإلا لا. وكذا غريب نزل بين ظهراني قوم لا يعدله قبل مضي ذلك الزمان. وكذا إذا تخللت تلك المدة بين والتعديل هل يؤثر في قبول الشهادة الماضية. وكان الإمام الثاني يقول ذلك الزمان ستة أشهر ثم رجع إلى سنة، ومحمد لم يقدره بل على ما يقع في القلوب الوثوق وعليه الفتوى؛ كذا في البزازية. وفيها أيضاً وفي المنتقى: شهدوا بمال فلم يعدلوا فطلب المدعى عليه من القاضي يكتب وثيقة ويحكم بأنه مردود الشهادة حتى لا يقبله قاض آخر حكم وكتب به. وإذا فعل ذلك لا يقبل القاضي الآخر هذه الشهادة. فإن كان الأول لم يحكم برد شهادتهم للثاني أن يقبل إذا عدلوا ا هـ. وفي الملتقط: وإذا أبطل القاضي شهادته في دار فجاء بعد عشرين سنة فشهد بها أيضاً الآخر فشهادته باطلة ا هـ. وفي الخلاصة: من ردت شهادته في حادثة لعلة ثم زالت تلك العلة فشهد لم تقبل إلا في أربعة: الصبي والعبد والكافر على المسلم والأعمى إذا شهدوا فردت ثم زال المانع فشهدوا تقبل ا هـ. ثم اعلم أنه يفرق بين المردود لتهمة وبين المردود لشبهة فالثاني يقبل عند زوال المانع بخلاف الأول فإنه لا يقبل مطلقاً: أشار إليه في النوازل.
Book of Testimonies. Case: Testimony on the example of a man who entered a town whose people do not know him, not by pondering him, but by referring to the people of his hometown. So if he testifies, it is not permissible for the judge to rule by his testimony nor for the modifier to adjust him except by referring to the people of his hometown to know. And the apparent implication of his statement is also that he asks about them in every incident in which they testify. But they said: If he adjusted in an incident and ruled by it, then he testified in another, then if the period is distant, it is repeated, otherwise not. Similarly, a stranger who settled among a people is not adjusted before the passing of that time. Similarly, if that time intervenes between and the adjustment, does it affect the acceptance of the past testimony? Imam the second used to say that time is six months, then he retracted to one year, and Muhammad did not specify it, but rather based on what gives confidence in hearts, and upon that is the fatwa; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. And in it also and in al-Muntaqa: They testified about property and were not adjusted, so the defendant asked the judge to write a document and rule that his testimony is rejected so that no other judge accepts it. He ruled and wrote it. If he does that, the other judge does not accept this testimony. If the first did not rule to reject their testimony, the second may accept if they are adjusted. End quote. In al-Multaqat: If the judge invalidated his testimony in a jurisdiction, then he came after twenty years and testified by it also to another, his testimony is void. End quote. In al-Khulasa: Whoever's testimony is rejected in an incident for a reason, then that reason ceases, and he testified, it is not accepted except in four: the minor, the slave, the disbeliever against a Muslim, and the blind if they testified and were rejected then the impediment ceased and they testify, they are accepted. End quote. Then know that a distinction is made between one rejected for suspicion and one rejected for a doubt; the second is accepted when the impediment ceases, unlike the first, for it is not accepted absolutely: indicated to it in al-Nawazil.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage from the opening of the Book of Testimonies in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes the fundamental rule for verifying witnesses who are not locally known. The ruling is that when a stranger enters a town and presents himself as a witness, the judge cannot rely on local knowledge of his character; instead, he must send inquiries to the witness's hometown to ascertain his probity (tazkiyah). This principle ensures that the adjustment of witnesses is based on concrete information rather than superficial appearance. The text then addresses a procedural question: if a witness has been adjusted and his testimony accepted in one case, must he be re-adjusted when he testifies again? The answer depends on whether a significant period has elapsed. If the time between the two testimonies is long, the adjustment must be renewed; otherwise, it remains valid. The passage records an intra-Hanafi dispute on what constitutes a 'long period': Abu Hanifa is reported to have initially said six months, then retracted to one year. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, refused to fix a specific duration, stating that the standard is whatever inspires confidence in the judge's heart. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Imam Muhammad's view. The text then discusses cases where a witness's testimony was rejected by a previous judge. If the rejection was formalized (the judge wrote and ruled that the witness is rejected), then no subsequent judge may accept that witness's testimony even if he later appears to be upright. But if the first judge simply did not accept the testimony without a formal ruling of rejection, a later judge may accept it after proper adjustment. Another scenario: a witness whose testimony was invalidated in one jurisdiction moves to another jurisdiction and testifies after many years; his testimony remains void. An important exception is drawn from al-Khulasa: for four specific categories—minor, slave, disbeliever against a Muslim, and blind—if their testimony was rejected due to an impediment (like minority, slavery, disbelief, or blindness) and that impediment later ceases (they become adult, freed, convert, or regain sight), their subsequent testimony is accepted. Finally, the passage distinguishes between rejection due to 'tuhmah' (suspicion of wrongdoing) and 'shubhah' (doubt about qualification). The latter is curable by removal of the doubt, while the former is permanently disabling. This distinction is crucial for understanding when a witness can be rehabilitated.

Key Terms
تزكية (tazkiyah): The process of verifying a witness's probity ('adalah) by the judge or a designated modifier.
تعديل (ta'dil): The act of declaring a witness to be 'adl (upright), synonymous with tazkiyah in this context.
المردود لتهمة (al-mardud li tuhmah): A witness rejected due to suspicion of partiality or corruption; such rejection is permanent and not curable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a witness's testimony was rejected because he was a minor, and later he becomes an adult, can his testimony be accepted?
A) No, rejection is permanent.
B) Yes, because the impediment of minority has ceased.
C) Only if the judge re-adjusts him.
D) No, because he was already rejected.

Key Takeaway
A stranger witness must be verified from his hometown; tazkiyah validity depends on the judge's confidence (mufta bihi), and rejection due to suspicion (tuhmah) is permanent while rejection due to doubt (shubhah) is curable.

Conditions for Valid Tazkiyah and the Priority of Secret Adjustment
Listing eight conditions and procedural order for witness adjustment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight conditions for valid tazkiyah and explain the Hanafi rule that secret tazkiyah must precede public adjustment.

Core Idea
Tazkiyah requires personal knowledge; secret inquiry must precede public declaration.

In the Hanafi school, the integrity of witnesses is paramount. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lays out the precise conditions for a valid tazkiyah (adjustment of witnesses) and establishes a crucial procedural order: secret inquiry before public testimony. You will learn the eight conditions derived from al-Khassaf, understand the difference between secret and public tazkiyah, and see how the school handles witnesses who disappear or repent. This is essential for anyone studying Islamic judicial procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall procedure of tazkiyah
Recognize that tazkiyah is the process of verifying a witness's uprightness. The passage insists that secret tazkiyah must precede public tazkiyah, based on Abu Yusuf's ruling.
The order is procedural, not a pillar of validity according to all Hanafis.
2
List the eight conditions from al-Khassaf
Memorize the eight conditions: judge must be just and knowledgeable; modifier must have direct knowledge via partnership, transaction, or travel; witness must attend congregation, deal soundly in money, be trustworthy, truthful, avoid major sins, and avoid persistence in minor sins and acts compromising muru'ah.
These are found in Sharh Adab al-Qada' al-Khassaf.
3
Understand the order requirement from Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf states he does not accept public tazkiyah until secret tazkiyah is done. Imam Muhammad adds a layered inquiry: first investigate primary witnesses, then secondary ones.
Al-Khassaf went further by requiring that secret and public be done by different modifiers.
4
Note the effects of witness absence and repentance
If a sinful witness disappears and returns appearing righteous, he is not automatically adjusted. If a righteous witness disappears, he retains his status. A repentant sinner is not immediately adjusted; a period must confirm sincerity.
These rulings safeguard the integrity of testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال المؤلف سراً ثم علناً بثم دون الواو المكان أولى وإن أمكن حملها عليها ليفيد أنه لا بد من تقديم تزكية السر على العلانية لما في الملتقط عن أبي يوسف: لا أقبل تزكية العلانية حتى يزكي في السر ا وشمل الشاهد الأصلي والفرعي عن الكل؛ عن أبي يوسف. وعن محمد يسأل عن الأولين فإن زكيا سأل عن الآخرين؛ كذا في الملتقط. تنبيه: لا تجوز التزكية إلا أن تعرفه أنت أو وصف لك أو عرفت أن القاضي زكاه أو زكي عنده. وقال محمد: كم من رجل أقبل شهادته ولا أقبل تعديله يعني أن الشهادة على الظواهر ولا كذلك التعديل؛ كذا في الملتقط. فيشترط لجوازها شروط: الأول أن تكون الشهادة عند قاض عدل عالم. الثاني أن تعرفه وتختبره بشركة أو معاملة أو سفر. الثالث أن تعرف أنه ملازم للجماعة. الرابع أن يكون معروفاً بصحة المعاملة في الدينار والدرهم. الخامس أن يكون مؤدياً للأمانة. السادس أن يكون صدوق اللسان. السابع اجتناب الكبائر. الثامن أن تعلم منه اجتناب الإصرار على الصغائر وما يخل بالمروءة. والكل في شرح أدب القضاء للخصاف. وفي النوازل: من قال لا أدري أنا مؤمن أم غير مؤمن لا تعدله ولا تصلي خلفه ا هـ. وفي البزازية: عرف فسق الشاهد فغاب غيبة منقطعة ثم قدم ولا يدري منه إلا الصلاح لا يجرحه المعدل ولا يعدله. ولو كان معروفاً بالصلاح فغاب غيبة منقطعة ثم حضر فهو على العدالة. والشاهدان لو عدلا بعد ما تابا يقضى بشهادتهما. وكذا لو غابا ثم عدلاً، ولو خرسا أو عميا لا يقضى. تاب الفاسق لا يعدل كما تاب بل لا بد من مضي زمان يقع في القلب صدقه في التوبة ا هـ. تنبیه آخر: ولو زكى من في السر علناً يجوز عندنا، والخصاف شرط تغايرهما؛ كذا في البزازية. وفي المصباح: علن الأمر علونا من باب قعد ظهر وانتشر فهو عالن وعلن علناً من باب تعب لغة فهو علن وعلين والاسم العلانية مخففاً ا هـ.
And if the author said 'secretly then publicly' with 'then' without 'and', the position is better, even if it is possible to carry it upon it to indicate that secret tazkiyah must precede public tazkiyah, because in al-Multaqat from Abu Yusuf: I do not accept public tazkiyah until he adjusts in secret. And it includes the original witness and the secondary witness from all; from Abu Yusuf. And from Muhammad: he asks about the first two, if they are adjusted he asks about the others; thus in al-Multaqat. Note: Tazkiyah is not permissible unless you know him yourself, or someone described him to you, or you know that the judge adjusted him or he was adjusted in his presence. And Muhammad said: How many a man I accept his testimony but I do not accept his adjustment, meaning testimony is based on appearances, but adjustment is not so; thus in al-Multaqat. So conditions are required for its permissibility: first, that the testimony be before a just, knowledgeable judge. Second, that you know him and test him through partnership, transaction, or travel. Third, that you know he is regular in attending the congregation. Fourth, that he be known for sound dealing in dinar and dirham. Fifth, that he be trustworthy. Sixth, that he be truthful of speech. Seventh, avoidance of major sins. Eighth, that you know from him avoidance of persistence in minor sins and things that detract from manliness. All in Sharh Adab al-Qada' al-Khassaf. And in al-Nawazil: Whoever says 'I do not know whether I am a believer or not', do not adjust him and do not pray behind him. End quote. In al-Bazzaziyya: If the witness is known to be sinful and then disappears completely, then returns and nothing is known from him but righteousness, the modifier neither impugns him nor adjusts him. And if he was known for righteousness and then disappears completely, then returns, he remains upon righteousness. And two witnesses, if they adjust after repenting, their testimony is accepted. So too if they disappear then are adjusted. And if they become mute or blind, their testimony is not accepted. The sinful person who repents is not adjusted as soon as he repents; rather, a period must pass that gives confidence in his truthfulness in repentance. End quote. Another note: If one adjusts those in secret publicly, it is permissible according to us, but al-Khassaf stipulates that they be distinct; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. And in al-Misbah: 'Alana' the matter 'aluna' from the paradigm of qa'ada, meaning to appear and spread, so it is 'aalin', and 'alina' as a noun from the paradigm of ta'iba, so it is 'alin' and 'aliyyan', and the noun is 'alaniyyah' with tashdid, lightly. End quote.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a definitional ruling that establishes the procedural and substantive conditions for valid tazkiyah (witness adjustment). The text begins by insisting on the order: secret tazkiyah must precede public tazkiyah. This is based on a narration from Abu Yusuf in al-Multaqat, who states he does not accept public tazkiyah until the witness has been adjusted in secret. The same source adds that according to Imam Muhammad, the modifier first investigates the original witnesses (likely the primary witnesses), and if they are found upright, he then investigates the secondary witnesses. The passage then lists eight detailed conditions for a valid tazkiyah, drawn from Sharh Adab al-Qada' by al-Khassaf. These conditions are memorization-worthy and cover both the qualifications of the judge (must be just and knowledgeable) and the depth of personal knowledge required of the modifier (shared business, travel, etc.). The text also includes a peculiar condition: that the witness be regular in attending congregational prayer (a sign of public piety). Further, the passage addresses the effect of a witness's disappearance and return. If a witness known for sin disappears and returns appearing righteous, he is neither automatically impugned nor adjusted; a new investigation is needed. But if he was known for righteousness and disappears, he retains his status unless proven otherwise. Regarding repentance: a sinful witness who repents is not accepted immediately; a period must pass that convinces the modifier of the sincerity of his repentance. The text also touches on a linguistic point from al-Misbah about the word 'علانية' (public), distinguishing it from 'سر' (secret). Importantly, the text notes that according to the Hanafi school, it is permissible to publicly testify to the adjustment of someone already adjusted in secret, though al-Khassaf required that the two acts be distinct (different modifiers). This shows the flexibility within the school on procedural matters.

Key Terms
تزكية السر (tazkiyat al-sirr): Confidential inquiry into the witness's character, conducted privately before any public declaration.
تزكية العلانية (tazkiyat al-'alaniyyah): Public declaration of a witness's uprightness, usually in court.
مروءة (muru'ah): Social decency and propriety; behavior that is becoming of a person of integrity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the eight conditions for tazkiyah listed in the passage?
A) The witness must be known for sound financial dealings.
B) The witness must be free of major sins.
C) The witness must have memorized the Quran.
D) The witness must be truthful of speech.

Key Takeaway
Valid tazkiyah requires personal knowledge and, in the Hanafi school, secret inquiry must precede public declaration.

Tazkiyah by the Opponent: Invalidity and Exceptions
Ruling on opponent's tazkiyah with ta'lil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tazkiyah by the opposing party and identify the exception when it constitutes an admission.

Core Idea
The opponent's tazkiyah is invalid because his denial contradicts the witness's credibility.

In Hanafi court procedure, the credibility of witnesses is established through tazkiyah. This lesson examines why the opposing party's endorsement of a witness is not accepted and when such a statement transforms into an admission of liability. We follow the reasoning in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and its sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the defendant or plaintiff stating that the witness is just (adl). The ruling: not valid as tazkiyah.
The opponent is considered biased against the claim.
2
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The opponent denies the claim, thereby implicitly accusing the witness of lying. Therefore, he is not a credible source for tazkiyah.
The text says: 'because in the claim of the plaintiff… the opponent is a liar in his denial.'
3
Distinguish the exception
If the opponent says 'they spoke truth' or 'they are just, believe them', it is an admission, not tazkiyah.
In Hidayah, this is considered a confession of the right.
4
Apply the ruling to the plaintiff a fortiori
The ruling applies even more strongly to the plaintiff, as his own interest is even clearer.
Al-Bazzaziyya adds restriction based on whether the opponent is relied upon for tazkiyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه آخر: يسأل القاضي عن الشهود الذمة عدول المسلمين وإلا فيسأل عنهم عدول الكفار؛ كذا في المحيط والاختيار. قوله: ( وتعديل الخصم لا يصح) أي تزكية المدعى عليه الشاهد بقوله هو عدل غير مقبولة لأن في زعم المدعي وشهوده أن الخصم كاذب في إنكاره مبطل في إصراره فلا يصلح معدلاً. وموضوع المسألة إذا قال عدول إلا أنهم أخطؤوا أو نسوا، أما إذا قال صدقوا أو هم عدول صدقة فقد اعترف بالحق؛ كذا في الهداية. وفي شرح أدب القضاء للصدر الشهيد أن يكون مقراً بقوله صدقوا فيما شهدوا به علي وبقوله هم عدول فيما شهدوا به علي. أطلقه وقيده في البزازية بما إذا كان المدعى عليه لا يرجع إليه في التعديل فإن كان صح قوله. وشمل الخصم المدعي والمدعى عليه وإن أراد به المدعى عليه وهو الظاهر فعدم صحته من المدعي بأولى كتعديل الشاهد نفسه. وأما فمقبول لما في البزازية: وقول الشاهد إنه ليس بعدل إقراره على نفسه جائز عليه وكان ينبغي له أن لا يفعل ا هـ. وظاهر ما في الظهيرية أنه يأثم بذلك حيث كان صادقاً في شهادته لما فيه من إبطال حق المدعي. ولم يذكر المؤلف رحمه الله تعديل أحد الشاهدين صاحبه وفيه اختلاف؛ قال في الظهيرية: شاهدان شهدا لرجل والقاضي يعرف أحدهما بالعدالة ولا يعرف الآخر فعدله الذي عرفه القاضي بالعدالة. قال نصير رحمه الله: لا يقبل القاضي تعديله ولابن سلمة فيه قولان، وعن أبي بكر البلخي في ثلاثة شهدوا والقاضي يعرف اثنين منهم بالعدالة ولا يعرف الثالث فإن القاضي يقبل تعديلهما لو شهد هذا الثالث شهادة أخرى ولا يقبل تعديلهما في الشهادة الأولى وهو كما قال نصير رحمه الله تعالى ا هـ. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا عدله المدعى عليه قبل الشهادة أو بعدها كما في البزازية ويحتاج إلى تأمل فإنه قبل الدعوى لم يوجد منه كذب في إنكاره وقت التعديل وكان الفسق الطارئ على المعدل قبل القضاء كالمقارن. وفي البزازية: ولا يسأل رجلاً له على المشهود عليه دين فلسه الحاكم. وهذا دليل على أن الشاهد إذا كان له دين على المشهود عليه وهو مفلس لا تقبل اهـ. وفي المحيط البرهاني من دفع الدعاوى معزياً إلى الأوزجندي: إذا قال المدعى عليه بعد الشهادة لي دفع لا يكون تعديلاً للشهود الجواز أن يكون بالطعن في الشاهد اهـ. قلت: بخلاف قول المدعي عليه في جواب دعوى الوكيل بالدين دفعته إلى الموكل أو أبرأني فإنه يكون إقراراً بالوكالة فإنه يؤمر بالدفع إلى الوكيل كما سيأتي فيها. قوله: (والواحد يكفي للتزكية والرسالة والترجمة وهذا عندهما. وقال محمد: لا يجوز
Another note: The judge asks about the witnesses of the dhimma (non-Muslim subjects) from just Muslims, otherwise he asks about them from just disbelievers; thus in al-Muhit and al-Ikhtiyar. His statement: (And the adjustment of the opponent is not valid) meaning the defendant's tazkiyah of the witness by saying 'he is just' is not acceptable, because in the claim of the plaintiff and his witnesses, the opponent is a liar in his denial and wrong in his persistence, so he is not suitable as a modifier. The subject of the issue is when he says 'they are just except that they erred or forgot', but if he says 'they spoke truth' or 'they are just, believe them', then he has confessed the right; thus in al-Hidaya. In Sharh Adab al-Qada' by al-Sadr al-Shahid, he must be confessing by his statement 'they spoke truth in what they testified against me' and by his statement 'they are just in what they testified against me'. It was left unrestricted and restricted in al-Bazzaziyya to when the defendant is not relied upon for tazkiyah; if he is, his statement is accepted. And it includes the opponent whether plaintiff or defendant, though he meant the defendant, which is apparent, so its lack of validity from the plaintiff is even more so, like tazkiyah of the witness by himself. And as for [self-tazkiyah], it is accepted because of what is in al-Bazzaziyya: The witness's statement that he is not just is an admission against himself, binding upon him, and he should not do it. End quote. And the apparent from al-Zahiriyya is that he sins by that if he is truthful in his testimony because it involves invalidating the plaintiff's right. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention the adjustment of one of the two witnesses by his companion, and there is disagreement about it. He said in al-Zahiriyya: Two witnesses testified for a man, and the judge knows one of them to be just, but does not know the other, so the one he knows to be just adjusts him. Nasir (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The judge does not accept his adjustment. And Ibn Salama has two opinions. And from Abu Bakr al-Balkhi regarding three who testified, and the judge knows two of them to be just and does not know the third: the judge accepts the adjustment of the two if this third testifies in another case, but does not accept their adjustment in the first testimony. And it is as Nasir (may Allah have mercy on him) said. End quote. And he left it unrestricted, so it includes whether the defendant adjusted him before or after the testimony, as in al-Bazzaziyya. And it needs reflection, for before the lawsuit, there was no lie from him in his denial at the time of adjustment, and the sin that occurs on the part of the modifier before the judgment is like that which coexists. In al-Bazzaziyya: And the judge does not ask a man who has a debt on the one against whom testimony is given if he is insolvent. This is evidence that if a witness has a debt on the one against whom he testifies and he is insolvent, his testimony is not accepted. End quote. In al-Muhit al-Burhani from Daf' al-Da'awa quoting al-Awzjandi: If the defendant after testimony says 'I have a defense', it is not an adjustment of the witnesses because it could be impugning the witness. End quote. I say: Unlike the defendant's statement in answer to the agent's claim of debt, 'I paid it to the principal' or 'he discharged me', for that is an acknowledgment of the agency, so he is ordered to pay the agent as will come later. His statement: (And one suffices for tazkiyah, message, and translation, and this is according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: It is not permissible...
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This final passage of the window delves into several specific issues within the law of testimony, each with its own legal reasoning (ta'lil). First, regarding tazkiyah by the opponent (al-khasm): The text rules that a defendant's statement that a witness is just is not acceptable as tazkiyah. The reason given is that the defendant's position inherently contradicts the plaintiff's claim; by denying the claim, the defendant implicitly accuses the witnesses of lying, so his word cannot be trusted to exalt their credibility. However, if the defendant explicitly says 'they spoke the truth' or 'they are just, believe them', that is considered an admission of liability, not a tazkiyah. The Hidayah is cited for this distinction. Al-Sadr al-Shahid's commentary adds that the defendant must be effectively confessing to the claim when he endorses the witnesses. Al-Bazzaziyya qualifies that if the defendant is not the one relied upon for tazkiyah (i.e., he is not a credible source even when not a party), then his adjustment of the witness is invalid anyway. The same reasoning applies a fortiori to the plaintiff (who is also a party) and to self-tazkiyah (a witness declaring himself just). On self-tazkiyah, the text cites al-Bazzaziyya that if a witness declares himself unjust, that is a valid admission against himself, and he should not do so. Al-Zahiriyya adds that he sins by such self-impugnment if he is truthful, because it invalidates the plaintiff's right. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq then notes that the matn author (al-Kanz) did not mention the issue of one witness adjusting his fellow witness. The text records a dispute: In al-Zahiriyya, Nasir says the judge does not accept such adjustment, while Ibn Salama has two opinions. Abu Bakr al-Balkhi makes a distinction: if the known just witnesses vouch for the third in a separate case, it is accepted; but in the same case, it is not. The text also addresses the situation where a witness has a debt on the opposing party and that party is insolvent—such testimony is not accepted because of perceived bias. Finally, the text touches on the rule that one single person suffices for tazkiyah, for delivering a message (risala), and for translation (tarjama). This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions), while Imam Muhammad is reported to have said it is not permissible (probably referring to tazkiyah by one; the text cuts off). This intra-Hanafi dispute is left partially unresolved, but the relied-upon position is that one person is sufficient for tazkiyah, as is well known in the school.

Key Terms
تعديل الخصم (ta'dil al-khasm): The adjustment of a witness by the opposing party, which is invalid in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject tazkiyah by the opponent?
A) Because the opponent is not a Muslim.
B) Because the opponent's denial of the claim implies he considers the witness a liar.
C) Because the opponent is not a judge.
D) Because the opponent has no personal knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The opponent's tazkiyah is invalid because his adversarial position makes him an unreliable source for witness credibility.
